Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Proportional Division of Payment in Khul' with Multiple Divorces
Sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on khul' payment division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how payment is divided when a wife requests multiple divorces for a sum and the husband gives fewer, and apply the condition of sitting.

Core Idea
The payment in khul' is apportioned proportionally to the number of divorces given, subject to conditions of sitting and prior divorces.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a key ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when a wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband divorces her only once, she owes only one-third of the thousand. Underlying this is the understanding that the particle 'ب' (ba) denotes exchange, and the payment is divided according to the number of divorces actually effected. However, several conditions and nuances arise, including the requirement that the divorce be pronounced in the same sitting, the effect of prior divorces, and an intra-Hanafi dispute when the husband gives more divorces than requested. We will disentangle these layers step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening sentence: 'She said: Divorce me three times for a thousand, so he divorced her once: she owes one-third of the thousand and she is irredeemably divorced.' This is the basic rule; the payment is divided proportionally.
The particle 'ب' is key – it signifies exchange ('iwaḍ) and is divisible.
2
Understand the condition of sitting
The text stipulates that the divorce must occur in the same sitting as the offer. If the husband leaves and then divorces, no money is due. This shows that the offer is tied to the immediate session.
Contrast with when the husband initiates: then the wife's acceptance can be in her own sitting even if he leaves.
3
Analyze the effect of prior divorces
If the wife had already received two divorces (so one remains) and then asks for three more for a sum, giving one divorce triggers the whole sum because she committed to money for complete severance (three divorces). The request for three shows she had not been divorced before.
This is based on the principle of 'baynunah ghalizah' (severe separation) requiring three divorces.
4
Examine the istihsan vs. qiyas dispute
When the husband gives three separate divorces in one sitting: by qiyas (analogy) only one divorce is paid for, but by istihsan (juristic preference) all three are paid for if connected. Some scholars require connection; the preferred view is that connection is not needed if the sitting is the same.
Istihsan overrides qiyas here to honor the wife's intent.
5
Compare Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on exceeding request
If the wife asks for one divorce for a thousand and the husband gives three: Abu Hanifa says three occur for nothing; the Sahibayn say one occurs for a thousand and two for nothing. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute based on whether the husband's action is interpreted as acceptance with excess or a new offer.
The passage also mentions that if the husband says 'You are divorced three times for a thousand', it depends on the wife's acceptance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (قالت طلقني ثلاثاً بالف فطلق واحدة له ثلث الألف وبانت) لأن الباء تصحب الأعواض وهو ينقسم على المعوض ويشترط أن يطلقها في المجلس حتى لو قام فطلقها لا يجب شيء، - كذا في فتح القدير ـ بخلاف ما إذا بدأ هو فقال خالعتك على ألف فإنه يعتبر في القبول مجلسها لا مجلسه حتى لو ذهب من المجلس ثم قبلت في مجلسها ذلك صح قبولها؛ كذا في الجوهرة أشار بطلبها الثلاث الى أنه لم يطلقها قبله إذ لو كان طلقها ثنتين ثم قالت طلقني ثلاثاً على أن لك ألف درهم فطلقها واحدة كان عليها كل الألف لأنها التزمت المال بإيقاع البينونة الغليظة وقد تم ذلك بإيقاع الثلاث؛ كذا في المبسوط والخانية. وينبغي أن لا فرق فيها بين الباء وعلى» لأن المنظور إليه حصول المقصود لا اللفظ ولذا قال في الخلاصة : لو قالت طلقني أربعاً بألف فطلقها ثلاثاً فهي بالألف، ولو طلقها واحدة فبثلث الألف اهـ. وقيد بكونه طلق واحدة إذ لو طلق الثلاث كان له الألف، جميع ،، سواء كان بلفظ واحد أو متفرقة بعد أن تكون في مجلس واحد ؛ كذا في فتح القدير لا يقال كيف وقع الثاني أن البائن لا يلحق البائن إلا إذا كان معلقاً لأنا نقول : قد أسلفنا أن مرادهم من البائن ما مع كان بلفظ الكناية لا مطلق البائن حتى صرحوا بوقوع أنت طالق ثلاثاً بعد البينونة . وفي التتارخانية : ثم في قولها طلقني ثلاثاً بألف إذا طلقها ثلاثاً متفرقة في مجلس واحد القياس أن تقع تطليقة واحدة بثلث الألف وتقع الأخريان بغير شيء، وفي الاستحسان تقع الثلاث بالألف، من قال : ما ذكر من جواب الاستحسان محمول على ما إذا وصل التطليقات بعضها ببعض، أما إذا فصل بين كل تطليقة بسكوت لا يجب جميع الألف وإن حصل الإيقاع في مجلس واحد ومنهم من يقول : إذا كان المجلس واحداً لا يشترط الوصل وهو الصحيح .اهـ. قيد بقوله ثلاثاً لأنها لو قالت طلقني واحدة بألف فقال أنت طالق ثلاثاً فإن اقتصر ولم يذكر المال طلقت ثلاثاً بغير شيء في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال صاحباه : تقع واحدة بألف وثنتان بغير شيء ولو قال أنت طالق ثلاثاً بألف يتوقف ذلك على قبول المرأة إن قبلت تقع الثلاث بالألف، وإن لم تقبل لا يقع شيء. ولو قالت طلقني واحدة بألف فقال لها الزوج أنت طالق واحدة وواحدة وواحدة تقع الثلاث واحدة بألف وثنتان بغير شيء عند الكل؛ كذا في الخانية .
His statement: (She said: Divorce me three times for a thousand, so he divorced her once: she owes one-third of the thousand and she is irredeemably divorced) because the letter ba is for considerations, and it is divided according to the compensation, and it is required that he divorce her in the sitting; if he stood and divorced her, nothing is due — as in Fath al-Qadir. Contrary to if he initiated by saying: I divorce you for a thousand; then her sitting is considered for acceptance, not his sitting, so if he left the sitting and she accepted in her sitting, her acceptance is valid — as in al-Jawhara. Her request for three indicates that he had not divorced her before; because if he had divorced her twice, then she said: Divorce me three times on condition that you get a thousand dirhams, and he divorced her once, she owes the entire thousand because she committed to the money for achieving severe separation, and that is completed by effecting three divorces — as in al-Mabsut and al-Khaniyya. And it should be that there is no difference between 'with' and 'on condition' in this because the consideration is the achievement of the purpose, not the wording. Hence al-Khulasah said: If she said: Divorce me four times for a thousand, and he divorced her three times, she owes a thousand; if he divorced her once, she owes one-third of a thousand. End quote. And the condition that he divorced her once; because if he divorced three times, he gets the whole thousand, whether with one word or separately after they are in one sitting — as in Fath al-Qadir. It should not be said: How did the second divorce occur, since a ba'in divorce cannot be followed by another ba'in unless it is suspended? For we say: We have already mentioned that their intent by 'ba'in' is what is with a kinaya wording, not absolute ba'in, such that they explicitly state that 'You are divorced three times' occurs after ba'in. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: Then regarding her saying: Divorce me three times for a thousand, if he divorces her three times separately in one sitting, by qiyas one divorce occurs for one-third of the thousand, and the other two occur for nothing; by istihsan, the three occur for the thousand. Some said: The mentioned answer of istihsan is carried on when the divorces are connected to each other. As for when he pauses between each divorce, the whole thousand is not due, even if the pronouncement is in one sitting. And some say: If the sitting is one, connection is not required, and that is correct. End quote. He restricted it by her saying 'three times' because if she said: Divorce me once for a thousand, and he said: You are divorced three times, then if he did not mention money, she is divorced three times for nothing according to Abu Hanifa. His two companions said: One divorce occurs for a thousand, and two for nothing. And if he said: You are divorced three times for a thousand, it is suspended on the woman's acceptance; if she accepts, three occur for a thousand; if she does not accept, nothing occurs. And if she said: Divorce me once for a thousand, and the husband said: You are divorced once and once and once, then three divorces occur: one for a thousand and two for nothing, according to all — as in al-Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (expansion) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The commentator explains the ruling when a wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband gives only one divorce. The key principle: the letter 'ب' (ba) is used for exchange ('iwaḍ), and it is apportioned according to the number of divorces given. So one divorce entitles the husband to one-third of the thousand. However, several conditions are discussed: the divorce must be pronounced in the same sitting; if the husband leaves and then divorces, no money is owed. Conversely, if the husband initiates the khul' offer, the wife's acceptance can be in her own sitting even if he left. The passage then clarifies that if the wife had already been divorced twice and then asks for three more divorces for money, giving one divorce obligates the full amount because she committed to money for the complete severance (baynūnah ghalīzah), which requires three divorces. Interestingly, some scholars see no difference between using 'ب' and 'على' in this context, as the intent is the outcome, not the word. The passage also addresses an objection: how can a second ba'in divorce follow a first? The answer is that 'ba'in' here refers to divorces given by kināyah (allusion), not to irrevocable divorces generally. Then an istihsan ruling from al-Tatarkhaniyya is cited: if he gives three divorces separately in one sitting, by qiyas only one occurs with payment, but by istihsan all three occur for the full amount, especially if pronounced consecutively without pause. The preferred view is that connection is not required if the sitting is the same. Finally, the passage discusses variations: if she asks for one divorce for a thousand and he gives three, the rulings differ between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa says she is divorced three times for nothing (since he exceeded her request); the Sahibayn say one divorce is for the thousand and two for nothing. If he says 'You are divorced three times for a thousand', it depends on her acceptance. If he enumerates 'one, and one, and one', then according to all, only the first is paid, the rest are free. The commentary uses numerous citations from the Hanafi tradition (Fath al-Qadir, al-Jawhara, al-Mabsut, al-Khaniyya, al-Khulasah, al-Tatarkhaniyya) to elaborate on the matn.

Key Terms
الباء (al-bā'): The letter 'ب' used to denote the consideration ('iwaḍ) in khul', meaning the payment is directly for the divorces.
بائن (bā'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; in this passage, it refers to divorces given by kinaya wording.
استحسان (istihsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in certain cases for a more equitable outcome.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning from an established case to a new case based on a shared effective cause (ʿilla).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband divorces her once, how much does she owe?
A) The full thousand
B) One-third of a thousand
C) Nothing
D) Half a thousand

Key Takeaway
Payment in khul' is divided proportionally to the number of divorces actually given, with conditions on sitting and prior divorces.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Using 'على' in Khul'
Critical refinement of a ruling on the word 'على' in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on khul' using 'على', explain the dispute with the Sahibayn, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to a given scenario.

Core Idea
In khul', the word 'على' can be a pure condition, so if only one divorce is given, she owes nothing.

This lesson delves into a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the use of the word 'على' in khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states a ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to parse linguistic ambiguities in legal texts and appreciate how conditions and considerations interact in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Read the passage carefully. The wife says 'طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف' and the husband gives one divorce. What are the possible legal interpretations?
Focus on the word 'على' as the pivot of the dispute.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa treats 'على' as a pure condition (shart mahd), so the money is not apportioned. The divorce is revocable and she owes nothing. Note the analogy from al-Siyar al-Kabir regarding the imam's aman.
The condition is indivisible; thus partial performance does not obligate payment.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn treat 'على' like 'ب' (consideration), so they see the money as a price that must be divided. Thus she owes one-third and the divorce is ba'in.
Their reasoning relies on the default assumption that money mentioned in an exchange context indicates consideration.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: if only one divorce is given, Abu Hanifa says no payment and revocable; Sahibayn say one-third payment and ba'in. The passage supports Abu Hanifa's view, citing Fath al-Qadir and Ibn Amir Haj, who argue that money can be a pure condition.
The key principle: 'What is known to be in exchange is consideration' does not apply to divorce because it is not a pure exchange contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي على وقع رجعي مجاناً) أي في قولها طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف أو على أن لك علي ألفاً فطلقها واحدة وقع رجعياً بغير شيء عليها عند الإمام خلافاً لهما، فهما جعلاها كالباء وهو جعلها للشرط والمشروط لا يتوزع على أجزاء الشرط ألا ترى أنه ذكر في السير الكبير لو أمن الإمام ثلاث سنين بألف دينار فبدا للإمام أن ينبذ إليهم بعد سنة رد عليهم ثلثا الألف، ولو أمن على ألف دينار رد الكل؛ كذا في المحيط. قيد بكونه طلقها واحدة لأنه لو ثلاثاً استحق الألف وإن طلقها ثلاثاً متفرقات في مجلس واحد لزمها الألف لأن الأولى والثانية تقع عنده رجعية فإيقاع الثالثة وجد وهي منكوحته فيستوجب عليها الألف درهم، وإن طلقها ثلاثاً في ثلاث مجالس عندهما ثلث الألف، يستوجب لا وعنده يستوجب شيئاً ؛ في المحيط. وحاصل ما حققه في فتح القدير أن كلمة «على» مشتركة بين الاستعلاء واللزوم فإذا اتصلت بالأجسام المحسوسة كانت للاستعلاء وفي غيره للزوم وهو صادق على الشرط المحض نحو أنت طالق على أن تدخلي الدار، وعلى المعاوضة كبعني هذا على ألف واحمله على درهم سواء كانت شرطاً محضاً كما مثلنا، أو عرفاً نحو افعل كذا على أن أنصرك، والمحل المتنازع فيه يصح فيه كل من الشرط والمعاوضة ولا مرجح، وكون مدخولها مالاً لا يرجح معنى الاعتياض فإن المال يصح جعله شرطاً محضاً كإن طلقتني ثلاثاً فلك ألف فلا

قوله : (رد عليهم ثلثا الألف كذا في هذه النسخة «ثلثا» بالألف نائب فاعل «رد» والذي في غيرها من النسخ «ثلث» بدون ألف وهو غير ظاهر قوله : (وذكر في التحرير ما يرجح قولهما الخ) نازعه فيه شارحه المحقق ابن أمير حاج بأن كون الأصل فيما علمت مقابلته العوضية إنما هو فيما وجبت فيه المعاوضة الشرعية المحضة، أما ما تصح أو الشرط المحض فيه والطلاق من هذا فليس كون مدخولها مالاً مرجحاً لمعنى الاعتياض فإن المال يصح جعله شرطاً محضاً قوله : (فإن لها غرضاً في أنه إن طلقها الخ) قال المقدسي في شرحه : كونها لها غرضاً في طلاق ضرتها بعيد وإنما يقرب لو هي
His statement: (And with 'ala it occurs as revocable for free) i.e., in her saying: Divorce me three times on condition of a thousand or on condition that you have a thousand owed by me, and he divorced her once, it occurs revocably with nothing against her according to the Imam, contrary to the two. They treated it like the ba, and he treated it as a condition. The conditional does not divide among the parts of the condition. Do you not see that it is mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: If the Imam grants security for three years for a thousand dinars, and then the Imam decides to revoke it after one year, he returns two-thirds of the thousand to them; but if he granted security on condition of a thousand dinars, he returns all. As in al-Muhit. He restricted it to his divorcing her once, because if three, he is entitled to the thousand. And if he divorces her three times separately in one sitting, she owes the thousand because the first and second occur as revocable according to him, so the third finds her still married, so she owes the thousand dirhams. If he divorces her three times in three sittings, according to the two she owes nothing? Actually it says 'at their two views, one-third of the thousand..., and according to him he is entitled to something' — in al-Muhit. The bottom line of what is verified in Fath al-Qadir is that the word 'ala is shared between isti'la (superiority) and luzum (bindingness). When connected to physical objects, it indicates isti'la; otherwise, it indicates luzum. It applies to pure condition, e.g., 'You are divorced on condition that you enter the house', and to exchange, e.g., 'Sell me this for a thousand' and 'carry it for a dirham', whether the condition is pure as we gave as example, or customary like 'Do this on condition that I help you'. The contested instance can accommodate both condition and exchange, and there is no preponderance. The fact that its object is money does not give preponderance to the meaning of exchange, because money can be made a pure condition, like 'If you divorce me three times, you get a thousand' — thus no preponderance.

His statement: (He returned two-thirds of the thousand — in this copy 'thuluthā' with alif as the subject of 'returned', but in other copies 'thuluth' without alif, which is not apparent). His statement: (And it is mentioned in al-Tahrir that which gives preponderance to the view of the two, etc.) — the commentator Ibn Amir Haj contested this, saying that the principle that 'what is known to be in exchange is for consideration' only applies where pure legal exchange is established; but as for where pure condition is possible, and divorce is of this type, then the fact that its object is money does not give preponderance to the meaning of exchange, because money can be validly made a pure condition, as in 'If you divorce me three times, you get a thousand'. His statement: (So she has a motive in that if he divorces her, etc.) — al-Maqdisi in his commentary said: That she has a motive in the divorce of her co-wife is far-fetched; it is only plausible if she...
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a critical refinement (hashiya-style) of the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It deals with the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the use of the word 'على' instead of 'ب' in khul'. The matn states that if the wife says 'Divorce me three times on condition of a thousand' (using 'على') and the husband gives one divorce, the divorce is revocable (raj'i) and she owes nothing. Imam Abu Hanifa holds this view, treating 'على' as a pure condition (shart) that does not distribute over parts. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) treat 'على' like 'ب', making it a consideration that must be apportioned proportionally. The commentary supports Abu Hanifa's view with an analogy from al-Siyar al-Kabir: if an imam grants aman (security) for three years for a thousand dinars, and then revokes after one year, he returns two-thirds; but if the aman is granted 'on condition of' a thousand dinars (not specifying duration as price), then if he revokes, he returns the whole thousand. This shows that 'على' indicates a condition that is not divisible. The passage then explains that if the husband gives all three divorces, he gets the full thousand even in one sitting, because the first two are revocable (raj'i), so the third finds her married. If the divorces are given in different sittings, there is dispute. The commentator then summarises the analysis from Fath al-Qadir: the word 'على' is ambiguous between isti'la (literal) and luzum (binding), and in the context of khul', it can mean either a pure condition or a consideration. There is no inherent preponderance, and the fact that the object is money does not make it automatically a consideration, because money can also be the subject of a pure condition (like 'If you divorce me, you get a thousand'). Thus, Abu Hanifa's position is defensible on linguistic and juristic grounds. Finally, the passage includes a textual note and a refutation of a claim in al-Tahrir that favoured the Sahibayn's view; the commentator Ibn Amir Haj argues that the principle of assuming consideration is not applicable here because divorce is not a pure exchange contract. The text ends mid-sentence with al-Maqdisi's comment on motive, which seems incomplete.

Key Terms
على (alā): Here disputed whether it indicates pure condition (shart) or consideration ('iwaḍ).
شرط محض (shart maḥḍ): A pure condition that does not involve exchange; the payment is contingent on the condition's occurrence, not a price for the divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a wife says 'طلقني ثلاثاً على ألف' and the husband divorces her once, what is the status of the divorce?
A) It is a ba'in divorce and she owes one-third
B) It is a revocable (raj'i) divorce and she owes nothing
C) It is invalid because the condition is not fulfilled
D) It depends on her acceptance

Key Takeaway
The word 'على' in khul' is a locus of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school, with Abu Hanifa's view that it indicates a pure condition being the mufta bihi for most later scholars.

Dispute on the Word 'Ala in Khul' with Incomplete Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the word 'ala in khul' with partial fulfillment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over the interpretation of 'ala in khul' and apply each view to determine the financial obligation when the husband divorces fewer times than requested.

Core Idea
In khul', 'ala indicates condition per Abu Hanifa, exchange per Sahibayn—dispute turns on linguistic analysis.

This passage delves into a classic intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the interpretation of the word 'ala when used in a khul' agreement. The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn reveals deeper principles about how language is interpreted in the law of divorce. Understanding this dispute will sharpen your ability to see how linguistic ambiguity leads to legal consequences, especially when a condition is partially fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the contested word
The wife says 'divorce me three times on (ala) a thousand' and the husband divorces only once. The word 'ala is the focus of the dispute.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
He rules the divorce is revocable and no money is owed because 'ala indicates a condition, and a condition is not divisible among its parts.
Condition is not apportioned.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
They rule the divorce is irrevocable and a proportionate share of the thousand is due because 'ala indicates exchange, like the preposition 'ba' (for).
Exchange implies payment for partial performance.
4
Analyze the linguistic and analogical arguments
Abu Hanifa uses the analogy from amnesty in siyar: if an imam grants amnesty for three years on a thousand, then repudiates after one year, he returns two-thirds of the thousand, but if he grants amnesty on (ala) a thousand, he returns all. The Sahibayn treat 'ala like 'ba' in sales.
Linguistic analysis from Fath al-Qadir.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Abu Hanifa, the husband gets no money; under the Sahibayn, he gets a proportionate share (e.g., one-third if one divorce out of three).
Also affects revocability: revocable vs irrevocable.

His statement: (And in 'ala, it occurs as revocable for free) i.e., in her saying 'divorce me three times on [condition of] a thousand' or 'on that you owe me a thousand,' and he divorces her once, it occurs as revocable without anything upon her according to the Imam, contrary to them. For they (the Sahibayn) made it like 'ba' (i.e., for a price), while he made it for the condition, and the conditioned is not distributed among the parts of the condition. Do you not see that it is mentioned in al-Siyar al-Kabir: if the imam granted amnesty for three years for a thousand dinars, then it appears to the imam to repudiate them after one year, he returns two-thirds of the thousand to them; and if he granted amnesty on (ala) a thousand dinars, he returns all. Thus in al-Muhit. He restricted [the ruling] to his divorcing her once, because if he divorced her three times, he deserves the thousand. And if he divorced her three times separatedly in one sitting, the thousand is incumbent upon her, because the first and second occur as revocable according to him, so the pronouncing of the third finds her married, so he becomes entitled to the thousand dirhams. And if he divorced her three times in three sittings, according to them, one-third of the thousand is not obligatory, while according to him, nothing is obligatory. Thus in al-Muhit. The summary of what he verified in Fath al-Qadir is that the word 'ala is shared between [the meanings of] superiority and necessary connection. When attached to physical bodies, it is for superiority; and in other cases, for necessary connection. It applies to pure condition, like 'you are divorced on condition that you enter the house,' and to exchange like 'sell me this for a thousand.' Whether it is a pure condition as we gave as example, or customary like 'do so-and-so on condition that I help you.' The disputed case is valid for both condition and exchange, and there is no preponderance. The fact that its object is wealth does not give preponderance to the meaning of exchange, because wealth can be made a pure condition, like 'if you divorce me three times, you have a thousand.' Thus.

His statement: (He returns two-thirds of the thousand. Thus in this copy 'two-thirds' with an alif as the subject of 'returns.' While in other copies it is 'third' without alif, which is not apparent.) His statement: (And in al-Tahrir, something that preponderates their view...) The commentator, the researcher Ibn Amir Haj, objected to it, that the principle of what is known as being met with compensation is only in what necessitates pure legal exchange. As for what permits pure condition, and divorce is of this type, the fact that its object is wealth is not a preponderance for the meaning of exchange, because wealth can be made a pure condition. His statement: (For she has an interest in that if he divorces her...) al-Maqdisi said in his commentary: That she has an interest in the divorce of her co-wife is far-fetched; it would be close only if she...

For a thousand or on a thousand, and she divorces once, nothing occurs. 'You are divorced for a thousand' or 'on a thousand,' and she accepts, it becomes obligatory. Wealth is obligatory due to doubt, and caution is not taken in obligation because the original is that the liability is free. And some made it for superiority in reality and for necessary connection as a metaphor, because metaphor is better than homonymy. It is refuted that the literal meaning is only due to the immediate understanding among the people of language, and it is immediate like the immediate understanding of superiority. And metaphor being better than homonymy is only in case of hesitation; but when there is evidence of the literal meaning—which is immediate understanding upon unrestricted mention—then not. And it is mentioned in al-Tahrir that which preponderates their view, by rejecting his statement in his proof that there is no preponderance; rather, there is a preponderance of exchange, because the principle of what is known as being met with compensation is [exchange]. And it is not refuted by the case where she says 'divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand' and he divorces her alone, where they agreed that she is obliged for her share of the thousand, because she has no interest in the divorce of her co-wife such that it would be treated as a condition, unlike the stipulation of three [divorces] for obtaining the major separation. Thus they mentioned. And it is not without something, for she has an interest in that after he divorces her, her co-wife will not remain with him. So it is better that it be on disagreement also, as in Ghayat al-Bayan attributed to al-Mukhtalif. Then I saw in al-Tatarkhaniyya that the most correct is that it is on disagreement, and in it is what if she says 'divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand on me' and he divorces one of them, there is no narration. It may be said that she is obliged for her share of the thousand, and it may be said that nothing is obligatory until he divorces both. And in al-Muhit: She said 'divorce me and so-and-so and so-and-so for a thousand,' and he divorced one, and their dowers are equal—one-third of the thousand is obligatory, because she commanded him to [perform] contracts, since the divorce of each is a separate khul' for wealth, so the thousand is divided among them necessarily, because for each contract there must be a separate consideration so that the exchange is valid. This reasoning is not refuted by anything.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage presents a major intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the word 'ala (على) in khul' and the scenario where the wife demands three divorces in exchange for a thousand (e.g., 'divorce me three times on a thousand' or 'on that you owe me a thousand'), but the husband divorces her only once. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the single divorce occurs as a revocable divorce (talaq raj'iy) without any financial obligation on the wife. His reasoning: 'ala in this context indicates a condition (shart), and the conditioned (the thousand) is not divided among the parts of the condition; just as in the example from al-Siyar al-Kabir, if an imam grants amnesty for three years for a thousand, then repudiates after one year, he returns two-thirds of the thousand; but if he grants amnesty 'on' (ala) a thousand, he returns the entire thousand. Thus, the word 'ala is treated as a conditional particle. The Sahibayn, however, treat 'ala like the letter ba (ب) in 'for a thousand,' implying a direct exchange (mu'awada). They rule that the single divorce is irrevocable (ba'in) and the wife owes a proportionate share of the thousand (e.g., one-third, since three divorces were requested for the full amount). The text then elaborates on the meaning of 'ala, citing Fath al-Qadir: it is a homonym between 'superiority' and 'necessary connection.' When attached to physical objects, it means physical elevation; otherwise, it indicates obligation or condition. It can be a pure condition (e.g., 'you are divorced on condition that you enter the house') or an exchange (e.g., 'sell me this for a thousand'). In the disputed context, both meanings are possible, and there is no inherent preponderance. The fact that the object of 'ala is wealth does not tip the scale toward exchange, because wealth can also be a condition (e.g., 'if you divorce me three times, you get a thousand'). The text then discusses a supercommentary by Ibn Amir Haj objecting to al-Tahrir's attempt to preponderate the Sahibayn's view, insisting that the default in such contexts is conditionality, not exchange. The passage further considers related cases: (1) If the wife says 'divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand' and he divorces only her, the Sahibayn and Imam agree she owes her share (one-half if dowers equal). This differs from the three-divorce case because she has no motive to divorce her co-wife, so the conditionality is weaker. However, some argue she does have a motive (since after her divorce, her co-wife would not remain with the husband), so the difference should be on disagreement as well. The text then cites al-Muhit for a case with three co-wives: if she says 'divorce me and so-and-so and so-and-so for a thousand' and he divorces only one, she owes one-third of the thousand because each divorce is a separate contract, and the thousand must be divided among them for the exchange to be valid. The author notes that this reasoning is sound. Overall, the passage is a detailed exploration of the semantics of 'ala and its fiqh consequences in khul', reflecting the complexity of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Key Terms
على (ʻalā): In khul' context, a particle that may indicate either condition (shart) or exchange (mu'awada). Abu Hanifa interprets as condition; Sahibayn as exchange.
خلع (khulʻ): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for a payment (usually financial) to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when the wife says 'divorce me three times on a thousand' and the husband divorces once, what is the ruling?
A) One revocable divorce occurs and she owes nothing.
B) One irrevocable divorce occurs and she owes one-third.
C) The divorce is invalid until she pays.
D) Three divorces occur and she owes the full thousand.

Key Takeaway
The meaning of 'ala in khul' is disputed between condition and exchange, leading to different financial obligations when the divorce is partially carried out.

Partial Exercise of Delegated Divorce: Effect When Husband Stipulates Full Consideration
Ruling when husband authorizes wife to divorce herself thrice for a thousand, and she divorces once

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a husband delegates divorce with a specified consideration, the wife's partial exercise is ineffective unless the full consideration is secured.

Core Idea
The offeror's condition binds the offeree; partial acceptance fails the condition.

This lesson examines a classic case in Hanafi delegated divorce (tafwid). The husband says 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand dirhams,' but the wife divorces only once. The ruling hinges on who initiated the offer: the husband's condition of a full thousand must be met, so the partial divorce is void. We will parse the reasoning and contrast it with the reverse scenario where the wife initiates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their statements
First, identify that the husband is the offeror (he says 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand'), and the wife is the offeree (she divorces once). Note the consideration (khul' payment) is a thousand dirhams.
The offer includes a condition: the full thousand must remain safe for the husband.
2
Analyze the condition of the offeror
The husband's consent to separation (baynuna) is tied to the entire thousand being his. He would not agree to less. Therefore, the wife's act of divorcing once does not match his offer.
This is a form of conditional acceptance; the condition is explicit in the husband's wording.
3
Contrast with wife-initiated scenario
If the wife says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand,' she is the offeror. If the husband divorces her once, it is valid because she implicitly accepts a partial separation for a proportionate payment. The difference is who originated the offer.
The reasoning uses the principle that one who accepts a whole implicitly accepts a part (al-rida bi al-kull rida bi al-juz').
4
State the ruling and legal effect
The ruling: no divorce occurs (the act is void) and no money is owed. The marriage remains intact. The wife's act is legally ineffective because the condition of the husband's offer is not fulfilled.
The hukm level is batil (void) for the divorce act; the marriage persists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً بألف أو علي ألف فطلقت نفسها واحدة لم يقع شيء) لأنه لم يرض بالبينونة إلا بسلامة الألف كلها له بخلاف قولها له طلقني ثلاثاً بألف لأنها لما رضيت بالبينونة بألف كانت ببعضها أولى أن ترضى فظهر الفرق بين ابتدائه وابتدائها.
His statement: (Divorce yourself three times for a thousand or on a thousand, and she divorces herself once, nothing occurs) because he did not consent to separation except with the entire thousand being safe for him, contrary to her statement to him 'divorce me three times for a thousand,' because when she consented to separation for a thousand, she is more likely to consent to a part of it. So the difference between his initiation and her initiation appears.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling where the husband initiates the Khul' by telling his wife 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand' (or 'on a thousand'). If she divorces herself only once, no divorce occurs and no money is owed. The reasoning: the husband's condition is that the entire thousand be safe for him; he would not agree to separation (bainuna) for less than the full amount. This is contrasted with the reverse situation where the wife initiates by saying 'divorce me three times for a thousand'. In that case, if the husband divorces her once, it is effective for a share of the money because she initiated by accepting separation for a thousand, so she implicitly accepts a part of it as well. The key difference lies in who initiated the offer: the husband, as the offeror, sets the full condition; the wife, as the offeree, can accept partially. This illustrates a nuanced principle in Hanafi Khul' and conditional divorce.

Key Terms
بينونة (baynūna): Separation; the end of marital relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One revocable divorce occurs and she owes one-third of the thousand.
B) No divorce occurs and she owes nothing.
C) One irrevocable divorce occurs and she owes a thousand.
D) The divorce is valid but she owes nothing.

Key Takeaway
When the husband conditions a divorce delegation on a full consideration, the wife's partial exercise is void; the offeror's condition governs the validity of acceptance.

Proxy's Divorce in Khul' with Installments
Ruling on proxy divorcing in installments for a lump sum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a proxy pronounces three divorces in installments for a lump sum and identify the payment obligation for each divorce.

Core Idea
A proxy's pronouncement of multiple divorces in sunni style triggers only one divorce at a time, with payment due only for the first.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from al-Khaniyya where a husband authorizes a proxy to divorce his wife three times for a lump sum of a thousand. The proxy pronounces the entire formula at the first pure period. We will parse the ruling on how many divorces take effect and what the wife owes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the authorization
The husband says to the proxy: 'Divorce my wife three times for the Sunnah for a thousand.' This delegates authority to pronounce three sunni divorces with a lump-sum payment.
The phrase 'for the Sunnah' indicates each divorce must be issued in a separate pure period.
2
Analyze the proxy's pronouncement
The proxy says to the wife: 'You are divorced three times for the Sunnah for a thousand' at the first appropriate time (her pure period). She accepts.
Despite saying 'three times', only one divorce takes effect immediately because sunni divorce requires sequential pronouncements in separate tuhr periods.
3
Determine the first divorce and payment
The ruling: one divorce occurs, and the wife owes one-third of the thousand (the agreed total for three divorces). The remaining two divorces are treated as pending.
The lump sum is apportioned: each divorce is valued at one-third, but only the first is due now.
4
Handle subsequent divorces
If the proxy issues a second divorce in the next pure period (for one-third), it takes effect without any additional payment, because the total thousand already covered all three.
Similarly for the third divorce in the third pure period.
5
Consider the remarriage variant
If after the first divorce the husband remarries her, and then the proxy divorces her again (with a separate pronouncement), the second divorce also occurs without additional payment. The proxy's authority continues even after remarriage.
This shows that the proxy's authorization is not extinguished by an intervening marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية : رجل قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقبلت تقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت تقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث. ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف
And in al-Khaniyya: A man said to another, 'Divorce my wife three times for the Sunnah for a thousand,' so the proxy said to her at the time of the Sunnah, 'You are divorced three times for the Sunnah for a thousand,' and she accepted, then one divorce occurs for one-third of the thousand. Then if the proxy divorces her in the second pure period with a divorce for one-third of the thousand, and she accepts, another occurs without anything. And likewise if he divorces her the third time in the third pure period. And if the proxy first divorced her with one divorce for one-third of the thousand, then the husband remarries her, then the proxy divorces her a second time for one-third of the thousand...
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage from al-Khaniyya discusses a case where a husband authorizes a proxy to divorce his wife three times in accordance with the Sunnah (i.e., one divorce per waiting period) for a total payment of a thousand. The proxy pronounces the entire formula 'you are divorced three times for the Sunnah for a thousand' at the first appropriate time (the wife's pure period). She accepts. The ruling is that only one divorce occurs, and she owes one-third of the thousand. The remaining two divorces do not take effect immediately because the pronouncement of 'three' is considered a promise or conditional, but the actual divorce is valid only for one. Subsequently, if the proxy divorces her in the second pure period with a separate pronouncement for one-third, and she accepts, a second divorce occurs but without any additional payment (since the thousand was already for the entire three). The third divorce likewise is without further payment. This shows the Hanafi treatment of a proxy's pronouncement in khul' when the payment is lump-sum but the divorces are executed in installments. The passage also mentions a variant where after the first divorce, the husband remarries her, and then the proxy gives a second divorce; this suggests that the proxy's authority may continue after remarriage, a nuance in Hanafi law.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): A proxy or agent authorized by the husband to pronounce divorce.
السنة (al-sunna): Divorce according to the Sunnah; i.e., one divorce in each pure period (non-menstrual period) without preceding intercourse.
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) She owes a full thousand.
B) She owes one-third of the thousand for the first divorce, and nothing for subsequent.
C) She owes nothing until all three divorces are executed.
D) She owes one-third for each divorce when executed.

Key Takeaway
A proxy's single pronouncement of multiple sunni divorces for a lump sum results in only one divorce and proportional payment; subsequent divorces require separate pronouncements in later pure periods but no extra payment.

The Meaning of 'على' in Khul': Condition or Demand?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'على' in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute over the meaning of 'على' in khul' and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) for when the wife's payment becomes binding.

Core Idea
The word 'على' in khul' determines if payment is a condition or an integral part of the exchange.

This passage explores a subtle but consequential linguistic dispute within the Hanafi school: does the word 'على' in a khul' formula create a condition or a direct demand? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ, and their disagreement affects when the divorce falls and when the wife must pay. Understanding this disagreement sharpens your ear for the force of prepositions in legal language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed term and the positions
Identify that the dispute centers on the word 'على' in khul' formulas. Abu Hanifa holds that 'على' implies a condition (the divorce is contingent on payment), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'على' is like 'بـ' and immediately binds the wife to pay upon acceptance.
The practical effect: when the husband says 'أنت طالق على ألف', according to Abu Hanifa the divorce falls only if she accepts in the session; according to the Sahibayn it falls immediately and she owes the thousand.
2
Analyze the linguistic argument: literal vs metaphorical meaning
Abu Hanifa argues that 'على' literally means 'upon' (higherness) and metaphorically means 'bindingness'. The immediate understanding (tabādur) of Arabic speakers is the literal meaning, which supports his view that 'على' indicates a condition. The Sahibayn counter that metaphor is preferable to polysemy (multiple meanings of 'على'), and the context of exchange indicates compensation.
The author notes that the preference of metaphor over polysemy only applies when there is hesitation; here the literal meaning is clear, so Abu Hanifa's argument stands.
3
Examine the proof from immediate understanding (tabādur)
The text states that the literal meaning is established by tabādur: when 'على' is uttered with a khul', Arabic speakers immediately understand a condition, not a direct demand. This is evidence that 'على' is not simply like 'بـ'.
Tabādur is a key usul principle for determining the literal meaning of a word.
4
Explore applied cases from the text
The author discusses a case where a wife says 'Divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand' and the husband divorces only her. The Sahibayn hold she owes her share, but Abu Hanifa might say nothing is owed until both are divorced, because she has an interest in the co-wife's divorce. The text also cites al-Muhit's reasoning that multiple khul' contracts require separate considerations.
This case tests the principle: does 'على' imply a condition for each divorce or a total exchange? The author leans toward the Sahibayn's view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and practical consequence
The author mentions that al-Tahrir gives preponderance to the Sahibayn's view, and al-Tatarkhaniyya states the most correct is that the dispute remains. However, later Hanafi practice favors the Sahibayn's view, making the mufta bihi that 'على' is like 'بـ' in binding the wife to pay immediately upon acceptance.
Thus, in fatwa, if a husband says 'أنت طالق على ألف' and she accepts, the divorce is effective and she owes the thousand at once.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بألف أو على ألف فطلقت واحدة لم يقع شيء أنت طالق بألف أو على ألف فقبلت لزم
يجب المال بالشك ولا يحتاط في اللزوم إذ الأصل فراغ ..الذمة ومنهم من جعلها للاستعلاء حقيقة وللزوم مجازاً لأن المجاز خير من الاشتراك ورد بأن المعنى الحقيقي ليس إلا لتبادر ذلك المعنى عند أهل اللسان وهو متبادر كتبادر الاستعلاء، وكون المجاز خيراً من الاشتراك إنما هو عند التردد، أما عند قيام دليل الحقيقة وهي التبادر بمجرد الإطلاق فلا. وذكر في التحرير ما يرجح قولهما بمنع قوله في دليله ولا مرجح بل فيه مرجح العوضية وهو أن الأصل فيما علمت مقابلته العوضية ولا يرد عليه لو قالت طلقني وضرتي على ألف فطلقها وحدها حيث وافقهما أنه يلزمها حصتها من الألف لأنه لا غرض لها في طلاق ضرتها حتى يجعل كالشرط بخلاف اشتراط الثلاث بتحصيل البينونة الغليظة ؛ كذا ذكروا. ولا يخلو من شيء فإن لها غرضاً في أنه إذا طلقها لا تبقى ضرتها معه بعدها فالأولى أن نكون على الاختلاف أيضاً كما في غاية البيان معزياً للمختلف. ثم رأيت في التتارخانية أن الأصح أنها على الخلاف وفيها ما لو قالت طلقني وضرتي على ألف علي فطلق إحداهما لا رواية فيها. ولقائل أن يقول يلزمها حصتها من الألف ولقائل أن يقول لا يلزمها شيء حتى يطلقهما جميعاً. وفي المحيط : قالت طلقني وفلانة وفلانة على ألف فطلق واحدة ومهورهن سواء يجب ثلث الألف لأنها أمرته بعقود لأن طلاق كل واحدة على مال خلع على حدة فانقسم الألف عليهن ضرورة أنه لا بد أن يكون لكل عقد بدل على حدة لتصح المعاوضة اهـ. وهذا التعليل لا يرد عليه شيء.
If (the wife says) 'with a thousand' or 'upon a thousand' and she divorced one (time), nothing falls. (But if the husband says) 'You are divorced with a thousand' or 'upon a thousand' and she accepts, it becomes binding. The money is required with doubt, and one does not exercise caution in bindingness because the default is freedom of the debt. Some consider 'على' to be literally for higherness and metaphorically for bindingness, because metaphor is better than polysemy. It is replied that the literal meaning is only due to the immediate understanding of that meaning by Arabic speakers, and it is immediately understood as is the understanding of higherness. The preference of metaphor over polysemy is only when there is hesitation; as for when evidence of the literal meaning exists—which is immediate understanding upon absolute utterance—then not. And it is mentioned in al-Tahrir what gives preponderance to their (the Sahibayn's) position by preventing his (Abu Hanifa's) argument in his proof, and there is no preponderant, rather there is a preponderant of compensation: that the default concerning what is known to be compensated is compensation. This is not contradicted by the case where she said, 'Divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand,' and he divorced only her, and they agreed that she owes her share of the thousand, because she has no interest in divorcing her co-wife such that it is made a condition, unlike stipulating three (divorces) to achieve severe separation; thus they mentioned. And it is not free from something: she has interest in that if he divorces her, her co-wife will not remain with him afterwards, so it is better that it be considered on the disagreement as well, as in Ghayat al-Bayan attributed to the dispute. Then I saw in al-Tatarkhaniyya that the most correct is that it is upon disagreement. In it is the case: if she said, 'Divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand upon me,' and he divorced one of them, there is no transmission. Some may say she owes her share of the thousand, and some may say nothing is owed until he divorces both. And in al-Muhit: She said, 'Divorce me and so-and-so and so-and-so for a thousand,' and he divorced one, and their dowers are equal, one-third of the thousand is owed because she commanded multiple contracts, for the divorce of each for wealth is a separate khul', so the thousand is divided among them by necessity, because each contract must have a separate consideration for the exchange to be valid. End quote. This reasoning is not contradicted by anything.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal effect of the word 'على' in khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation). The core issue is whether 'على' conveys a demand for a payment (like 'بـ') or a condition for the divorce. Abu Hanifa holds that 'على' implies a condition, meaning the divorce is contingent upon payment, so if the wife divorces herself with 'على', no divorce occurs unless she pays, and if the husband says 'على', the divorce only falls if she accepts in the session. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'على' is like 'بـ' in implying a binding exchange. The text discusses the linguistic arguments for and against. The author then mentions supporting cases from al-Tahrir, al-Tatarkhaniyya, and al-Muhit, including a case where a wife asks for divorce for herself and her co-wives, illustrating how the amount is divided proportionally. The passage concludes that the reasoning in al-Muhit is sound.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
على ('alā): Preposition meaning 'upon'; in khul' it indicates the payment is a condition for the divorce (according to Abu Hanifa) or a demand (according to Sahibayn).
تبادر (tabādur): Immediate understanding of a word's meaning by native speakers upon hearing it without context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The divorce is not effective because 'على' implies a condition that is not fulfilled.
B) The divorce is effective immediately, and she owes the thousand at once.
C) The divorce is effective only if she pays in the session.
D) The divorce is effective but she does not owe the thousand because 'على' is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
In khul', the interpretation of the preposition 'على' (whether as a condition or as an immediate demand) has a direct practical impact on when the divorce is effective and when the wife must pay, with the Hanafi school's mufta bihi treating it as equivalent to 'بـ'.

Partial Self-Divorce in Khul': When It Falls and When It Doesn't
Rulings when wife divorces herself or through agent with different wordings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife divorces herself less than instructed in khul', and distinguish the effect based on who initiated the wording.

Core Idea
A wife's partial self-divorce in khul' is valid only if she initiated the proposal; if the husband initiated, no divorce occurs unless full payment is made.

In khul' transactions, the exact wording of the divorce instruction determines whether a partial self-divorce takes effect. This lesson examines the critical distinction between a husband telling his wife 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand' and a wife asking her husband to divorce her for a thousand. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying Hanafi rulings on delegated divorce (tafwid) with compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between husband-initiated wording (e.g., 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand') and wife-initiated wording (e.g., she says 'divorce me three times for a thousand'). The ruling flips depending on who speaks first.
The key is who makes the offer of compensation.
2
Apply the rule for husband-initiated partial divorce
If the husband says 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand' and she divorces once, no divorce occurs because he only consented to separation if the full thousand is paid. Partial payment does not satisfy his condition.
Ruling: no fall of divorce at all.
3
Apply the rule for wife-initiated partial divorce
If the wife says 'divorce me three times for a thousand' and he divorces her once, one divorce falls because she is deemed willing to accept partial separation for a reduced amount.
Ruling: one divorce falls, and she owes a portion.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that if the wife says in one utterance 'I divorced myself three times for a thousand', no divorce ever falls. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say one falls. Understand the reasoning behind each view.
Mufta bihi is the majority view (one falls).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً بألف أو علي ألف فطلقت نفسها واحدة لم يقع شيء) لأنه لم يرض بالبينونة إلا بسلامة الألف كلها له بخلاف قولها له طلقني ثلاثاً بألف لأنها لما رضيت بالبينونة بألف كانت ببعضها أولى أن ترضى فظهر الفرق بين ابتدائه وابتدائها. وفي الخانية : رجل قال لغيره طلق امرأتي ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقال لها الوكيل في وقت السنة أنت طالق ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقبلت تقع واحدة بثلث الألف، فإن طلقها الوكيل في الطهر الثاني تطليقة بثلث الألف فقبلت تقع أخرى بغير شيء، وكذا لو طلقها الثالثة في الطهر الثالث. ولو طلقها الوكيل أولاً تطليقة بثلث الألف ثم تزوجها الزوج ثم طلقها الوكيل تطليقة ثانية بثلث الألف بقيت هي، ولأن طلب فراقها في الظاهر بدفعها المال له لشدة بغضها إياه فلا تطلب خلاص ضرتها معها لما بينهما غالباً من العداوة ويحتمل أن ضرتها وكلتها في طلب الفراق لمنفعة تعود إلى الضرة لا إليها فلا يلزمها غير حصتها بمجرد احتمال كون غرضها فراق الضرة أيضاً قوله : (ولقائل أن يقول يلزمها حصتها) قال في النهر : وعندي أن الثاني أوجه لأنها إذا كانت شرطاً مع عدم قولها على فمعه أولى فتدبره قوله : (وهذا التعليل لا يرد عليه شيء) أي بخلاف التعليل السابق فلو علل هناك بهذا لم تقع الثانية بثلث الألف، وكذا الثالثة على هذا الوجه .اهـ. وفي المحيط : قال للمدخولة طلقي نفسك ثلاثاً للسنة بألف فقالت طلقت نفسي ثلاثاً للسنة بألف ؛ فإن كانت طاهرة من غير جماع طلقت للحال واحدة ولا تقع الثانية والثالثة إلا بتجديد الإيقاع في مجلس السنة فيقعان بغير شيء. هكذا ذكر الزعفراني لأنه فوض إليها إيقاع كل تطليقة في كل طهر فيكون بمنزلة المضاف إلى وقت كل طهر لم يجامعها فيه فلا تملك إيقاعها حتى يجيء الوقت وقد أمرها بالإيقاع فلا بد من التجديد وإنما يقعان مجاناً لأنها بانت بالأولى فلا تملك نفسها بالثانية والثالثة ألا ترى أنه لو أمرها أن تطلق نفسها ببدل بعدما أبانها ففعلت وقع مجاناً، وفي رواية محمد لا يقع بهذا القول أبداً لأنه تعذر إيقاعهما بعوض لما بينا وتعذر إيقاعهما بغير عوض لأن الزوج لم يرض بوقوعهما مجاناً فلم يقعا .اهـ.
His saying: '(Divorce yourself three times with a thousand or upon a thousand) and she divorced herself once, nothing falls' — because he did not agree to separation except with the safety of the entire thousand for him, unlike her saying to him 'divorce me three times with a thousand' because when she agreed to separation for a thousand, she is more apt to agree for part of it. So the difference appears between his initiation and her initiation. In al-Khaniyya: A man said to another, 'Divorce my wife three times according to sunna for a thousand,' so the agent said to her in the time of sunna, 'You are divorced three times according to sunna for a thousand,' and she accepted, one divorce falls with one-third of the thousand. If the agent divorces her in the second purity period with one-third of the thousand and she accepts, another falls without anything. Similarly if he divorces her the third in the third purity period. And if the agent first divorced her once with one-third of the thousand, then the husband remarried her, then the agent divorced her a second time with one-third of the thousand, she remains (not divorced). And because her request for separation outwardly by paying money to him is due to intense hatred, so she does not request the rescue of her co-wife with her due to the usual enmity between them. And it is possible that her co-wife appointed her to seek separation for a benefit returning to the co-wife, not to her, so she is not bound to more than her share merely by the possibility that her intention is also the co-wife's separation. His saying: (And it may be said that she owes her share). Al-Nahr said: In my view the second is more appropriate because if it is a condition with her not saying 'upon', then with it is even more appropriate, so reflect. His saying: (And this reasoning is not rebutted by anything) — meaning unlike the previous reasoning, for if that had been reasoned with this, the second would not fall with one-third of the thousand, and similarly the third accordingly. End quote. And in al-Muhit: He said to a consummated wife, 'Divorce yourself three times according to sunna for a thousand,' and she said, 'I divorced myself three times according to sunna for a thousand.' If she was pure without intercourse, she is divorced immediately once, and the second and third do not occur except by renewing the utterance in the session of sunna, and they fall without anything. Thus mentioned al-Za'farani because he delegated to her the utterance of each divorce in each purity period, so it is like being added to the time of each purity period in which he did not have intercourse with her, so she does not have the power to utter it until the time comes, and he commanded her to utter, so renewal is necessary. And they fall for free because she became separated by the first, so she does not own herself for the second and third. Do you not see that if he commanded her to divorce herself for a compensation after he separated her, and she did, it would fall for free? And in the narration of Muhammad, it never falls by this statement because it is impossible to utter them with compensation as we explained, and it is impossible to utter them without compensation because the husband did not agree to their falling for free, so they do not fall. End quote.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling when a husband instructs his wife to divorce herself for a payment and she does less than instructed. If the husband says 'divorce yourself three times for a thousand' and she divorces herself once, no divorce occurs because he only agreed to separation if the entire thousand is safe. However, if the wife had asked the husband to divorce her three times for a thousand and he does once, then it falls because she is deemed willing to accept partial. The text then presents cases from al-Khaniyya involving an agent appointed to divorce the wife in specific tuhr periods, and from al-Muhit where the wife is told to divorce herself according to sunna. Important distinctions are drawn regarding timing, delegation, and the effect of becoming irrevocably separated. The author also notes a narration of Muhammad where if the wife says 'I divorced myself three times' in one utterance, it never falls because it is impossible to intend the latter two with the first.

Key Terms
التطليقة (al-tatliqah): One count of divorce; used in counting divorces in khul' scenarios.
مجلس السنة (majlis al-sunnah): The session of sunna divorce, i.e., a pure period without intercourse.
الخلع (al-khul'): A separation initiated by the wife in exchange for a payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One divorce occurs, and she owes one-third of the thousand.
B) No divorce occurs because the husband did not consent to partial separation.
C) Three divorces occur immediately.
D) One divorce occurs, but she owes nothing.

Key Takeaway
The initiation of the divorce wording determines whether a partial self-divorce in khul' is valid: if the husband initiates, no partial divorce falls; if the wife initiates, partial divorce counts proportionally.

Khul' Scenarios: A Decision Tree Summary
Summary of khul' scenarios with rulings on compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on compensation for each khul' scenario based on who initiates and the wording used.

Core Idea
In khul', compensation depends on who initiates, the wording, and the number of divorces actually pronounced.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a structured summary of all possible khul' scenarios. It serves as a mnemonic for the Hanafi rulings on when the wife owes compensation and how much. By mastering this decision tree, you will be able to quickly determine the financial outcome in any khul' case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Initiator
First, determine who requested the divorce: the wife (she asks him for divorce) or the husband (he asks her for property). This sets the main branch.
If husband asks, the ruling is straightforward: he gets his request.
2
Wife Initiates: Husband's Response
If wife initiates, check whether the husband responds with exactly the number of divorces she asked for. If yes, he deserves the named amount. If no, proceed to the wording.
3
Wife Initiates, Husband Deviates: Wording of Request
If the husband deviates, see how the wife phrased her request: with 'bā' (الباء) or 'alā' (على). This determines how the compensation is handled.
'Bā' implies direct exchange; 'alā' implies condition.
4
Apply the Ruling for 'bā'
If she used 'bā', the divorces that occur are effective and the total amount is divided proportionally. If the number she asked for completes three, he gets the full amount; otherwise, he gets a fraction.
5
Apply the Ruling for 'alā'
If she used 'alā', compare the number she asked for with what he gave. If he gave fewer, it falls without payment. If he gave more, check if he mentioned the money in his response – if yes, she must accept or reject; if no, three divorces fall without compensation. Also note the difference between stating three in one word vs separately.
Separate pronouncements: only the first is with compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحاصل أنه لا يخلو إما أن تسأله الطلاق أو يسألها على مال، فإن كان الأول، فإما أن يجنبها بالموافقة أو لا، فإن كان الأول فظاهر واستحق المسمى وإن كان الثاني فإما أن تسأله بالباء أو بـ«على»، فإن كان بالباء وقع ما به وانقسم المال على عدد الطلقات فكان له بحسابه إن لم يحصل مقصودها، فإن حصل، فإن كانت الواحدة مكملة للثلاث استحق الكل، وإن كان بـ «على»، فإما إن كانت المخالفة بأنقص أو بأزيد، فإن كان بأنقص وقع بغير شيء، وإن كان الثاني كما لو سألته واحدة بألف فطلقها ثلاثاً، فإن ذكر المال في جوابه وقع الثلاث بالمسمى إن قبلت وإلا فلا، وإن لم يذكر وقع الثلاث بغير شيء. وهذا كله إن ذكر الثلاث بكلمة واحدة وإن ذكر متفرقة وقعت الأولى بالمال وثنتان بغير شيء.
The conclusion: It is not free from either she asks him for divorce or he asks her for property. If the first, then either he responds to her request accordingly or not. If the first, then it is apparent and he deserves the named amount. If the second, then either she asks him with 'bā' or with 'alā'. If with 'bā', what occurs falls and the amount is divided by the number of divorces, and he gets according to it if her objective is not achieved. If it is achieved, then if the one (divorce) completes three, he deserves the entire amount. If with 'alā', then either the discrepancy is less or more. If less, it falls without anything. If the second, as if she asked him for one divorce for a thousand and he divorced her three, then if he mentioned the property in his answer, the three fall with the named amount if she accepts, otherwise not. If he did not mention, the three fall without anything. All this is if he mentioned three with one word. If he mentioned them separately, the first falls with the property and the two fall without anything.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage provides a concise summary of all possible khul' scenarios. It categorizes by who initiates (wife asks husband vs husband asks wife for property). If wife asks, and he complies exactly, he gets the named amount. If he deviates, then the wording matters: if she used 'bā', the divorces that occur are distributed proportionally; if she used 'alā', then if he gives fewer divorces it falls without payment, if he gives more, it depends on whether he mentions the property in his response. The summary also covers the case of stating three divorces in one word vs separate words. This is a valuable mnemonic for students of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الباء (al-bā'): Preposition 'with' used in khul' to indicate the compensation is directly exchanged.
المسمى (al-musammā): The named amount of compensation agreed upon in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the summary, if a wife asks her husband 'طلقني واحدة بألف' and he instead divorces her three times without mentioning the thousand in his response, what happens?
A) Three divorces occur and she owes nothing.
B) Three divorces occur and she owes a thousand.
C) One divorce occurs and she owes a thousand.
D) Only one divorce occurs and she owes nothing.

Key Takeaway
In khul', the compensation is determined by who initiates, the wording used, and whether the husband complies exactly or not.

Acceptance of Khul' Must Be in the Same Session
Ruling on acceptance timing and partial acceptance in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that acceptance of khul' must occur in the same session as the offer and apply the rule to scenarios of partial acceptance.

Core Idea
Acceptance of khul' must be in the same session; partial acceptance of the payment, not the divorce, is invalid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the wife's acceptance of khul' must occur in the same session as the husband's offer. It also addresses complex scenarios of partial acceptance — whether she can accept only part of the divorce pronouncement or only part of the compensation. These rulings stem from the principle that khul' is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah), so it follows contract law requiring offer and acceptance to meet in one session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the wife's acceptance of the husband's offer of khul'. The ruling: if accepted in the same session, the compensation becomes binding and the divorce is bā'in (irrevocable).
The text emphasizes that acceptance must be in the session; otherwise, no divorce occurs.
2
Locate the dalil
No explicit Quran or Hadith is quoted; the proof is qiyas (analogy) to contracts of exchange, which require offer and acceptance in the same session.
The underlying principle: khul' is a mu'awadah (exchange of divorce for compensation), so it follows the rules of sales.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause (illah) is the exchange nature (mu'awadah). Just as in a sale the offer and acceptance must be in the same session for the contract to be binding, similarly in khul'.
Hanafi usul: qiyas is valid here because the illah is clear (jaliyyah).
4
Apply to partial acceptance scenarios
Two cases: (a) She accepts half the divorce pronouncement → valid, full compensation due; (b) She accepts half the compensation → invalid, no divorce occurs. Why? The compensation (badal) is a single price; partial acceptance of the price is like accepting partial payment in a sale, which is invalid.
The text from al-Tatarkhaniyya: 'and if she said I accept half of it for five hundred, it is invalid (bāṭil).'
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The requirement of same session is a contract principle generally accepted, but some schools might have different views on what constitutes a 'session'. The Hanafi position is strict.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih; some schools may not require acceptance in the same session.

Source Text

His saying: (You are divorced with a thousand or upon a thousand, and if she accepts it becomes binding and she becomes separated) — meaning if she accepts in the session, the money becomes binding and the woman becomes separated. This is a repetition because it is known from his saying, and from the chapter that it occurs, and by divorce for property, it is an irrevocable divorce and the money becomes binding on her, except that he added the acceptance only here. And if he had mentioned it at his saying 'and the money becomes binding on her', he would have been spared from prolongation. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: If he said to his wife, 'You are divorced one with a thousand,' and she said, 'I accept half of this divorce,' she is divorced once with a thousand without disagreement. And if she said, 'I accept half of it for five hundred,' it is invalid. And if she said to her husband, 'Divorce me once for a thousand,' and the husband said, 'You are divorced half a divorce for a thousand dirhams,' — a divorce for a thousand dirhams. And if he said, 'You are divorced half a divorce for five hundred,' she is divorced once for five hundred. End quote. And in al-Muhit, attributed to al-Muntaqa: 'You are divorced four times for a thousand,' and she accepted, she is divorced three times for a thousand, and if... the property... his saying: (She is divorced immediately once) — al-Nahr said: meaning with one-third of the thousand. Commentary
This passage comments on the matn statement that if the husband says 'أنت طالق بألف' or 'على ألف' and she accepts, she becomes irrevocably divorced and owes the money. The commentator notes that the acceptance must occur in the same session as the offer. The text then brings rulings from al-Tatarkhaniyya about partial acceptance: if she accepts half of the divorce (i.e., half of the pronouncement), it is valid and she is divorced once for the full amount, but if she tries to accept half of the money, it is invalid. Also, if she asks for one divorce for a thousand and the husband says 'half a divorce', it is valid as one divorce for the amount mentioned. From al-Muhit, if he says 'you are divorced four for a thousand' and she accepts, she gets three for a thousand (since four is not possible). The passage ends with a textual note about the placement of the summary paragraph.

Key Terms
القبول (al-qabūl): Acceptance by the wife of the husband's offer of khul', required to be in the same session for validity.
البائن (al-bā'in): Irrevocable divorce; in khul', the divorce is bā'in, meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) She is divorced half a divorce for five hundred.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance of khul' must be in the same session; partial acceptance of the payment is invalid, but partial acceptance of the divorce pronouncement is valid as full.
