The Waw Dispute: Divorce and Payment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on waw interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of the waw in the phrase 'anti taliq wa 'alayki alf' and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'wa' in a divorce vow determines whether payment is required — Abu Hanifa's literal interpretation upholds the presumption of innocence from liability.

This passage examines a famous intra-Hanafi disagreement about the conjunction 'wa' when a husband says 'You are divorced and upon you is one thousand.' The dispute hinges on whether the waw is conjunctive, circumstantial, or resumptive, and affects whether the wife must pay if she does not accept. By studying this, you will learn how Hanafi jurists apply linguistic analysis (ilm al-ma'ani) and the principle of bara'at al-dhimmah (immunity of liability) to resolve doubts.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
The husband says to his wife: 'anti taliq wa 'alayki alf' — 'You are divorced and upon you is one thousand.' Identify the two components: talaq (divorce) and a financial obligation. The dispute is about the meaning of 'wa' that connects them.
2
Identify the Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: divorce falls immediately regardless of acceptance; payment is only due if she accepts. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): both divorce and payment fall only if she accepts; otherwise nothing occurs.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
3
Analyze the linguistic basis
Sahibayn interpret the waw as hal (circumstantial) meaning 'while upon you is one thousand', making payment a condition. Abu Hanifa interprets it as 'atf (conjunctive) or isti'naf (resumptive), keeping the two clauses independent. The disagreement stems from whether the first clause is khabar (informative) or insha' (performative).
Hanafi usul: default is literal meaning (haqiqah); metaphorical (majaz) requires a reason.
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
The commentator prefers Abu Hanifa's view based on bara'at al-dhimmah — the original presumption is that no payment is owed without clear evidence. Interpreting the waw as isti'naf avoids imposing liability without acceptance.
Tarjih relies on usul principle: al-asl bara'at al-dhimmah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the wife does not accept, according to Abu Hanifa she is divorced and owes nothing; according to Sahibayn, neither divorce nor payment occurs. This affects marital status and financial rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أنت طالق وعليك ألف أو أنت حر وعليك ألف طلقت وعتق مجاناً) يعني قبلاً أو لا عند الإمام، وعندهما وقع إن قبلا ولزمهما المال وإلا لا عملاً بأن الواو للحال مجازاً لتعذر حملها على العطف للانقطاع لأن الأولى جملة إنشائية والثانية خبرية، وعنده الواو للعطف هنا عملاً بالحقيقة ولا انقطاع لأن التحقيق أن الجملة الأولى خبرية لا انشائية؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وذكر في تحريره أن الأوجه أن الواو للاستئناف عدة أو غيره لا للعطف للانقطاع، ولا شك أنه مجاز لكن ترجح على مجاز أنها للحال بالأصل وهو براءة الذمة وعدم إلزام المال بلا معين، واتفقوا على أنها للحال في أد الي ألفاً وأنت حر» و «انزل وأنت آمن» لتعذر العطف لكمال الانقطاع بين الجملتين لكنه من باب القلب لأن الشرط الأداء والنزول، واتفقوا على أنها بمعنى الباء وهو المعاوضة في قوله احمل هذا الطعام ولك درهم لأن العطف المعاوضة في الإجارة أصلية، واتفقوا على تعين الأصل وهو من غير احتمال غيره في
His statement: 'You are divorced and upon you is one thousand' or 'You are free and upon you is one thousand' — she is divorced and becomes free without payment, meaning whether she accepts or not according to al-Imam. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it falls only if they accept and the payment becomes obligatory, otherwise not, acting on the basis that the waw is for hal (circumstantial) metaphorically because it is impossible to consider it as conjunctive due to disconnection because the first sentence is performative and the second is informative. According to him (Abu Hanifa), the waw here is conjunctive, acting on the literal meaning, and there is no disconnection because in reality the first sentence is informative, not performative. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And it is mentioned in his Tahrir that the most likely view is that the waw is for isti'naf (resumptive) for a promise or other, not for conjunction due to disconnection, and there is no doubt it is metaphorical, but it is preponderant over the metaphor of hal because the original is the immunity of liability and not imposing payment without a specified consideration. And they agreed that it indicates hal in 'Pay one thousand and you are free' and 'Descend and you are safe' because conjunction is impossible due to complete disconnection between the two sentences, but it is a case of inversion because the condition is payment and descent. And they agreed that it means ba (the preposition for exchange) in his statement 'Carry this food and you have a dirham' because conjunctive exchange in hiring is original. And they agreed on the determination of the original without any other possibility.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the meaning of the waw (واو) in the phrase 'أنت طالق وعليك ألف' (You are divorced and upon you is one thousand). The core issue is whether the waw indicates a conjunction (عطف) or a circumstantial clause (حال), which affects whether the payment (الألف) is owed. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the waw is conjunctive ('atf), meaning both the divorce and the payment are linked, so if she accepts, payment is due; but if she does not accept, the divorce falls regardless? Actually the text says: at Imam's view, she falls without payment whether she accepts or not? Wait the text says 'يعني قبلاً أو لا عند الإمام' meaning that according to Imam, she is divorced without payment regardless of acceptance. That is because he interprets the waw as conjunctive and the first sentence as informative (خبرية) not performative (إنشائية), so the statement is a report that combines both, and the payment is conditional on a contract which requires acceptance, but since the statement is unilateral, payment is not enforced without her acceptance? Actually the reasoning is that the waw is for 'atf, but because the first part is a report of divorce (which is not a request), and the second is a promise of payment, the payment is not binding unless she accepts, but the divorce occurs by his statement alone. So at Imam, without acceptance, divorce occurs without payment. At the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the waw is interpreted as hal (circumstantial), meaning 'while upon you is one thousand,' which makes the payment a condition for the divorce; thus divorce and payment depend on her acceptance. If she accepts, both occur; if not, neither. The commentator then discusses the linguistic evidence for each interpretation, noting that in other contexts like 'ادخل وأنت آمن' the waw must be hal because of the complete disconnection between the two sentences. He concludes that the most correct view (الأوجه) is that the waw is for isti'naf (resumptive), meaning a separate sentence, which also leads to the divorce being effective without payment unless she accepts. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi methodology of using linguistic analysis ('ilm al-ma'ani) to derive legal rulings.

Key Terms
الواو (al-waw): The conjunction 'and' or circumstantial particle here debated as 'atf (conjunction) vs. hal (circumstantial) vs. isti'naf (resumptive).
الحال (al-hal): Circumstantial clause indicating the condition in which an action occurs; here it would impose payment as a condition.
العطف (al-'atf): Conjunction linking two independent clauses.
الإستئناف (al-isti'naf): Resumptive, starting a new sentence; here it means the second clause is independent and expresses a promise.
براءة الذمة (bara'at al-dhimmah): Presumption of being free from liability; the principle that no payment is due without clear evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the commentator prefers Abu Hanifa's view over the Sahibayn's in the 'anti taliq wa 'alayki alf' dispute?
A) The Sahibayn's view contradicts a clear Quranic verse.
B) Abu Hanifa's view aligns with the principle of bara'at al-dhimmah.
C) The Sahibayn's view was never transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah.
D) Abu Hanifa's view is supported by a hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab resolves disputes over ambiguous phrases by combining linguistic analysis with core principles like bara'at al-dhimmah, giving preponderance to interpretations that align with original presumptions.

Exception to Payment Distribution When First Talaq is Ba'inah
Exception to payment distribution rule when first talaq is ba'inah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the exception rule for payment distribution in khul' when the first talaq is described as ba'inah or bighayr shay'.

Core Idea
Describing the first divorce as ba'inah negates payment for it; the badal belongs solely to the second.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains an exception to the general rule that when a husband pronounces two divorces with a single payment, the payment is split equally. The exception arises when the first divorce is described in a way that negates the obligation of payment, such as 'ba'inah' (irrevocable) or 'bighayr shay'' (with nothing). Understanding this exception is crucial for correctly distributing the badal in khul' arrangements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and general rule
The act is pronouncing two divorces (one immediate, one deferred) with a fixed total payment. The general rule is that the payment is distributed equally between both divorces.
This is the baseline before the exception.
2
Locate the exception
The exception is when the first divorce is described with something negating the obligation of payment, e.g., 'ba'inah' or 'bighayr shay''. This shifts the entire payment to the second divorce.
The key is the description of the first divorce only; describing both as ba'inah reverts to equal split.
3
Understand the linguistic implication
Describing a divorce as 'ba'inah' or 'bighayr shay'' indicates that the husband intends no financial compensation for that divorce. Therefore, the payment cannot be for it.
The description itself negates the obligation (wujub) of payment for that talaq.
4
Apply to the examples
In the text: if the husband says 'You are divorced now one ba'inah and tomorrow another ba'inah for a thousand,' the payment is split equally because both are described. If only the first is described as ba'inah, the payment goes entirely to the second, unless she remarries before the deferred time, in which case the second occurs and payment is split.
The remarriage condition: if he marries her again before the deferred time, the second divorce occurs and gets its half.
5
Summarize the logic
The description of the first divorce as negating payment means it receives no portion of the badal. The badal therefore attaches to the second divorce. If both are described, neither negates the payment for the other, so split.
This is a linguistic implication (wajh al-dalalah) underlying the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (إلا إذا وصف الأول بما ينافي الوجوب الخ أفاد هذا الاستثناء أن قوله «أولاً يكون مقابلاً بهما سواء لم يصف شيئاً منهما بالمنافي أو وصفهما جميعاً أو وصف الثاني فقط» يوضحه ما في التتارخانية عن المحيط ولو قال لها أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف أو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة بائنة وغداً أخرى بائنة بألف درهم أو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بألف درهم، فالبدل ينصرف إليهما ويكون كل تطليقة بنصف الألف فيقع واحدة في الحال بنصف الألف وغداً مجاناً إلا أن يتزوجها قبل مجيء الغد ثم جاء الغد فحينئذ تقع أخرى بنصف الألف ا هـ
His statement: 'Except when he describes the first with something negating obligation' etc. This exception indicates that his statement 'first' is considered to correspond to both, whether he did not describe either with negating, or described both, or described only the second. This is clarified by what is in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Muhit: If he said to her 'You are divorced now one, I have the right to take her back, and tomorrow another, I have the right to take her back, for one thousand,' or he said 'You are divorced now one ba'inah (irrevocably) and tomorrow another ba'inah for one thousand dirhams,' or he said 'You are divorced now one with nothing, and tomorrow another for one thousand dirhams,' then the payment is directed to both and each talaq is for half the thousand. So one falls now with half the thousand, and tomorrow without payment, unless he marries her before the coming of tomorrow, then when tomorrow comes, another falls with half the thousand.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage explains an exception to the general rule regarding the distribution of payment (badal) when a husband pronounces two divorces, one immediate and one deferred, specifying a total payment. The general rule is that the payment is distributed equally over both divorces. However, if the first divorce is described with something that negates the obligation of payment – such as 'ba'inah' (irrevocable) or 'bighayr shay' (with nothing) – then the payment does not apply to it; it applies only to the second divorce, resulting in the first falling without payment and the second with payment (if it occurs). The exception is detailed through examples from al-Tatarakhaniyya quoting al-Muhit. The key is that when the first talaq is described as ba'inah, it is known that the husband intended no payment for it, so the entire payment is for the second. If he does not describe either as negating payment, or describes both, or describes only the second, then the payment is equally split between both. The exception also covers a scenario where the second talaq is conditional on marriage before its occurrence; if she remarries before the deferred time, the second talaq takes effect and receives its half of the payment.

Key Terms
بائنة (ba'inah): An irrevocable divorce that does not allow revoking (ruju'), so it ends the marriage immediately without financial compensation for the husband.
بدل (badal): The payment (one thousand dirhams) that the wife owes in exchange for the divorce.
تطليقة (tatliqah): A single pronouncement of divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example where the husband says 'You are divorced now one ba'inah and tomorrow another ba'inah for one thousand dirhams,' and the second divorce occurs after remarriage, how is the payment distributed?
A) The first divorce gets 1000, the second gets 0.
B) Both get 500 each.
C) The first gets 0, the second gets 1000.
D) The first gets 500, the second gets 500.

Key Takeaway
Describing the first divorce as ba'inah or bighayr shay' negates payment for it, directing the entire badal to the second divorce; describing both as such leaves the payment split.

Payment Obligation in Khul' When Wife Says 'Taliqtuki bi-Alf'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on payment in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether payment is obligatory when a wife says 'Divorce me and you have one thousand' and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The wife's phrase 'wa laka alf' is a promise, not an offer — payment only due if specifically accepted.

In khul' transactions, the wording of the wife's request is critical. When she says 'Divorce me and you have one thousand,' does that constitute an offer of compensation? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differed on this point, with practical consequences for validity of divorce and payment obligation. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's statement
The wife says 'طلقني ولك ألف' or 'اخلعني ولك ألف'. Note the waw (and) – does it join a condition or a promise?
The wording is ambiguous; the waw could indicate a conditional offer or a mere promise.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
According to Abu Hanifa, the waw indicates a promise (وعد), not an offer. Therefore, if the husband divorces without explicitly conditioning on her acceptance, the divorce falls but she owes nothing.
Her statement is not a binding offer; it is a promise of a gift that she may or may not fulfill.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the waw indicates a conditional offer (تعويض). Thus, the husband's divorce is an acceptance of that offer, making payment obligatory.
They treat the phrase as an implicit offer of compensation for the divorce.
4
Apply to the al-Muhit case
In al-Muhit, the husband says 'I divorce you for the thousand you mentioned, if you accept'. If she accepts, all agree divorce and payment occur. If she does not accept, Abu Hanifa says nothing occurs; the Sahibayn say divorce still falls and payment is due, because they view the condition as invalid.
This shows the practical consequence: the condition of acceptance is effective only according to Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا الخلاف لو قالت طلقني ولك ألف أو اخلعني ولك ألف ففعل فعنده وقع ولم يجب المال. وقالا : يجب المال ؛ كذا في الكافي. وفي المحيط : لو قالت طلقني ولك ألف فقال طلقتك على الألف التي سميتها إن قبلت يقع الطلاق ويجب المال، وإن لم تقبل لا يقع الطلاق ولم يجب عنده لأنها التمست طلاقاً بغير عوض لأن قولها ولك ألف» لم يكن تعويضاً على الطلاق فقد أعرض الزوج عما التمست حيث أوقع طلاقاً تعوض، فإن قبلت وقع وإلا بطل. وعندهما يقع ويجب المال ا هـ
And based on this difference, if she said 'Divorce me and you have one thousand' or 'Khul' me and you have one thousand,' and he did (i.e., divorced her), then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it falls and payment is not obligatory. The two say: payment is obligatory. Thus in al-Kafi. And in al-Muhit: If she said 'Divorce me and you have one thousand,' and he said 'I divorce you for the thousand you mentioned, if you accept,' then the divorce falls and payment is obligatory if she accepts, but if she does not accept, the divorce does not fall and payment is not obligatory according to him, because she sought a divorce without compensation, since her saying 'and you have one thousand' was not a compensation for the divorce. So the husband turned away from what she sought by pronouncing a divorce with compensation. If she accepts, it falls; otherwise it is void. According to the two, it falls and payment is obligatory.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage continues the intra-Hanafi dispute in a different scenario: when the wife says 'طلقني ولك ألف' (Divorce me and you have one thousand). The same difference of opinion applies: According to Abu Hanifa, if the husband merely says 'divorced you', without specifying acceptance, the divorce falls without payment, because her phrase 'wa laka alf' is not an offer of compensation but a promise. According to the Sahibayn, it is an offer, and the husband's divorce is acceptance, so payment is due. The second example from al-Muhit clarifies: if the husband responds with an explicit conditional acceptance ('I divorce you for the thousand you mentioned, if you accept'), then if she accepts, all agree divorce and payment occur; if she does not accept, according to Abu Hanifa nothing occurs, while according to the Sahibayn, divorce falls (perhaps without payment? Actually the text says 'وعندهما يقع ويجب المال' meaning divorce falls and payment is obligatory regardless of her acceptance? That seems contradictory because in the first scenario they said payment is due even without acceptance. Let's read: 'فقال طلقتك على الألف التي سميتها إن قبلت' so he conditioned on her acceptance. If she does not accept, according to Abu Hanifa no divorce, but Sahibayn say divorce falls and payment is obligatory? That would mean the condition is invalid according to them. This is the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
تعويض (ta'wid): Compensation; here it means the payment in exchange for divorce.
وعد (wa'd): Promise; a non-binding commitment. Abu Hanifa considers the wife's statement a promise, not an offer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a wife says 'Divorce me and you have one thousand' and the husband says 'You are divorced,' what is the ruling?
A) Divorce does not fall because the husband did not mention the payment.
B) Divorce falls and she must pay one thousand.
C) Divorce falls but she does not have to pay.
D) Divorce is suspended until she accepts.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the wife's phrase 'wa laka alf' in a divorce request is treated as a promise, not an offer, so payment is not due unless the husband explicitly conditions the divorce on her acceptance.

Divorce Falling Without Payment Despite Mentioning Mal
Additional examples of talaq falling without payment when mal is mentioned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a divorce is effective without payment when the named mal is invalid or when the husband violates the wife's specified request.

Core Idea
A divorce with invalid mal or violation of wife's request is effective without payment.

The Hanafi school holds that mentioning mal in a divorce does not automatically obligate payment if the mal is not valid or if the husband does not comply with the wife's request. This lesson examines two cases from the matn: one involving an unowned slave, and another where the husband divorces three times when asked for one. Understanding these principles is crucial for applying the correct rulings in khul' and other conditional divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the mal mentioned
For the first case, pinpoint the husband's statement: 'You are divorced for this slave of mine.' For the second, note the wife's request: 'Divorce me once for one thousand' and the husband's response: three divorces without mentioning the thousand.
2
Check validity of the mal
In the first case, the slave turns out to be free, so the mal (the slave) is not valid property (not owned). In the second case, the husband did not mention the thousand, so no specific mal is named in his pronouncement.
Validity of mal depends on it being owned and deliverable.
3
Determine effect of invalidity on the divorce
According to Abu Hanifa, if the named mal is invalid, the divorce is effective without payment. This is because the condition for payment is not fulfilled. Zufur's analogy to a slave owned by another is rejected because delivery is impossible in the free slave case.
4
Identify violation in the second case
The wife asked for one divorce for one thousand; the husband gave three without mentioning the thousand. This is a violation (mukhalafah) of her request because he exceeded the number specified.
Abu Hanifa requires strict compliance for payment; violation nullifies the condition.
5
Determine ruling for violation
Abu Hanifa rules three divorces fall without payment. The Sahibayn say three fall but she owes one thousand for one divorce (the one she asked for), and the other two are without payment. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The Sahibayn view: he is considered to have responded to her request for one and initiated the other two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن الوقوع مجاناً مع ذكر المال لا يختص بمسألة الكتاب بل يكون في مسائل أخرى منها لو قال أنت طالق على عبدي هذا فإذا هو حر طلقت مجاناً لعدم صحة التسمية، وأوجب عليها زفر قيمته قياساً على تسمية عبد الغير، وفرقنا بإمكان تسليمه بإجازة مالكه في المقيس عليه وفي المقيس لا يتصور تسليمه. ومنها لو قالت طلقني واحدة بألف أو على ألف فطلقها ثلاثاً ولم يذكر الألف طلقت ثلاثاً مجاناً عنده للمخالفة، وعندهما طلقت ثلاثاً وعليها الألف بإزاء الواحدة لأنه مجيب بالواحدة مبتدئاً بالباقي، وإن ذكر الألف لا يقع شيء عنده ما لم تقبل المرأة، وإذا قبلت الكل وقع الثلاث بالألف، وعندهما إن لم تقبل فهي طالق واحدة فقط، وإن قبلت طلقت ثلاثاً واحدة بألف وثنتان بغير شيء؛ كذا في الكافي.
Then know that falling without payment despite mentioning payment is not specific to the issue of the book, but occurs in other issues: among them, if he said 'You are divorced for this slave of mine' and it turns out to be free, she is divorced without payment due to the invalidity of the named item. Zufur made its value obligatory by analogy to naming a slave belonging to another. We differentiated by the possibility of delivery with the owner's permission in the analogized case while in this case delivery is inconceivable. And among them, if she said 'Divorce me once for one thousand' or 'on one thousand,' and he divorced her three times without mentioning the thousand, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) she is divorced three times without payment due to violation (of her request). According to the two, she is divorced three times and owes the thousand for one (the first) because he responded to one and initiated the rest. If he mentioned the thousand, nothing falls according to him unless the woman accepts; if she accepts all, three fall for the thousand. According to the two, if she does not accept, she is divorced only once; if she accepts, she is divorced three times, one for a thousand and two with nothing.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage broadens the principle that a valid divorce can occur without payment even when mal was mentioned, if the mal is invalid for some reason. Two examples are given: (1) If the husband says 'You are divorced for this slave of mine' but the slave is actually free (not owned by him), the divorce is effective without payment because the named item is invalid (cannot be owned as property). Zufur analogizes to the case where a slave belonging to another is named, where the wife owes the value if she accepts, but here the husband's own slave is not owned – distinction: in the other case, delivery is possible with owner's permission; here, the slave is free, so no delivery possible. (2) If the wife says 'Divorce me once for one thousand' and the husband divorces her three times without mentioning the thousand, then according to Abu Hanifa, she is divorced three times without payment because he violated her request (she asked for one, he gave three). According to the Sahibayn, she is divorced three times and owes one thousand for the first (since that was the response to her request), the other two are free. If he mentions the thousand in his pronouncement, then at Abu Hanifa, nothing falls unless she accepts the whole; if she accepts, three fall for one thousand. At Sahibayn, if she does not accept, only one falls (the first) and she owes nothing for it? Actually the text says 'فهي طالق واحدة فقط' meaning one falls without payment? It says 'وإن لم تقبل فهي طالق واحدة فقط' not mentioning payment; but from context, since he mentioned thousand, it might be with payment? The text is complex, but the main point is the operation of the principle.

Key Terms
صحة التسمية (sihhat al-tasmiyah): The validity of naming the compensation; if the named item is not valid property, the compensation is void.
مخالفة (mukhalafah): Violation of the wife's request; here, divorcing three times when she asked for one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Three divorces fall, she owes one thousand.
B) Only one divorce falls, she owes one thousand.
C) Three divorces fall, she owes nothing.
D) No divorce falls because of violation.

Key Takeaway
A divorce with invalid mal or violation of request is effective without compensation.

The Principle of Khiyar in Khul': A Transaction for Her, an Oath for Him
Principle of khiyar in khul' with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits khiyar al-shart for the wife in khul' but not for the husband, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
Khul' is a transaction for the wife but an oath for the husband; thus khiyar applies to her but not to him.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a key principle: in khul' and divorce on payment, the wife's position is that of a contracting party in a financial exchange, while the husband's pronouncement is like an oath that takes immediate effect. This dual nature explains why the condition of option (khiyar al-shart) is valid when stipulated by the wife, but invalid when stipulated by the husband. The commentator also presents the disagreement of the Sahibayn and affirms the Imam's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State that the ruling is: khiyar al-shart is valid for the wife but not for the husband in khul' and divorce on payment.
2
Understand the ta'lil (legal reasoning)
The text gives two reasons: from her side it is a transaction (mu'awada), so contract rules apply, including option conditions. From his side it is an oath (yamin), which cannot be conditioned.
Consider the fundamental difference between contracts and oaths in usul al-fiqh.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Sahibayn also forbid khiyar from the wife's side, arguing the oath aspect predominates. The commentator sides with Abu Hanifa.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator declares 'al-Haqq ma qalahu al-Imam' (the truth is what the Imam said). The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
This tarjih is based on the stronger analogy (qiyas) to financial transactions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصح خيار الشرط لها لا له لما قدمنا أنه معاوضة من جهتها ويمين من جهته ولذا صح رجوعها قبل القبول ولا تصح إضافتها وتعليقها بالشرط ولا يتوقف على ما وراء المجلس وانعكست الأحكام من جانبه وهما منعاه من جانبها أيضاً نظراً إلى جانب اليمين، والحق ما قاله الإمام رضي الله تعالى عنه أطلقه فشمل الخلع والطلاق على مال ويتفرع على هذا الأصل مسائل منها ما لو قال أنت طالق على ألف على أني بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فقبلت بطل الخيار ووقع الطلاق ومنها ما لو قال أنت طالق على ألف على أنك بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فقبلت إن ردت الطلاق في الأيام الثلاثة بطل الطلاق، وإن اختارت الطلاق في الأيام الثلاثة وقع
His statement: 'And the condition of option is valid for her, not for him' because we have stated that it is a transaction (mu'awada) from her side and an oath (yamin) from his side. Hence her revocation before acceptance is valid, and it (the khul') cannot be added (future tense) or suspended on a condition, and it does not depend on remaining in the session, and the rulings are reversed from his side. The two (Sahibayn) prohibited it from her side as well, considering the aspect of oath. The truth is what Imam (Abu Hanifa) said, and he made it general to include khul' and divorce on payment. Branches from this principle: among them, if he said 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepted, the option is void and divorce falls. And among them, if he said 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have the option for three days' and she accepted, if she rejects the divorce within the three days, the divorce is void, and if she chooses the divorce within the three days, it falls.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage explains the legal nature of khul' and divorce on payment (talaq bil-mal). It establishes that from the wife's side, it is a transaction (mu'awada) – a financial exchange – so rules of contracts apply, e.g., she can revoke her offer before acceptance, and the condition of option (khiyar al-shart) is valid for her. From the husband's side, it is an oath (yamin) – a unilateral divorce – so he cannot attach a condition of option for himself; the divorce is immediate upon his pronouncement. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also prohibit khiyar from the wife's side, arguing that the oath aspect predominates. The commentator sides with Abu Hanifa. Two branches are given: (1) If the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have an option for three days,' and she accepts, the option is void and the divorce falls immediately because he cannot have option. (2) If the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have an option for three days,' and she accepts, then within three days she can reject (and void the divorce) or choose (and confirm the divorce). This shows the application of khiyar from her side.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a contract allowing a party to rescind within a specified period.
معاوضة (mu'awadah): A transaction involving exchange of values; from wife's side khul' is a financial deal.
يمين (yamin): Oath; the husband's divorce is considered like an oath that takes effect immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is khiyar al-shart valid for the wife?
A) Because khul' is a form of transaction (mu'awada) from her side.
B) Because the husband's divorce is an oath (yamin).
C) Because the Sahibayn permitted it.
D) Because the wife has the right to revoke her offer before acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, khiyar al-shart in khul' and divorce on payment is valid for the wife because it is a transaction from her side, but invalid for the husband because it is an oath from his side.

Branches (Furu') of Khiyar in Divorce on Payment
Applied branches (furu') of khiyar in divorce on payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of khiyar in divorce on payment to the two scenarios: when the husband stipulates an option and when the wife stipulates an option, and determine the correct outcome.

Core Idea
The husband's option is void and divorce is immediate; the wife's option is valid, giving her the right to reject or accept within the period.

This lesson focuses on two concrete examples from the text that illustrate the principle of khiyar in khul' and divorce on payment. The first example shows the consequence when the husband tries to reserve an option for himself; the second shows how the wife's option works in practice. These furu' reinforce the distinction between the transaction side and the oath side.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage gives two scenarios: (1) husband says 'You are divorced for 1000 on condition that I have an option for 3 days'; (2) husband says 'You are divorced for 1000 on condition that you have an option for 3 days'.
2
Analyze case 1: husband's option
Since khiyar is invalid for the husband, his stipulation is void. The divorce takes effect immediately upon her acceptance.
The rule: 'batal al-khiyar wa waqa' al-talaq'.
3
Analyze case 2: wife's option
Since khiyar is valid for the wife, she has a binding option. She can choose to reject the divorce during the three days (voiding it) or accept it (confirming it).
The rule: 'in raddat al-talaq fi al-ayam al-thalathah batal al-talaq'.
4
Summarize the practical difference
The key is whose side the option is on. The thamarah (result) depends on identifying whether the stipulator is the wife or the husband.
The furu' confirm the principle of mu'awada vs yamin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

His statement: 'And the condition of option is valid for her, not for him' because we have stated that it is a transaction (mu'awada) from her side and an oath (yamin) from his side. Hence her revocation before acceptance is valid, and it (the khul') cannot be added (future tense) or suspended on a condition, and it does not depend on remaining in the session, and the rulings are reversed from his side. The two (Sahibayn) prohibited it from her side as well, considering the aspect of oath. The truth is what Imam (Abu Hanifa) said, and he made it general to include khul' and divorce on payment. Branches from this principle: among them, if he said 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepted, the option is void and divorce falls. And among them, if he said 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have the option for three days' and she accepted, if she rejects the divorce within the three days, the divorce is void, and if she chooses the divorce within the three days, it falls.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage explains the legal nature of khul' and divorce on payment (talaq bil-mal). It establishes that from the wife's side, it is a transaction (mu'awada) – a financial exchange – so rules of contracts apply, e.g., she can revoke her offer before acceptance, and the condition of option (khiyar al-shart) is valid for her. From the husband's side, it is an oath (yamin) – a unilateral divorce – so he cannot attach a condition of option for himself; the divorce is immediate upon his pronouncement. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) also prohibit khiyar from the wife's side, arguing that the oath aspect predominates. The commentator sides with Abu Hanifa. Two branches are given: (1) If the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have an option for three days,' and she accepts, the option is void and the divorce falls immediately because he cannot have option. (2) If the husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have an option for three days,' and she accepts, then within three days she can reject (and void the divorce) or choose (and confirm the divorce). This shows the application of khiyar from her side.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option in a contract allowing a party to rescind within a specified period.
معاوضة (mu'awadah): A transaction involving exchange of values; from wife's side khul' is a financial deal.
يمين (yamin): Oath; the husband's divorce is considered like an oath that takes effect immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second scenario (wife has option), if she rejects the divorce within three days, what happens?
A) The divorce is confirmed.
B) The divorce is void.
C) The option extends for another three days.
D) The husband can revoke.

Key Takeaway
In khul' and divorce on payment, the husband's option condition is void, while the wife's option is valid, allowing her to reject or accept the divorce within the stipulated period.

Talaq — Divorce

Khiyar al-Shart in Khul': Validity and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary expanding on the validity of stipulating option in khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-shart in khul', distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to branch cases.

Core Idea
Khul' is compensation from the wife and an oath from the husband; thus option is valid for her but null for him.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the stipulation of an option (khiyar al-shart) in khul' divorce. The commentator explains the foundational principle: khul' is a mu'awada (exchange contract) from the wife's side and a yamin (oath/divorce) from the husband's side. This dual nature determines the validity of the option. We will explore the core ruling, the disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and several derived cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling from the matn
The matn states: 'صح خيار الشرط لها لا له' — the stipulation of option is valid for the wife, not for the husband. Confirm this as the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
2
Understand the rationale: mu'awada vs. yamin
Khul' is a compensation from the wife (she pays to be free), so option is valid for her as in sale. From the husband, it is a divorce (yamin), which does not admit option. This justifies the asymmetry.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare Abu Hanifa's view (option prevents immediate divorce) with the Sahibayn's (option void, divorce immediate). Identify their proofs: Abu Hanifa analogizes to sale (option suspends contract); Sahibayn say khul' does not admit annulment.
4
Apply to the first branch case
Case: Husband says 'You are divorced for 1000 on condition I have option for 3 days.' According to Abu Hanifa, his option is void, divorce occurs immediately. Apply the principle.
5
Apply to the second branch case
Case: Husband gives option to wife for 3 days. If she rejects within 3 days, divorce is void (Abu Hanifa). If she accepts, divorce occurs. Note the practical difference from Sahibayn.

خذه واعمل به في البز للإنشائية فلا تتقيد المضاربة به ولو نوى واتفقوا على احتمال الأمرين في أنت طالق وأنت مريضة أو مصلية لأنه لا مانع من كل منهما ولا معين فيتنجز الطلاق قضاء ويتعلق ديانة إن أراده فالضابط الاعتبار بالصلاحية وعدمها فإن تعين معنى الحال تقيد وإلا فإن احتمل فالمعين النية وإلا كانت لعطف الجملة؛ كذا في التحرير والبديع . وعلى هذا الخلاف لو قالت طلقني ولك ألف أو اخلعني ولك ألف ففعل فعنده وقع ولم يجب المال. وقالا : يجب المال ؛ كذا في الكافي. وفي المحيط : لو قالت طلقني ولك ألف فقال طلقتك على الألف التي سميتها إن قبلت يقع الطلاق ويجب المال، وإن لم تقبل لا يقع الطلاق ولم يجب عنده لأنها التمست طلاقاً بغير عوض لأن قولها ولك ألف» لم يكن تعويضاً على الطلاق فقد أعرض الزوج عما التمست حيث أوقع طلاقاً تعوض، فإن قبلت وقع وإلا بطل. وعندهما يقع ويجب المال ا هـ . ثم اعلم أن الوقوع مجاناً مع ذكر المال لا يختص بمسألة الكتاب بل يكون في مسائل أخرى منها لو قال أنت طالق على عبدي هذا فإذا هو حر طلقت مجاناً لعدم صحة التسمية، وأوجب عليها زفر قيمته قياساً على تسمية عبد الغير، وفرقنا بإمكان تسليمه بإجازة مالكه في المقيس عليه وفي المقيس لا يتصور تسليمه. ومنها لو قالت طلقني واحدة بألف أو على ألف فطلقها ثلاثاً ولم يذكر الألف طلقت ثلاثاً مجاناً عنده للمخالفة، وعندهما طلقت ثلاثاً وعليها الألف بإزاء الواحدة لأنه مجيب بالواحدة مبتدئاً بالباقي، وإن ذكر الألف لا يقع شيء عنده ما لم تقبل المرأة، وإذا قبلت الكل وقع الثلاث بالألف، وعندهما إن لم تقبل فهي طالق واحدة فقط، وإن قبلت طلقت ثلاثاً واحدة بألف وثنتان بغير شيء؛ كذا في الكافي.

قوله : (وإذا أطلقا ينبغي أن يكون لها الخيار الخ قال في النهر : وعندي فيه نظر لاقتضائه أن يقبل النقض بعد التمام والظاهر أنه لا يقبله بدليل أنه لا يجري التقايل فيه بخلاف البيع وهذا كما سيأتي في البيع من أن ثبوته عند الإطلاق مقيد بما إذا قال له البائع ذلك بعد البيع، أما عند العقد فيفسد البيع عند الإمام والفرق بينهما سيأتي في البيع إن شاء الله تعالى .
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Khul'. The condition (of option) is for her, not for him: 'I divorced you yesterday for one thousand and you did not accept, then she said: I accept.' He is believed, unlike sale. And it falls. Take it and act upon it in [the context of] inceptive sentences, so the partnership is not restricted by it, even if he intended. And they agreed on the possibility of two things in 'You are divorced while you are sick or praying' because there is no prevention from either and no specification, so the divorce takes effect judicially, and it pertains religiously if he intended it. The principle is consideration of suitability and its absence; if the meaning of the situation is determined, it is conditioned; otherwise if it is possible, then the intention determines; otherwise it is for conjunction of sentences. Thus in al-Tahrir and al-Badi'. And upon this difference of opinion, if she said: 'Divorce me and you have one thousand' or 'Divorce me for compensation and you have one thousand' and he did so, then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it occurs and the money is not obligatory. And they both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: The money is obligatory. Thus in al-Kafi. And in al-Muhit: If she said: 'Divorce me and you have one thousand' and he said: 'I divorce you for the one thousand you mentioned, if you accept', then the divorce occurs and the money is obligatory; if she does not accept, the divorce does not occur and the money is not obligatory according to him because she requested a divorce without compensation, since her statement 'and you have one thousand' was not a compensation for the divorce; so the husband turned away from what she requested by effecting a divorce with compensation. If she accepts, it occurs; otherwise it is void. And according to them both, the divorce occurs and the money is obligatory. End. Then know that occurrence gratuitously with mention of money is not specific to the issue of the book, but occurs in other issues: among them, if he said: 'You are divorced for this slave of mine' and it turns out to be free, she is divorced gratuitously because the specification is invalid; Zufar obligated its value by analogy to specifying a slave belonging to another, and we differentiated by the possibility of delivery by the owner's permission in the analogized case, while in the analogized-from case delivery is inconceivable. Among them, if she said: 'Divorce me once for one thousand' or 'for one thousand' and he divorced her three times without mentioning the thousand, she is divorced three times gratuitously according to him due to the violation; according to them both she is divorced three times and she owes the thousand for the one (divorce) because he responded with one and initiated the rest. If he mentioned the thousand, nothing occurs according to him until she accepts; if she accepts all, the three occur for the thousand; according to them both, if she does not accept, she is divorced only once, and if she accepts, she is divorced three times: one for a thousand and two for nothing. Thus in al-Kafi. 'She accepted'? Statement (of the author): 'And the stipulation of option for her, not for him, is valid' because we have mentioned that it is a compensation from her side and an oath from his side, so her revocation before acceptance is valid, and its addition and suspension by condition are not valid, and it does not depend on the [continuation of the] session beyond, and the rulings are reversed from his side, and they both prevent it from her side as well, considering the oath side, and the truth is what Imam (Abu Hanifa) said, may Allah be pleased with him. He made it absolute, so it includes khul' and divorce for money. And from this principle branch issues: among them, if he said: 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepted, the option becomes void and the divorce occurs. Among them, if he said: 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have the option for three days' and she accepted: if she rejects the divorce within the three days, the divorce becomes void; if she chooses the divorce within the three days, it occurs and the thousand is obligatory for him. According to them both, the divorce occurs in both cases and the money is incumbent on her, and the option is void in both cases. Thus in al-Kafi and others. And in Fatawa Qadikhan from the chapter of coercion: If a man said to his wife: 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that you have the option for three days' and she accepted, the divorce occurs and she has the option according to the statement of Abu Hanifa. This is problematic, and apparently it is a slip of the pen, because the divorce does not occur before dropping the option, either by consent or by passage of time, not that it occurs and then is revoked by the option. For this reason it is stated in al-Bada'i': Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say in the issue of option that the option is only legislated for annulment, and khul' does not admit annulment. Abu Hanifa's response to this is that the place of option is in preventing the contract from being concluded with respect to the ruling according to our school's principle, so the contract was not concluded with respect to the ruling for now, but rather suspended until the time the option falls; then it operates as known in sales. End. If you say: Is it valid to stipulate option for her after khul'? I say: I have not seen it explicitly, and the implication of treating it like sale is that it would be valid, because stipulating a subsequent option after sale has issues, since the divorce has occurred where it was without condition, so how can it be raised after its occurrence? Like the concurrent option. And he made the duration absolute, so it includes stipulating it for her more than three days according to him. The distinction for the Imam between it and sale is that stipulating it in sale is contrary to analogy because sale is a category of transfers, so it is confined to the textual basis; while in khul', it is in accordance with analogy because khul' is a category of relinquishments, and the money, although intended with respect to the contracting party, is subsidiary in establishment to the divorce which is the purpose of the contract, just as the price is subsidiary in sale. And with respect to the purpose, it follows that it should not be restricted to three. Thus in al-Kashf from the end of the discussion of jest. Accordingly, if they specify a time and it passes, the option becomes void, whether it is three or more, and the divorce occurs and the money becomes obligatory. If they leave it unspecified, it should be that she has the option only in her session; if she leaves it, it becomes void, deduced from when they leave it unspecified in sale, because it has a resemblance to sale. And the commentator mentioned that the side of the slave in emancipation is like the side of the woman in divorce, so stipulating option for him is valid but not for the master. Then know that they have transmitted here that there is no suspension (ta'liq) for her in khul' because it is valid as a compensation from her side. Al-Hakim mentioned in al-Kafi that if she said: 'If you divorce me three times, then you have one thousand upon me', then if he accepts in the session, he has the thousand; if he accepts afterwards, he has nothing. And al-Fath al-Qadir attributed it to him and did not comment, despite it being a suspension from her with an explicit condition. And the apparent meaning of their absolute statement is that there is no difference, whether the acceptance or offer is suspended. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He divorced her for compensation and she said: 'If I do not pay the consideration within four days, the khul' is void', then the time passed and she did not pay. This is like a stipulation of option in khul', and it is subject to the difference of opinion if it is from... between. Statement (of the author): 'And if they leave it unspecified, it should be that she has the option, etc.' Al-Nahr said: In my view there is consideration in this, because it would imply that it accepts annulment after completion, and apparently it does not accept it, as evidenced by the fact that no mutual revocation (taqayul) occurs in it, unlike sale. This is as will come in sale: that its establishment when left unspecified is restricted to when the seller says that after the sale. As for at the time of contract, it invalidates the sale according to Imam. The difference between them will come in sale, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion probe on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the validity of stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) in khul' divorce. The commentator explains the core principle: khul' is a compensation from the wife's perspective (she pays to be free) and an oath/divorce from the husband's perspective. Therefore, the option is valid for the wife (she can decide whether to accept the terms) but not for the husband (since his side is like an oath, which does not admit option). This leads to several branch rulings: (1) If the husband says 'I divorce you for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepts, the option is void and divorce occurs immediately; (2) If the condition is for the wife (she has the option), then she can choose to reject or accept the divorce within the period. According to Abu Hanifa, if she rejects, the divorce does not occur; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the divorce is immediate and the option is void. The commentator then discusses the 'alif vs. lam' issue in 'टिकني ولك अल्फ' and other cases where divorce occurs without compensation despite mentioning money. The passage also addresses the question of stipulating option after the khul' contract (post-formation) and the analogy to sale, noting differences because khul' is a relinquishment (isqat) rather than a transfer (tamlik). Finally, it touches on suspension (ta'liq) in khul' and cites various sources like al-Kafi, al-Muhit, and Fatawa Qadikhan.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated option that allows one party to annul or confirm a contract within a specified period.
خلع (khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually money) paid to the husband.
معاوضة (mu'awada): A contract of exchange where each party gives something in return for another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens if the husband says to his wife, 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition that I have the option for three days' and she accepts?
A) The option is valid and the divorce does not occur until the period ends.
B) The option is void and the divorce occurs immediately with the thousand obligatory.
C) The divorce occurs but she has the option to annul it.
D) The divorce does not occur at all because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
Khiyar al-shart in khul' is valid for the wife (as mu'awada) but not for the husband (as yamin); this asymmetry is unique to the Hanafi school's dual characterization of khul'.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Dispute over Khiyar (Option) in Khul': Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Analysis of an intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding khiyar in khul', explain the reasoning behind each view, and apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
In khul', Abu Hanifa allows khiyar to suspend the divorce; the Sahibayn reject khiyar because khul' is not revocable.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: may a husband stipulate an option period in a khul' contract? The answer reveals deep differences in how Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples conceptualize khul'—as a contract analogous to sale (mu'awada) or as an irrevocable forfeiture (isqat). Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to parse Hanafi rulings on suspended contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband says 'You are divorced for 1000 on condition you have the option for 3 days.' The wife accepts. This is the case under dispute.
The scenario is from Fatawa Qadikhan, chapter on coercion.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa: The divorce is suspended until the option is dropped; no immediate talaq takes effect.
The divorce only occurs when the option falls away (by acceptance or expiry).
3
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: The divorce occurs immediately, and the option is invalid because khul' does not admit revocation (faskh).
Khiyar is only legislated for faskh, and khul' cannot be revoked.
4
Compare the dalil
Abu Hanifa analogizes to sale (qiyas): just as khiyar suspends a sale contract, so too in khul'. The Sahibayn counter that the analogy fails because khiyar is for revocation, and khul' is an isqat (forfeiture) that cannot be undone.
The core difference is how each party defines the nature of khul'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى قاضيخان من باب الإكراه : لو قال لامرأته أنت طالق على ألف على إنك بالخيار ثلاثة أيام فقبلت يقع الطلاق ولها الخيار في قول أبي حنيفة. وهو مشكل والظاهر أنه سبق قلم فإن الطلاق لا يقع قبل إسقاط الخيار عند أبي حنيفة بالرضا أو بمضي المدة لا أنه وقع ثم يرتفع بالفسخ بالخيار ولذا قال في البدائع: إن أبا يوسف ومحمداً يقولان في مسألة الخيار إن الخيار إنما شرع للفسخ والخلع لا يحتمل الفسخ . وجواب أبي حنيفة عن هذا أن محل الخيار في منع انعقاد العقد في حق الحكم على أصل أصحابنا فلم يكن العقد منعقداً في حق الحكم للحال بل موقوف إلى وقت سقوط الخيار فحينئذ يعمل على ما عرف في البيوع ا.هـ.
And in Fatawa Qadikhan from the chapter on coercion: If a man said to his wife, 'You are divorced for one thousand on the condition that you have the option for three days', and she accepted, the divorce occurs and she has the option according to Abu Hanifa. This is problematic, and apparently it is a slip of the pen, for divorce does not occur before the option is dropped, according to Abu Hanifa, either by acceptance or by expiry of the term; it is not that it occurs and then is annulled by revocation through the option. For this reason, he said in al-Bada'i': Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say concerning the issue of option that the option is only legislated for revocation, and khul' does not admit revocation. Abu Hanifa's response to this is that the place of the option is in preventing the conclusion of the contract in terms of legal effect according to the principle of our companions; so the contract is not concluded in terms of legal effect at present, but rather suspended until the time the option falls away, then it operates according to what is known in sales.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of stipulating a khiyar (option) in a khul' contract. The scenario: a husband says 'You are divorced for one thousand on condition you have the option for three days.' The wife accepts. According to Abu Hanifa, the divorce does not take effect immediately; it is suspended until the option is resolved—either by the wife's acceptance (dropping the option) or by expiry of the term. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the divorce occurs immediately and the dower is obligatory, but the option is invalid because khul' does not admit of revocation (faskh). They argue that khiyar is only for revocation, and khul' is not revocable. Abu Hanifa responds by explaining that, on his view, the khiyar prevents the contract from being legally concluded at the moment; it is suspended (mawquf) until the option falls away, at which point the contract takes effect. He analogizes this to the rule in sales, where a khiyar can suspend the contract. This illustrates a difference in principle: Abu Hanifa treats khul' as analogous to sale in certain aspects, while the Sahibayn emphasize the distinct nature of khul' as an isqat (forfeiture) that cannot be undone.

Key Terms
الخيار (al-khiyar): The option or right to rescind a contract within a specified period.
الخلع (al-khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually monetary) paid to the husband.
الفسخ (al-faskh): Revocation or annulment of a contract, undoing it from its inception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to the divorce when a khiyar (option) is stipulated in khul'?
A) The divorce occurs immediately and the option is invalid.
B) The divorce is suspended until the option is dropped, then it takes effect.
C) The divorce occurs but can be revoked if the option is exercised.
D) The divorce does not occur at all.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa treats khul' as a mu'awada contract analogous to sale, allowing khiyar to suspend legal effect, while the Sahibayn treat khul' as an isqat that cannot be deferred.

Duration of Khiyar in Khul' and Its Distinction from Sale
Explaining the duration of khiyar in khul' and its distinction from sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of khiyar in khul' and explain the talil (rationale) that distinguishes it from sale.

Core Idea
Khiyar in khul' is not limited to three days because khul' is an isqat, not a tamlik – the nature of the contract governs the option's duration.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the duration of khiyar (option) in khul' and its justification. It distinguishes between isqatat (forfeitures) and tamlikat (transfers), using this distinction to explain why the three-day limit on khiyar in sale does not apply to khul'. The passage also clarifies which types of khiyar are valid in khul' and discusses conditional khul' (ta'liq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its condition
The passage addresses the validity of stipulating a khiyar for the wife after khul'. It states that according to Abu Hanifa, the duration is not limited to three days. First, identify that the ruling is about when a time is specified versus when it is left unspecified.
2
Locate the dalil (talil) – the reason
The author cites the distinction between isqat (forfeiture) and tamlik (transfer). In sale (tamlik), khiyar is an exception restricted to textual proof; in khul' (isqat), khiyar is in accordance with analogy (qiyas) and thus not restricted.
3
Apply the distinction to the duration
If the parties specify a time (e.g., five days), the option ends when that time expires, regardless of it being more than three. If no time is specified, the option lasts only for the session (majlis); standing up nullifies it.
4
Note the types of khiyar applicable in khul'
Only khiyar al-shart (stipulated option) is allowed. Khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight) is not valid because khul' does not permit revocation. Khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) applies only for major defects in the compensation.
5
Understand the ta'liq (suspension) example
The passage cites a case where the wife says, 'If you divorce me thrice, I owe you one thousand.' If the husband accepts in the session, he deserves the payment; if after, he gets nothing. This shows that conditional khul' is valid and functions like an option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت هل يصح اشتراط الخيار لها بعد الخلع؟ قلت: لم أره صريحاً ومقتضى جعله كالبيع أن يصح لأن شرط الخيار اللاحق بعد البيع أن فيه اشكالاً لأن الطلاق وقع حيث كان بلا شرط فكيف يرتفع بعد وقوعه؟ كالمقارن وأطلق في المدة فشمل اشتراطه لها أكثر من ثلاثة عنده والفرق للإمام بينه وبين البيع أن اشتراطه في البيع على خلاف القياس لأنه من التمليكات فيقتصر على مورد النص، وفي الخلع على وفقه لأنه من الإسقاطات والمال وإن كان مقصوداً فيه بالنظر إلى العاقد لكنه تابع في الثبوت في الطلاق الذي هو مقصود العقد كما أن الثمن تابع في البيع وبالنظر إلى المقصود يلزم أن لا يتقدر بالثلاث؛ كذا في الكشف من آخر بحث الهزل، فعلى هذا إذا قدرا وقتاً ومضى بطل الخيار سواء كان ثلاثة أو أكثر ووقع الطلاق ولزم المال، وإذا أطلقا ينبغي أن يكون لها الخيار في مجلسها فقط، فإن قامت منه بطل استنباطاً مما إذا أطلقا في البيع لما أنه له شبه البيع. وذكر الشارح أن جانب العبد في العتاق مثل جانب المرأة في الطلاق حتى صح اشتراط الخيار له دون المولى. ثم اعلم أنهم نقلوا هنا أنه لا تعليقها للخلع لكونه يصح معاوضة من جهتها، وقد ذكر الحاكم في الكافي أنها لو قالت إن طلقتني ثلاثاً فلك علي ألف ، فإن قبل في المجلس فله الألف وإن قبل بعده فلا شيء له. وعزاه إليه في فتح القدير ولم يتعقبه مع أنه تعليق منها له بصريح الشرط. وظاهر إطلاقهم أنه لا أن فرق يعلق القبول أو الإيجاب. وفي البزازية : خالعها وقالت إن لم أؤد البدل إلى أربعة أيام فالخلع باطل فمضت المدة ولم تؤد فهذه بمنزلة شرط الخيار في الخلع وأنه على الخلاف إذا كان من جانبه ا هـ. يعني إذا مضت المدة قبل الأداء بطل الخلع وإن أدت في المدة وقع كمسألة العقد في البيع، واستفيد منه أن الخيار لا يتقيد بالثلاث كما قدمناه صريحاً. وقيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار الرؤية لا يثبت في الخلع ولا في كل عقد لا يحتمل الفسخ كما ذكره العمادي في فصوله، وأما خيار العيب في بدل الخلع فثابت في العيب الفاحش دون اليسير والفاحش ما يخرجه من الجودة إلى الوساطة ومن الوساطة إلى الرداءة ا وفي جامع الفصولين: الأصل أن من له الرجوع عن خطابه قولاً يبطل خطابه بقيامه ومن لا رجوع له لا يبطل بقيامه ثم قال : والحاصل أن الخلع من جانبه يبطل بقيامها لا بقيامه ومن جانبها يبطل بقيام كل منهما ا هـ .
If you say: Is it valid to stipulate the option for her after the khul'? I say: I have not seen it explicitly, and the implication of making it like sale is that it is valid, because stipulating an option after the sale has occurred is problematic, because the divorce has occurred when it was without condition, so how can it be annulled after its occurrence? Like the concurrent [option]. And he gave an unqualified period, so it includes stipulating it for more than three according to him, and the difference for the Imam between it and sale is that stipulating it in sale is against analogy because it is from the transfers (tamlikat), so it is restricted to the textual proof, while in khul' it is in accordance with analogy because it is from the forfeitures (isqatat), and wealth, even if it is intended with respect to the contracting party, is subordinate in establishing the divorce which is the object of the contract, just as the price is subordinate in sale. With respect to the object, it follows that it is not limited to three. Thus in al-Kashf from the end of the discussion of jest. So on this, if they specify a time and it passes, the option becomes void whether it is three or more, the divorce occurs and the wealth is due. If they are unqualified, it is appropriate that she has the option only in the session; if she stands from it, it becomes void, deduced from what if they are unqualified in sale, since it has a resemblance to sale. And the commentator mentioned that the side of the slave in manumission is like the side of the woman in divorce, so that stipulating the option for him is valid, but not for the master. Then know that they transmitted here that there is no suspension (ta'liq) of her in khul' because it is valid as a consideration from her side. And al-Hakim mentioned in al-Kafi that if she said, 'If you divorce me three times, then I owe you one thousand,' then if he accepted in the session, he gets the thousand; if he accepted thereafter, he gets nothing. And he attributed it to him in Fath al-Qadir and did not critique it, even though it is a suspension from her by explicit condition. And the apparent meaning of their unqualified statement is that there is no difference whether the acceptance or the offer is suspended. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He made khul' with her and she said, 'If I do not pay the compensation within four days, then the khul' is void,' so the period passed and she did not pay—this is like a condition of option in khul' and that it is subject to the difference if it is from his side. Meaning: if the period passes before payment, the khul' becomes void; if she pays within the period, it takes effect, like the issue of the contract in sale. And it is understood from this that the option is not limited to three, as we have stated explicitly. And it is restricted to khiyar al-shart because khiyar al-ru'yah is not established in khul' nor in any contract that does not admit revocation, as mentioned by al-'Imadi in his Fusul. As for khiyar al-'ayb in the compensation of khul', it is established for major defects, not minor; and major is that which takes it from quality to mediocrity and from mediocrity to badness. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The principle is that whoever has the right to retract his statement verbally, his statement is nullified by his standing; whoever has no right to retract, it is not nullified by his standing. Then he said: The summary is that khul' from his side is nullified by her standing, not by his standing, and from her side it is nullified by the standing of each of them.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage addresses several issues related to khiyar (option) in khul'. First, it asks whether it is valid to stipulate a khiyar after the khul' contract (a later option). The answer is that it is problematic because divorce, once occurred without condition, cannot be undone. The text then explains that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the duration of khiyar in khul' is not limited to three days, unlike in sale. The reason is the fundamental difference: sale is a tamlik (transfer of ownership), so khiyar in sale is an exception to the general rule and is thus restricted to the texts; khul' is an isqat (forfeiture), so khiyar is in accordance with analogy and is not restricted. Although wealth (the compensation) is intended, it is subordinate to the divorce, which is the main object. Therefore, if the parties specify a time for the khiyar, and that time expires, the option is void and the divorce takes effect regardless of whether the time is three days or more. If they do not specify a time, the wife has the option only within the session (majlis); if she stands, the option is void. This is deduced from the rule in sale when nothing is specified. The text also compares the slave's side in manumission with the wife's side in khul', allowing the stipulation of option for the slave but not for the master. The passage then discusses ta'liq (suspension) of khul' by the wife, citing al-Kafi that if the wife says 'If you divorce me three times, I owe you one thousand' and the husband accepts in the session, he gets the thousand; if he accepts later, he gets nothing. This is treated as a valid conditional khul', akin to an option condition. The text also notes the types of khiyar: khiyar al-shart (stipulated option) is allowed, but khiyar al-ru'yah (option of sight) does not apply in khul' because khul' does not admit revocation. Khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) applies only for major defects in the compensation. Finally, the Jami' al-Fusulayn cites a principle: the right to retract a statement is nullified by standing up if one has the right to retract; otherwise not. In khul', from the husband's side, the contract is nullified if she stands away; from the wife's side, it is nullified if either party stands away (since she can retract her offer until acceptance).

Key Terms
الإسقاطات (al-isqatat): Legal acts that forfeit or relinquish a right, such as divorce (which forfeits marital rights) and manumission.
التمليكات (al-tamlikat): Legal acts that transfer ownership, such as sale.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'yah): The option of sight, allowing a buyer to rescind a sale after seeing the object if it was not previously seen.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum duration of a stipulated khiyar in khul' if not specified?
A) Three days
B) The duration of the session (majlis) only
C) Unlimited, until the option is explicitly dropped
D) One day

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the duration of khiyar in khul' is not bound by the three-day limit because khul' is an isqat; the wife's option is intended to protect her from inequity.
