Past-Tense Divorce on Compensation: Husband's Word Accepted vs. Sale
Ruling with proof: husband believed in past khul' dispute, contrasted with sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school accepts the husband's claim in a past-tense khul' dispute and distinguish it from a sale contract using the concept of 'aqd yamin.

Core Idea
Divorce on compensation is a contract of oath, complete without acceptance; sale requires acceptance.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common dispute: a husband claims he divorced his wife yesterday for a sum, but she did not accept; the wife says she accepted. Who is believed? The Hanafi ruling may surprise you, especially in contrast to a sale contract. The key distinction lies in the nature of the contract: divorce on compensation ('khul') is a 'contract of oath' that is complete even without the wife's acceptance, while a sale is incomplete without the buyer's acceptance. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the husband's claim that he divorced his wife yesterday for a specified sum and she did not accept. The ruling: the husband is believed (with his oath).
The wife's denial does not overturn the divorce.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a qiyas (analogy) contrasting khul' with sale. The distinguishing feature is that khul' is a contract of oath (yamīn) complete without acceptance, while sale requires acceptance.
The dalil is aqli (reason-based) not naqli.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Because khul' is complete without acceptance, the husband's admission of the khul' does not imply the wife's acceptance. In sale, admission implies acceptance by the buyer, so a subsequent denial is contradictory.
Thus the husband's claim is consistent; the wife's contradictory claim is not given weight.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may treat the husband's admission as implying acceptance, giving the wife's statement more weight. The Hanafi position is based on the unilateral nature of divorce.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is adopted because it aligns with the nature of divorce as a unilateral act effective by itself. It is the mufta bihi.
Supported by al-'Imadi in al-Fusul and Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( طلقتك أمس بألف فلم تقبلي وقالت قبلت صدق بخلاف البيع والفرق أن الطلاق على مال بلا قبول عقد تام وهو عقد يمين فلا يكون إقراره به اقراراً بقبول المرأة، أما البيع بلا قبول المشتري فليس ببيع فكان إقراره به اقراراً بقبول المشتري، فدعواه بعده عدم قبول تناقض ومراده من تصديق الزوج قبول قوله مع يمينه كما نص عليه العمادي في الفصول، ولو قيد المسألة بالمال كما في الهداية لكان أولى ولولا ما ذكره المصنف في الكافي شرحاً لقوله بخلاف البيع من أن صورته ما لو قال لغيره بعت منك هذا العبد بألف درهم أمس فلم تقبل وقال المشتري قبلت إلى آخره لشرحت قوله بخلاف البيع بما لو قال بعتك طلاقك أمس فلم تقبلي فقالت بل ،قبلت، فقد نص في فتح القدير أن القبول لها لمناسبته للطلاق وفيه : ولو قال لعبده أعتقك أمس على ألف فلم تقبل وبعتك أمس نفسك منك بألف فلم تقبل على قياس قول الزوج لها اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : لو أقاما بينة أخذ ببينة المرأة ا هـ . وفي البزازية : ادى الخلع على حالها والمرأة تنكر يقع الطلاق بإقراره والدعوى في المال على حالها وعكسه لا يقع كـ ما كان ادعت المهر أو نفقة العدة، لأنه طلقها وادعى الخلع وليس لها بينة ففي حق المهر القول لها وفي النفقة قوله ا هـ . وينبغي حمله على ما إذا كان مدعياً أن من جملة بدل الخلع وعلى تقديره فالفرق أن المهر كان ثابتاً عليه قبله فدعواه سقوطه غير مقبول، وأما نفقة العدة فليست واجبة قبله وهي تدعي استحقاقها بالطلاق وهو ينكر فكان القول له وهو مشكل فإنهما اتفقا على سبب استحقاقها لأن الخلع والطلاق يوجبان نفقة العدة فكيف تسقط؟ وفي جامع الفصولين : اختلفا في كمية الخلع فقال مرتان وقالت ثلاث قيل القول له، وقيل لو اختلفا بعد التزوج فقالت لم يجز التزوج لأنه وقع بعد الخلع الثالث نفقة العدة قوله : (ولو قيد المسألة بالمال الخ قال الرملي : النسخة التي شرح عليها الزيلعي والعيني ومنلا مسكين مقيدة بالمال فإن عبارتهم طلقتك أمس بألف اهـ . قلت : وكذلك عبارة النهر قوله: (وهو مشكل الخ) أصل الاستشكال لصاحب جامع الفصولين .
His saying: ('I divorced you yesterday for one thousand, and you did not accept'; and she said 'I accepted'), he is believed, unlike sale. And the difference is that divorce for compensation without acceptance is a complete contract, and it is a contract of oath, so his admission of it is not an admission of the woman's acceptance. As for sale without the buyer's acceptance, it is not a sale, so his admission of it is an admission of the buyer's acceptance. Therefore, his claim afterwards that there was no acceptance is contradictory. And what is meant by the husband being believed is that his statement is accepted with his oath, as al-'Imadi stated in al-Fusul. And if he had restricted the issue to wealth as in al-Hidaya, it would have been better. And were it not for what the author mentioned in al-Kafi as commentary on his saying 'unlike sale' that its form is if a man said to another, 'I sold you this slave for one thousand dirhams yesterday and you did not accept,' and the buyer said, 'I accepted,' etc., I would have explained his saying 'unlike sale' by what if he said, 'I sold you your divorce yesterday and you did not accept,' and she said, 'Rather, I accepted.' For it is stated in Fath al-Qadir that acceptance belongs to her because of its appropriateness to divorce. And in it: If he said to his slave, 'I emancipated you yesterday for one thousand and you did not accept,' and 'I sold you yourself from you for one thousand and you did not accept,' on the analogy of the husband's statement to her. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya: If they both produce evidence, the woman's evidence is taken. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He claimed khul' with her as she is, and the woman denies; the divorce occurs by his admission, and the claim regarding wealth remains as it was. And the opposite does not occur, as if she claimed the dower or the maintenance during the 'idda, because he divorced her and claimed khul', and she has no evidence. So regarding the dower, the statement is hers; regarding maintenance, his statement. This should be interpreted as when he claims that part of the compensation includes it. On that assumption, the difference is that the dower was established against him before, so his claim that it is dropped is not accepted. As for maintenance during 'idda, it was not obligatory before him; she claims entitlement to it by the divorce, and he denies, so the statement is his. This is problematic because they agree on the cause of entitlement (the divorce), and khul' and divorce both necessitate 'idda maintenance, so how can it be dropped? And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: They differed over the amount of khul': he said twice, she said three times. It is said the statement is his. And it is said if they differed after the marriage, and she said the marriage is not valid because it occurred after the third divorce, ['idda maintenance]... His saying: ('If he had restricted the issue to wealth, etc.') al-Ramli said: The copy that al-Zayla'i, al-'Ayni, and Mulla Miskin commented on is restricted to wealth; their phrase is 'I divorced you yesterday for one thousand.' I say: Similarly is the phrase of al-Nahr. His saying ('It is problematic, etc.') is originally from the author of Jami' al-Fusulayn.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a husband says 'I divorced you yesterday for one thousand, and you did not accept,' while the wife says 'I accepted.' The ruling is that the husband is believed (with his oath), unlike in sale where the seller would not be believed. The reason: divorce on compensation without acceptance is still a complete contract (a 'contract of oath'), so the husband's admission of the divorce does not imply that the wife accepted. He can consistently claim the divorce occurred without her acceptance. In sale, the contract is incomplete without the buyer's acceptance, so the seller's admission implies acceptance by the buyer; thus, his subsequent denial is contradictory. Therefore, the husband's word is taken. The text also discusses related rulings from various sources: if both parties produce evidence, the woman's evidence is preferred (because she is the one demanding compensation). In cases where the husband claims khul' and the wife denies, the divorce still occurs due to his admission, but the financial claims differ: for the dower (mahr), the wife's claim is believed (since it was established prior); for 'idda maintenance (nafaqah), the husband's claim is believed (since she claims a new right). This is problematic because both khul' and regular divorce give the wife 'idda maintenance, so it cannot be dropped simply by the husband's denial. Finally, if they differ over the number of divorces (e.g., husband says two, wife says three), there are two views: the husband's word is taken, or if they differ after the wife remarries, the marriage may be invalid if it occurred after the third divorce. The text ends with a note that the original matn in Kanz al-Daqaiq (and the copies used by major commentators) restricts the issue to wealth (i.e., 'with one thousand'), and the problematic part is from Jami' al-Fusulayn.

Key Terms
عقد يمين (aqd yamin): A contract of oath; here meaning that divorce (even on compensation) is an act that is effective by itself, similar to an oath, and does not require the other party's acceptance to be valid.
إقرار (iqrar): Admission or confession of a fact or right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the husband believed when he says 'I divorced you yesterday for one thousand, and you did not accept,' while the wife claims she accepted?
A) Because the husband is always believed in divorce matters.
B) Because divorce on compensation is a complete contract without acceptance; his admission does not imply acceptance.
C) Because the wife's claim is not supported by evidence.
D) Because the husband is the initiator of the contract.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, divorce on compensation is a 'contract of oath' that is complete without acceptance, so the husband's word is accepted in a past-tense dispute, unlike in sale.

Types of Khiyar in Khul': Conditions and Rulings
Defines types of khiyar in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, and khiyar al-‘ayb in khul', and state the Hanafi ruling for each type.

Core Idea
In khul', only khiyar al-shart is allowed; khiyar al-ru'ya is invalid and khiyar al-‘ayb applies only for major defects.

The term khiyar (option) appears in multiple contractual contexts. In khul', the Hanafi school distinguishes between types of options. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies which khiyar are valid in khul', which are not, and under what conditions. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the rules of khul' in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three khiyar mentioned
The text discusses khiyar al-shart, khiyar al-ru'ya, and khiyar al-‘ayb. Note the ruling for each.
Khiyar al-shart is valid; khiyar al-ru'ya is invalid; khiyar al-‘ayb is valid only for major defects.
2
Understand the basis for khiyar al-shart
The passage states that khul' allows a stipulated option period, not limited to three days, similar to sale. Why is it allowed? Because the contract is analogous to sale.
The period is agreed upon by the parties.
3
Explain why khiyar al-ru'ya is excluded
The text says it does not apply to any contract that does not permit rescission (فسخ). Khul' is such a contract.
Khiyar al-ru'ya is limited to contracts that allow rescission, like sale.
4
Determine khiyar al-‘ayb application
It applies only to the compensation (badal) and only for major defects. Define major defect as change from good to medium or medium to inferior.
Minor defects do not give the right to return the compensation.
5
Apply the standing-up principle
The final part distinguishes the effect of standing up on the offer/acceptance in khul'. This relates to retraction.
The husband's offer is nullified if the wife stands up; the wife's acceptance is nullified if either stands up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خيار جانبه ا هـ. يعني إذا مضت المدة قبل الأداء بطل الخلع وإن أدت في المدة وقع كمسألة العقد في البيع، واستفيد منه أن الخيار لا يتقيد بالثلاث كما قدمناه صريحاً. وقيد بخيار الشرط لأن خيار الرؤية لا يثبت في الخلع ولا في كل عقد لا يحتمل الفسخ كما ذكره العمادي في فصوله، وأما خيار العيب في بدل الخلع فثابت في العيب الفاحش دون اليسير والفاحش ما يخرجه من الجودة إلى الوساطة ومن الوساطة إلى الرداءة ا وفي جامع الفصولين: الأصل أن من له الرجوع عن خطابه قولاً يبطل خطابه بقيامه ومن لا رجوع له لا يبطل بقيامه ثم قال : والحاصل أن الخلع من جانبه يبطل بقيامها لا بقيامه ومن جانبها يبطل بقيام كل منهما ا هـ.
His saying: 'Her option, etc.' That is, if the period passes before payment, the khul' is void, and if she pays within the period, it is effective, like the case of the option in sale. It is understood from this that the option is not restricted to three days, as we have clearly stated earlier. It is restricted to khiyar al-shart because khiyar al-ru'ya is not established in khul' nor in any contract that does not admit of rescission, as al-‘Imadi mentioned in his Fusul. As for khiyar al-‘ayb in the consideration of khul', it is established for a major defect but not a minor one. A major defect is that which removes the item from good quality to medium, or from medium to inferior. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: The principle is that whoever has the right to retract his statement verbally, his statement is invalidated by his standing up; and whoever does not have the right to retract, his statement is not invalidated by his standing up. Then he said: In summary, the khul' from his side is invalidated by her standing up but not by his standing up, and from her side it is invalidated by each of them standing up.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage opens as an expansion and explanation of the earlier text regarding khiyar (option) in khul'. The commentator clarifies that if a fixed period is set for payment of the compensation, the khul' is void if payment is not made before expiry, but if payment is made within the period, it is valid—analogous to khiyar al-shart in sale. Importantly, the option period is not limited to three days, contrary to some misconceptions. The option in khul' is specifically khiyar al-shart (stipulated option); khiyar al-ru'ya (option of inspection) does not apply because khul' is a contract that does not admit of rescission. As for khiyar al-‘ayb (option of defect), it applies only to the compensation (badal) and only if the defect is major (fahish)—defined as reducing quality from good to medium or from medium to inferior. Minor defects give no option. The passage then quotes from Jami' al-Fusulayn a general principle about standing up as a retraction: if a party has the right to retract, standing up nullifies his statement; if not, it does not. Applied to khul', the husband's offer is nullified if the wife stands up (implying rejection), but not if he stands up; the wife's acceptance is nullified if either party stands up. This distinguishes the positions of the two parties.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khiyar al-shart): A stipulated period within which either party may rescind the contract; valid in khul' per this text.
خيار الرؤية (khiyar al-ru'ya): The right to rescind a contract after seeing an unseen item; not established in khul' because it does not admit rescission.
خيار العيب (khiyar al-‘ayb): The right to return an item due to a defect; applies to the compensation in khul' only for major defects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which type of khiyar is NOT established in khul'?
A) Khiyar al-shart
B) Khiyar al-ru'ya
C) Khiyar al-‘ayb for major defects
D) Khiyar al-‘ayb for minor defects

Key Takeaway
In khul', only khiyar al-shart is valid; khiyar al-ru'ya is invalid; khiyar al-‘ayb applies only to major defects in the compensation.

Dispute Over Acceptance in Khul' Compared to Sale
Comparing the ruling when husband claims divorce without acceptance, distinguishing khul' from sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the husband's denial of acceptance in khul' and explain why it differs from the sale case using the distinction between a contract of oath and a bilateral contract.

Core Idea
Khul' is a contract of oath, complete without acceptance; sale requires acceptance.

When a husband claims he pronounced khul' (divorce for compensation) but the wife did not accept, and the wife says she did accept, who is believed? The Hanafi school gives a surprising answer: the husband is believed, unlike in sale. This lesson explores the legal reasoning behind this distinction, rooted in the unique nature of khul' as a 'contract of oath' (عقد يمين). We will examine the proofs, the analogy to sale, and the practical implications for evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The husband states: 'I divorced you yesterday for a thousand and you did not accept.' The wife responds: 'I accepted.' Determine which party's claim is given precedence in Hanafi fiqh.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The husband is believed (with his oath) regarding non-acceptance. The divorce is considered to have occurred solely by his acknowledgment of the pronouncement.
As per al-‘Imadi in al-Fusul.
3
Contrast with the sale case
In sale, if the seller says 'I sold you yesterday and you did not accept' and the buyer says 'I accepted,' the seller's denial is not accepted because it is contradictory. Explain why, using the nature of the contract.
Sale is not complete without acceptance; admitting the sale implies admitting acceptance.
4
Understand the legal basis (talil)
Khul' is a 'complete contract' (عقد تام) even without acceptance because it is a contract of oath. Thus, the husband's acknowledgment of the contract does not imply acknowledgment of the wife's acceptance. Contrast with sale, which lacks completeness without acceptance.
This talil is the foundation of the distinction.
5
Note additional nuances and authorities
The passage cites further scenarios: when the wife denies khul' altogether, claims dower or iddah maintenance, and when both produce evidence. Note that the husband's belief is not absolute; for example, regarding the dower, the wife's statement is taken if she has no evidence.
These nuances show the ruling's limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( طلقتك أمس بألف فلم تقبلي وقالت قبلت صدق بخلاف البيع والفرق أن الطلاق على مال بلا قبول عقد تام وهو عقد يمين فلا يكون إقراره به اقراراً بقبول المرأة، أما البيع بلا قبول المشتري فليس ببيع فكان إقراره به اقراراً بقبول المشتري، فدعواه بعده عدم قبول تناقض ومراده من تصديق الزوج قبول قوله مع يمينه كما نص عليه العمادي في الفصول، ولو قيد المسألة بالمال كما في الهداية لكان أولى ولولا ما ذكره المصنف في الكافي شرحاً لقوله بخلاف البيع من أن صورته ما لو قال لغيره بعت منك هذا العبد بألف درهم أمس فلم تقبل وقال المشتري قبلت إلى آخره لشرحت قوله بخلاف البيع بما لو قال بعتك طلاقك أمس فلم تقبلي فقالت بل ،قبلت، فقد نص في فتح القدير أن القبول لها لمناسبته للطلاق وفيه : ولو قال لعبده أعتقك أمس على ألف فلم تقبل وبعتك أمس نفسك منك بألف فلم تقبل على قياس قول الزوج لها اهـ. وفي التتارخانية : لو أقاما بينة أخذ ببينة المرأة ا هـ . وفي البزازية : ادى الخلع على حالها والمرأة تنكر يقع الطلاق بإقراره والدعوى في المال على حالها وعكسه لا يقع كـ ما كان ادعت المهر أو نفقة العدة، لأنه طلقها وادعى الخلع وليس لها بينة ففي حق المهر القول لها وفي النفقة قوله ا هـ . وينبغي حمله على ما إذا كان مدعياً أن من جملة بدل الخلع وعلى تقديره فالفرق أن المهر كان ثابتاً عليه قبله فدعواه سقوطه غير مقبول، وأما نفقة العدة فليست واجبة قبله وهي تدعي استحقاقها بالطلاق وهو ينكر فكان القول له وهو مشكل فإنهما اتفقا على سبب استحقاقها لأن الخلع والطلاق يوجبان نفقة العدة فكيف تسقط؟
His saying: 'I divorced you yesterday for a thousand and you did not accept, and she said: I accepted.' He is believed, unlike in sale. The difference is that divorce for a consideration is a complete contract without acceptance, and it is a contract of oath. Therefore, his acknowledgment of it is not an acknowledgment of the woman's acceptance. As for sale without the buyer's acceptance, it is not a sale, so his acknowledgment of it is an acknowledgment of the buyer's acceptance. So his claim afterwards of non-acceptance is contradictory. His intent in 'believing the husband' is accepting his statement with his oath, as al-‘Imadi stated in al-Fusul. If he had restricted the issue to money as in al-Hidayah, it would have been better. Were it not for what the author mentioned in al-Kafi commenting on his statement 'unlike in sale'—that its form is where he says to someone else 'I sold you this slave yesterday for a thousand dirhams and you did not accept, and the buyer says I accepted' and so on—I would have explained his statement 'unlike in sale' by saying 'I sold you your divorce yesterday and you did not accept, and she says rather I accepted' because it is stated in Fath al-Qadir that acceptance is hers due to its appropriateness for divorce. And in it: If he said to his slave 'I freed you yesterday for a thousand and you did not accept, and I sold you your own self yesterday for a thousand and you did not accept,' it is analogous to the husband's statement to his wife. And in al-Tatar Khaniyya: If both produce evidence, the woman's evidence is taken. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If he performed khul' while she is as she is and the woman denies, the divorce occurs by his acknowledgment and the claim regarding money remains as it is, and the opposite does not occur. For example, if she claimed the dower or iddah maintenance, because he divorced her and claimed khul' and she has no evidence, regarding the dower the statement is hers, and regarding maintenance his statement is his. It should be interpreted as when he claims that it is part of the khul' consideration. On that interpretation, the difference is that the dower was established upon him before, so his claim of its falling is unacceptable. As for iddah maintenance, it is not obligatory upon him before, and she claims entitlement to it by the divorce while he denies, so the statement is his. But this is problematic because they both agree on the cause of entitlement, since khul' and divorce both necessitate iddah maintenance, so how does it fall?
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific evidentiary dispute in khul'. When the husband says 'I divorced you yesterday for a thousand and you did not accept' and the wife says 'I accepted,' the husband is believed (with oath) in the Hanafi school. This is contrary to the case of sale, where if the seller says 'I sold you yesterday and you did not accept' and the buyer says 'I accepted,' the buyer's statement is not taken; instead the seller's statement is taken—but the text says 'he is believed' referring to the husband. The key distinction is that a divorce for compensation (khul') is a complete contract (tam) even without acceptance, because it is classified as a contract of oath (yamin). Therefore, when the husband admits to the divorce, he is not admitting to the wife's acceptance. In contrast, a sale without the buyer's acceptance is not a sale at all, so if the seller admits to the sale, he is effectively admitting to the buyer's acceptance. Hence, his later claim of non-acceptance is contradictory (tanāquḍ). The text then cites various authorities: al-‘Imadi, al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, Fath al-Qadir, al-Tatar Khaniyya, and al-Bazzaziyya to elaborate on various scenarios, including cases where the woman denies the khul' altogether, cases where she claims dower or iddah maintenance, and the ruling on evidence. The passage concludes with a problematic point: that iddah maintenance should be due in both khul' and divorce, so if the husband denies it, why is he believed? This is left as an issue (mushkil).

Key Terms
عقد يمين (‘aqd yamin): A contract considered akin to an oath, not requiring acceptance to be complete. Khul' is so classified.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession. Here, the husband's acknowledgment of divorce does not imply acceptance.
تناقض (tanāquḍ): Contradiction in one's statements. Used to explain why the seller's claim of non-acceptance is rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the husband's denial of acceptance in khul' not considered contradictory, unlike the seller's denial in sale?
A) Because khul' is a contract of oath complete without acceptance.
B) Because the husband is always believed in family matters.
C) Because the wife must prove she accepted.
D) Because sale is more formal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes khul' from sale based on the nature of the contract: khul' is a contract of oath, complete without acceptance, so the husband's denial of acceptance is believed; sale requires acceptance, so the seller's denial is contradictory.

Disputes Over Khul' Compensation: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Resolving disputes over number of divorces and amount of compensation in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on disputes over the amount of khul' compensation and explain how it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In khul', the wife's word on compensation is taken because she is the payor.

Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. When a dispute arises between husband and wife over the amount of compensation, the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on whose word is accepted. This lesson examines the Hanafi rule and its basis, derived from the passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Recognize that the husband and wife agree that khul' occurred but differ on the amount of compensation (al-‘iwad).
The dispute is about the quantum, not the occurrence of khul'.
2
State the Hanafi rule
The Hanafi school holds that the wife's statement is taken (القول لها). She is the one paying, so her claim about what she owes is given precedence.
This is a procedural rule of evidence, not about the validity of khul'.
3
Explain the rationale
The wife is the payer (المملكة) and thus her word on the amount she agreed to pay is believed, unless the husband produces evidence to the contrary.
The principle is that the one who is liable to pay is trusted in the absence of proof.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i requires mutual oath-taking (taḥāluf) – both parties swear oaths regarding the amount. This can lead to the khul' being invalidated or reduced.
The Shafi'i approach is based on general rules of dispute resolution.
5
Note the practical consequence
In the Hanafi school, the wife's claim stands unless the husband proves otherwise. In the Shafi'i school, the case may be resolved by oaths, often resulting in a compromise.
The difference affects the burden of proof and the outcome of the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جامع الفصولين : اختلفا في كمية الخلع فقال مرتان وقالت ثلاث قيل القول له، وقيل لو اختلفا بعد التزوج فقالت لم يجز التزوج لأنه وقع بعد الخلع الثالث نفقة العدة قوله : (ولو قيد المسألة بالمال الخ قال الرملي : النسخة التي شرح عليها الزيلعي والعيني ومنلا مسكين مقيدة بالمال فإن عبارتهم طلقتك أمس بألف اهـ . قلت : وكذلك عبارة النهر قوله: (وهو مشكل الخ) أصل الاستشكال لصاحب جامع الفصولين . أولى ا هـ . هي وأنكره فالقول له ولو اختلفا في العدة وبعد مضيها فقال عدة الخلع الثاني وقالت هي عدة الخلع الثالث فالقول لها فلا يحل النكاح ا هـ . وفي القنية : لو أقامت بينة أن زوجها المجنون خالعها في صحته وأقام وليه أو هو بعد الإفاقة بينة أنه خالعها في جنونه فبينة المرأة وفي كافي الحاكم : قال لها قد طلقتك واحدة بألف فقبلت فقالت إنما سألتك ثلاثاً بألف فطلقتني واحدة فلك ثلثها فالقول للمرأة مع يمينها، فإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة الزوج، وكذا لو اختلفا في مقدار الجعل بعد الاتفاق على الخلع أو قالت اختلعت بغير شيء فالقول قولها والبيئة بيئة الزوج، أما إذا اتفقا أنها سألته أن يطلقها ثلاثاً بألف وقالت طلقتني واحدة وقال هو ثلاثاً فالقول قوله إن كانا في المجلس، ألا ترى أنه لو قال لها أنت طالق أنت طالق أنت طالق في مجلس سؤالها الثلاث بألف كان له الألف؟ فغاية هذا أن يكون موقعاً الباقي في المجلس فيكون مثله، وإن كان غير ذلك المجلس لزمها الثلاث، وإن كانت في العدة فمن المتفق عليه ولا يكون للزوج إلا ثلث الألف، وإن قالت سألتك أن تطلقني ثلاثاً على ألف فطلقتني واحدة فلا شيء لك يعني على قول أبي حنيفة، وقال هو بل سألتني واحدة على ألف فطلقتكها فالقول قولها على قول أبي حنيفة، وإن قالت سألتك ثلاثاً بألف فطلقتني في ذلك المجلس واحدة والباقي في غيره وقال بل الثلاث فيه فالقول لها، وإن قالت سألتك أن تطلقني أنا وضرتي على ألف فطلقتني وحدي وقال طلقتها معك وقد افترقا من المجلس فالقول لها وعليها حصتها من الألف والأخرى طالق بإقراره، وكذا إذا قالت فلم تطلقني ولا في ذلك المجلس، وفي مسألة خلع الثنتين بسؤال واحد تنبيه وهو أنه إذا خلع امرأتيه على ألف كانت منقسمة على قدر ما تزوجهما عليه من المهر حتى لو سألتاه طلاقهما على ألف أو بألف فطلق إحداهما لزم المطلقة حصتها من الألف على قدر ما تزوجها عليه، فإن طلق الأخرى في ذلك المجلس أيضاً لزمها حصتها لأن الألف تنقسم عليهما بالسوية، ولو طلقهما بعدما افترقوا فلا شيء له. وإذا ادعت المرأة الخلع والزوج ينكره فأقامت بينة فشهد أحدهما بالألف والآخر بألف وخمسمائة أو اختلفا في جنس الجعل فالشهادة باطلة. وإن كان الزوج هو المدعي للخلع والمرأة تنكره فشهد أحد شاهديه بألف والآخر بألف وخمسمائة والزوج يدعي وخمسمائة حازت شهادتهما على الألف، وإن ادعى ألفاً لم تجز شهادتهما ولزمه الطلاق بإقراره؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفيه : لو اختلفا في مقدار العوض فالقول لها عندنا، وعند الشافعي يتحالفان
And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: They differed over the quantity of khul'. He said twice and she said three times. It was said: the statement is his. It was said: If they differed after the marriage, and she said: the marriage is not valid because it occurred after the third divorce. ... Iddah maintenance. ... His saying: (If he had restricted the issue to money...) al-Ramli said: The copy upon which al-Zayla'i, al-‘Ayni, and Mulla Miskin commented is restricted to money, for their phrase is: 'I divorced you yesterday for a thousand'. I said: likewise the phrase in al-Nahr. His saying: (it is problematic etc.) The source of the problem is from the author of Jami' al-Fusulayn. ... He said: First. ... She and he denied, so the statement is his. And if they differed regarding the iddah and after its expiry, he said it is the iddah of the second khul' and she said it is the iddah of the third khul', the statement is hers, so the marriage is not permissible. And in al-Qunyah: If the woman produces evidence that her insane husband made khul' with her during his sanity, and his guardian or he after his recovery produces evidence that he made khul' during his insanity, the woman's evidence is taken. And in Kafi al-Hakim: He said to her: 'I divorced you once for a thousand and you accepted.' She said: 'I asked you for three divorces for a thousand and you divorced me once, so you have one-third of it.' The statement is the woman's with her oath. If both produce evidence, the predominance is the husband's. Similarly, if they differ over the amount of the consideration after agreeing on the khul', or she said: 'I made khul' for nothing.' The statement is hers and the evidence is the husband's. As for if they agree that she asked him to divorce her three times for a thousand, and she said: 'You divorced me once,' and he said: 'Three times.' The statement is his if they are in the session. Do you not see that if he said to her 'You are divorced, you are divorced, you are divorced' in the session of her request for three divorces for a thousand, he would have the thousand? The extent is that he has effected the remaining in the session, so it is like that. If it was not in that session, the three are binding upon her. If she was in the iddah, it is agreed upon, and the husband does not get except one-third of the thousand. If she said: 'I asked you to divorce me three times for a thousand, and you divorced me once,' then he gets nothing, meaning according to Abu Hanifa. And if he said: 'Rather, you asked me for one divorce for a thousand and I divorced you once,' the statement is hers according to Abu Hanifa. If she said: 'I asked for three times for a thousand and you divorced me once in that session and the rest in another,' and he said: 'The three were in it,' the statement is hers. If she said: 'I asked you to divorce me and my co-wife for a thousand, and you divorced me alone,' and he said: 'I divorced you both,' and they separated from the session, the statement is for her, and she owes her share of the thousand, and the other is divorced by his acknowledgment. Similarly, if she said: 'You did not divorce me at all,' or 'not in that session.' And in the issue of khul' of two wives with one request: a note: that if he made khul' with his two wives for a thousand, it is divided according to the dower he married each on, such that if they asked him to divorce them for a thousand, and he divorced one, the one divorced owes her share of the thousand according to what he married her on. If he divorced the other in that session as well, she owes her share, because the thousand is divided between them equally. If he divorced them after they separated, he gets nothing. If the woman claims khul' and the husband denies it, and she produces evidence, and one witness testifies to a thousand and the other to a thousand five hundred, or they differ on the type of consideration, the testimony is void. If the husband is the claimant of khul' and the woman denies it, and one of his witnesses testifies to a thousand and the other to a thousand five hundred, and the husband claims a thousand five hundred, their testimony is valid for a thousand. If he claims a thousand, their testimony is not valid, and the divorce is binding by his acknowledgment. This is from Fath al-Qadir. And in it: If they differ over the amount of the consideration, the statement is hers according to us, and according to al-Shafi'i they take oaths.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage compiles numerous scenarios of dispute in khul'. The general Hanafi principle is that the wife's statement is taken regarding the amount of the consideration because she is the one paying (المملكة), unless the husband admits to more. There are many exceptions: when they are still in the session of the request, the husband's statement about the number of divorces may be taken; when the dispute is about the occurrence of khul' itself, different rules apply. The passage also discusses evidentiary rules when witnesses conflict, and highlights the difference with the Shafi'i school, where both parties take oaths (tahāluf). The text relies on authorities like Jami' al-Fusulayn, al-Qunyah, Kafi al-Hakim, Fath al-Qadir, etc.

Key Terms
الاختلاف في كمية الخلع (al-ikhtilāf fī kammiyyat al-khul‘): Disagreement between husband and wife over the number of divorces (e.g., one, two, or three) in the khul' agreement.
الجعل (al-ja‘l): The compensation (consideration) paid by the wife in khul'.
التحالف (al-tahāluf): Mutual oath-taking by both parties when they differ over terms; used by Shafi'i school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if the husband and wife agree that she asked for khul' but differ over the amount of consideration, to whom is the statement given in the Hanafi school?
A) The husband
B) The wife
C) Both take oaths
D) They settle

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the wife's statement regarding the amount of khul' compensation is accepted, as she is the payer.

Disputes on Khul' Compensation and the Irrevocable Nature of Khul'
Rulings on dispute and textual correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who is believed in a dispute about khul' compensation receipt, and explain why khul' results in a ba'in divorce.

Core Idea
In khul', the husband is believed about receipt; the divorce is irrevocable.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two important points from the later Hanafi tradition. First, if a wife pays the khul' compensation but the husband claims he received it for a different reason, whose statement is accepted? Second, it clarifies the correct textual reading and confirms that khul' effects a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce. Understanding these rules helps in applying khul' correctly in cases of dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The wife paid the khul' compensation; the husband claims he received the same amount for another reason. The question is who is believed.
2
State the relied-upon opinion
Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that the husband's statement is taken. This is the mufta bihi view, though a contrary opinion says the wife is believed because she is the owner.
3
Understand the textual correction
The text notes a variant: some copies read 'the thousand is divided between them equally', but the correct reading in Fath al-Qadir is 'no, by a thousand after no' – this likely indicates that the thousand is not divided equally but given to the husband as full compensation.
This corrects a potential misunderstanding about division.
4
Confirm the nature of khul' divorce
Al-Hakim al-Shahid explicitly stated that the divorce in khul' is ba'in (irrevocable). This is the established Hanafi position.
Khul' does not count among the three revocable divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البزازية : دفعت بدل الخلع وزعم الزوج أنه قبضه بجهة أخرى، أفتى الإمام ظهير الدين أن القول له، وقيل لها لأنها المملكة . ذلك ألفاً قوله : (لأن الألف تنقسم عليها بالسوية كذا في النسخ والذي في الفتح لا إن بالألف بعد لا وهي الصواب قوله : (وقد صرح بوقوع الطلاق (الخ أقول : صرح به الحاكم الشهيد أيضاً وبأنه بائن البحر الرائق ج ٤/ م ١٠
And in al-Bazzaziyya: She paid the compensation of khul' and the husband claims that he received it by another means. Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that the statement is his. It was said: hers, because she is the owner. That is a thousand. His saying: (because the thousand is divided between them equally) This is how it is in the copies, but what is in al-Fath is 'no, by a thousand after no' and that is correct. His saying: (and it is explicitly stated that the divorce occurs etc.) I say: al-Hakim al-Shahid also explicitly stated it and that it is irrevocable.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This short passage covers two final points. First, if a woman pays the khul' compensation and the husband claims he received it for another reason, the relied-upon fatwa is that the husband is believed, but there is a differing opinion that the wife is believed because she is the one giving. Second, the text corrects a textual variant: in some copies it says 'the thousand is divided between them equally' but in Fath al-Qadir it is 'no, by a thousand after no,' which is the correct reading. It also notes that al-Hakim al-Shahid explicitly stated that the divorce in khul' is irrevocable (ba'in).

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul‘): The consideration paid by the wife in exchange for divorce.
قبض (qabd): Taking possession or receipt of payment.
بائن (bā’in): Irrevocable divorce; once khul' is confirmed, the divorce is ba'in.
أفتى (aftā): He gave a fatwa; indicates the relied-upon opinion in practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is a revocable divorce (raj'i)
B) It is an irrevocable divorce (ba'in)
C) It is a suspended divorce (mu'allaq)
D) It is not considered a divorce

Key Takeaway
In khul', the husband is believed about receipt of compensation, and the divorce itself is irrevocable (ba'in).

Whose Word is Trusted? Disputes in Khul' on Number and Consideration
Series of dispute scenarios in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whose statement is accepted in disputes during khul' by analyzing the scenario, including the impact of the majlis and the nature of the disagreement.

Core Idea
In khul' disputes, the husband's word is taken on the number of divorces given in the same majlis; otherwise, it depends.

Khul' is a dissolution of marriage by which the wife compensates the husband. Disputes often arise about how many divorces were pronounced and what consideration was agreed. The Hanafi jurists have detailed rules for resolving these disputes, placing great weight on whether the parties are still in the same session (majlis) and on who bears the burden of proof. This lesson walks through the key scenarios from Ibn Nujaym's Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Determine what exactly the husband and wife disagree about: the number of divorces, the amount of consideration, or the timing (e.g., 'iddah).
The ruling often hinges on whether the disagreement is about the offer or the acceptance.
2
Assess the role of the majlis
Check if the parties are still in the same session where the khul' was agreed. If they differ on the number of divorces and are still in the majlis, the husband’s statement is preferred because he controls the pronouncement.
If the session has ended, the wife's statement may be taken.
3
Apply the default rule for each scenario
For most disputes (e.g., about the amount of consideration, or whether any divorce occurred), the wife's statement with oath is accepted, because she is the one surrendering money. But for the number of divorces pronounced in the same majlis, the husband’s word prevails.
The passage also provides exceptions and special cases.
4
Handle cases of multiple wives
When two wives are divorced by khul' with a single request, the consideration is divided according to their dowers if they are divorced separately, but equally if both are divorced in the same session.
If one is divorced after the session ends, no consideration is due for her.
5
Synthesize the evidentiary rule
When both parties bring evidence (bayyinah), the husband's proof is usually preferred because the husband is the one who pronounces divorce. However, if the wife proves a special condition (like the husband's insanity at the time), her proof is accepted.
This aligns with the general Hanafi principle that the person who controls the act bears the burden of proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولى ا هـ . هي وأنكره فالقول له ولو اختلفا في العدة وبعد مضيها فقال عدة الخلع الثاني وقالت هي عدة الخلع الثالث فالقول لها فلا يحل النكاح ا هـ . وفي القنية : لو أقامت بينة أن زوجها المجنون خالعها في صحته وأقام وليه أو هو بعد الإفاقة بينة أنه خالعها في جنونه فبينة المرأة وفي كافي الحاكم : قال لها قد طلقتك واحدة بألف فقبلت فقالت إنما سألتك ثلاثاً بألف فطلقتني واحدة فلك ثلثها فالقول للمرأة مع يمينها، فإن أقاما البينة فالبينة بينة الزوج، وكذا لو اختلفا في مقدار الجعل بعد الاتفاق على الخلع أو قالت اختلعت بغير شيء فالقول قولها والبيئة بيئة الزوج، أما إذا اتفقا أنها سألته أن يطلقها ثلاثاً بألف وقالت طلقتني واحدة وقال هو ثلاثاً فالقول قوله إن كانا في المجلس، ألا ترى أنه لو قال لها أنت طالق أنت طالق أنت طالق في مجلس سؤالها الثلاث بألف كان له الألف؟ فغاية هذا أن يكون موقعاً الباقي في المجلس فيكون مثله، وإن كان غير ذلك المجلس لزمها الثلاث، وإن كانت في العدة فمن المتفق عليه ولا يكون للزوج إلا ثلث الألف، وإن قالت سألتك أن تطلقني ثلاثاً على ألف فطلقتني واحدة فلا شيء لك يعني على قول أبي حنيفة، وقال هو بل سألتني واحدة على ألف فطلقتكها فالقول قولها على قول أبي حنيفة، وإن قالت سألتك ثلاثاً بألف فطلقتني في ذلك المجلس واحدة والباقي في غيره وقال بل الثلاث فيه فالقول لها، وإن قالت سألتك أن تطلقني أنا وضرتي على ألف فطلقتني وحدي وقال طلقتها معك وقد افترقا من المجلس فالقول لها وعليها حصتها من الألف والأخرى طالق بإقراره، وكذا إذا قالت فلم تطلقني ولا في ذلك المجلس، وفي مسألة خلع الثنتين بسؤال واحد تنبيه وهو أنه إذا خلع امرأتيه على ألف كانت منقسمة على قدر ما تزوجهما عليه من المهر حتى لو سألتاه طلاقهما على ألف أو بألف فطلق إحداهما لزم المطلقة حصتها من الألف على قدر ما تزوجها عليه، فإن طلق الأخرى في ذلك المجلس أيضاً لزمها حصتها لأن الألف تنقسم عليهما بالسوية، ولو طلقهما بعدما افترقوا فلا شيء له.
Firstly, end quote. He denied it, so the statement is his. If they differed about the 'iddah and after its expiry, and he said the 'iddah of the second khul', and she said the 'iddah of the third khul', then the statement is hers, so marriage is not permissible. End quote. In al-Qunyah: If she brought proof that her insane husband divorced her by khul' while sane, and his guardian or he after recovery brought proof that he divorced her by khul' while insane, then the proof of the woman [is accepted]. In Kafi al-Hakim: He said to her, 'I have divorced you with one [divorce] for one thousand,' and she accepted. Then she said, 'I only asked you for three [divorces] for one thousand, and you divorced me with one, so you have one third of it.' Then the statement is the woman's with her oath. If they both bring proof, then the proof of the husband. Likewise, if they differed about the amount of the consideration after agreeing on the khul', or she said, 'I divorced by khul' without anything,' then the statement is hers, and the proof is the husband's. However, if they agreed that she asked him to divorce her three [times] for one thousand, and she said, 'You divorced me with one,' and he said, 'Three,' then the statement is his if they are in the session. Do you not see that if he said to her, 'You are divorced, you are divorced, you are divorced,' in the session of her asking for three for one thousand, he would have the thousand? So the utmost of this is that he made the remainder occur in the session, so it is like that. If it was other than that session, she is obligated with three. If she was in the 'iddah, then it is agreed upon, and the husband has only one third of the thousand. If she said, 'I asked you to divorce me three times for one thousand, and you divorced me with one,' then nothing is for you, meaning according to Abu Hanifa's statement. And he said, 'Rather, you asked me for one for one thousand, so I divorced you with it.' Then the statement is hers according to Abu Hanifa's statement. If she said, 'I asked you for three for one thousand, and you divorced me in that session with one, and the remainder in another [session],' and he said, 'Rather, the three in it [the session],' then the statement is hers. If she said, 'I asked you to divorce me and my co-wife for one thousand, and you divorced me alone,' and he said, 'I divorced her with you, and they have separated from the session,' then the statement is hers, and she is obligated for her share of the thousand, and the other is divorced by his admission. Likewise if she said, 'You did not divorce me, nor in that session.' In the issue of dissolving two [wives] khul' by one request, there is a note: that if he divorced his two wives by khul' for one thousand, it is divided according to the dower he married them for. So if they both asked him to divorce them for one thousand or by one thousand, and he divorced one of them, the divorced one is obligated for her share of the thousand according to the dower he married her for. If he divorced the other also in that session, then her share is obligated because the thousand is divided between them equally. If he divorced them after they separated, then nothing is for him.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from Kitab al-Talaq, Bab al-Khul', dealing with disputes between spouses in khul' scenarios. The author, Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, presents cases from various sources like al-Qunyah and Kafi al-Hakim. The core principle is that in a disagreement about the number of divorces or the consideration, the statement of the party who is more likely to be truthful is accepted, often with oath. For example, if the wife claims she asked for three divorces but received one, and the husband claims he gave three, the husband's statement is accepted if they are still in the session, because the context implies the full number. If they differ about the 'iddah, the wife's statement is accepted. The passage also covers the division of consideration when two wives are divorced by khul' with one request: the thousand is divided according to their dowers, but if both are divorced in the same session, it is divided equally. The ruling emphasizes the importance of the session (majlis) in determining the number of divorces and the amount due.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Dissolution of marriage by the wife paying compensation to the husband, considered a bain divorce.
العوض (al-'iwad): The consideration paid by the wife in khul', typically money or property.
المجلس (al-majlis): The sitting/meeting in which the offer and acceptance of khul' take place; affects legal consequences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1000
B) 333
C) Nothing
D) 500

Key Takeaway
In khul' disputes, the husband's word on the number of divorces is taken if they are still in the same session; otherwise, the wife's word with oath prevails.

Dispute Resolution for Consideration in Khul'
Rulings on witness testimony in khul' disputes and inter-madhhab disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for resolving disputes over the consideration in khul' and distinguish it from the Shafi'i rule.

Core Idea
In khul', the wife's statement about the consideration is accepted; witnesses are not required for the amount.

When a husband and wife disagree on how much the wife paid for khul', whose word is taken? This lesson examines the Hanafi position—that the wife's statement is accepted—and contrasts it with Imam al-Shafi'i's view that both parties must take oaths. We also explore related rules when witnesses differ on the amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute scenario
Determine whether the husband or wife is claiming khul', and whether witnesses differ on the amount of consideration.
The passage distinguishes when the wife is claimant vs. the husband.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule for witness disagreement
If the wife brings witnesses who differ on the amount, their testimony is invalid. If the husband brings witnesses and they differ, their testimony is valid for the lower amount.
This protects the interest of the party not claiming khul'.
3
Understand the Hanafi rule for direct dispute
When the parties themselves disagree on the amount, the wife's statement is taken under oath because she is the one who paid the consideration.
Hanafi: al-qawlu qawluhā (her word is accepted).
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both parties are claimants and must take oaths (tahāluf), leading to splitting the difference or dismissal.
The thamarah al-khilaf is a different practical outcome.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا ادعت المرأة الخلع والزوج ينكره فأقامت بينة فشهد أحدهما بالألف والآخر بألف وخمسمائة أو اختلفا في جنس الجعل فالشهادة باطلة. وإن كان الزوج هو المدعي للخلع والمرأة تنكره فشهد أحد شاهديه بألف والآخر بألف وخمسمائة والزوج يدعي وخمسمائة حازت شهادتهما على الألف، وإن ادعى ألفاً لم تجز شهادتهما ولزمه الطلاق بإقراره؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفيه : لو اختلفا في مقدار العوض فالقول لها عندنا، وعند الشافعي يتحالفان | هـ. . وفي البزازية : دفعت بدل الخلع وزعم الزوج أنه قبضه بجهة أخرى، أفتى الإمام ظهير الدين أن القول له، وقيل لها لأنها المملكة . ذلك ألفاً قوله : (لأن الألف تنقسم عليها بالسوية كذا في النسخ والذي في الفتح لا إن بالألف بعد لا وهي الصواب قوله : (وقد صرح بوقوع الطلاق (الخ أقول : صرح به الحاكم الشهيد أيضاً وبأنه بائن البحر الرائق ج ٤/ م ١٠
And if the woman claims khul' and the husband denies it, and she brings proof, and one of the witnesses testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand five hundred, or they differ in the type of consideration, then the testimony is invalid. If the husband is the claimant of khul' and the woman denies it, and one of his witnesses testifies to one thousand and the other to one thousand five hundred, and the husband claims one thousand five hundred, then their testimony is valid for one thousand. If he claims one thousand, their testimony is not valid, and divorce is necessary upon him by his admission; so in Fath al-Qadir. And in it: If they differ about the amount of the consideration, then the statement is hers according to us [Hanafis], and according to al-Shafi'i they both take oaths. End quote. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: She paid the consideration for khul' and the husband claimed that he received it for another reason; Imam Zahir al-Din gave a fatwa that the statement is his, and it was said hers because she is the owner. That is one thousand. His statement: (Because the thousand is divided between them equally) as in the copies, and what is in al-Fath is 'no' by the thousand after 'no' and that is correct. His statement: (And he clearly stated the occurrence of divorce) I say: Al-Hakim al-Shahid also clearly stated it, and that it is bain. Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq vol. 4, p. 10.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of disputes in khul', focusing on witness testimony and an inter-madhhab disagreement. The author, Ibn Nujaym, quotes from Fath al-Qadir and al-Bazzaziyyah. The first part deals with cases where witnesses differ in the amount of consideration. If the woman claims khul' and brings witnesses who disagree, their testimony is invalid. If the husband claims khul' and his witnesses differ, their testimony is valid for the lower amount. The crucial point is the Hanafi rule that in a dispute about the amount of consideration, the wife's statement is taken (with oath), whereas Imam al-Shafi'i holds that both take oaths and the claim is divided. This is a clear inter-madhhab difference. The passage also includes a fatwa from Imam Zahir al-Din regarding a husband claiming he received the consideration for another reason: the husband's statement is accepted. The marginal note at the end clarifies a textual issue in the division of the thousand between two wives.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): A form of divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for a consideration (usually financial) paid to the husband.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal proof, typically testimony of two male witnesses or one male and two females.
التحالف (al-tahāluf): Both parties take oaths; a procedure when evidence is lacking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband must prove the higher amount.
B) The wife must prove the lower amount.
C) The wife's statement is accepted with oath.
D) Both parties must take oaths.

Key Takeaway
In a khul' dispute over the consideration, the Hanafi school accepts the wife's statement with her oath.

Effect of Khul' and Mubara'ah on Mutual Claims
Khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all claims between spouses related to marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how khul' and mubara'ah extinguish mutual claims related to marriage, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute when no consideration is mentioned.

Core Idea
Khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all marital claims, like a mutual discharge.

This lesson explores the legal effect of khul' and mubara'ah in Hanafi fiqh. These forms of separation not only dissolve the marriage but also wipe out all rights and claims that each spouse had against the other arising from the marriage, such as unpaid dower. A key nuance arises when no compensation is specified at the time of khul', leading to a disagreement within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The passage begins by stating that khul' and mubara'ah extinguish every marital right between spouses. This includes the dower (mahr), whether paid or not, before or after consummation.
The ruling is based on the idea that these contracts imply a complete discharge from both sides.
2
Distinguish between named and unnamed consideration
The text covers sixteen scenarios based on whether compensation is named (the dower, part of it, or other property) and whether it was received before or after consummation. The principle is that if compensation is named, the husband gets it and all claims are waived.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
When no consideration is mentioned, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one (preferred) holds that both are free from claims, but if the wife had received dower, she must return it because customarily khul' implies compensation. The other narration and the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that neither is free from the other's claims.
The preferred view is that both are free, as affirmed by Sarakhsi and Khuwahar Zadeh.
4
Note the consequences of khul' and mubara'ah
These forms of separation result in a bain (irrevocable) divorce. The husband's intention regarding the number of divorces is considered, but if he denies intent after taking compensation, he is not believed in court.
Mubara'ah is treated exactly like khul' in all these rulings.

Khul' and mubara'ah [extinguish] every right that each one has over the other related to marriage. So if he divorced her by khul' or mubara'ah for known property, the husband gets what she named, and no claim remains for either of them against the other regarding the dower, whether it was received or not received before or after consummation. If he divorced a minor by khul' with her property, it is not valid for her. If [it is] for one thousand on condition that he is a guarantor, she is divorced and the thousand is upon him. His statement: (Khul' and mubara'ah extinguish every right that each one has over the other related to marriage. So if he divorced her by khul' or mubara'ah for known property, the husband gets what she named, and no claim remains for either of them against the other regarding the dower, whether it was received or not received before or after consummation, because khul' is like a discharge that implies discharge from both sides. Because it indicates separation, and that cannot be realized unless no right remains for each against the other; otherwise, conflict would occur afterward. And 'mubara'ah' with hamza, and leaving it out is incorrect. She says, 'I am free from your marriage for such and such'; so in Sharh al-Wiqayah. Each aspect has two aspects: either the dower was received or not, and each has two aspects: before or after consummation. If they do not name anything, each is free of claims, as corrected in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyyah. The wording of al-Khulasa: If he divorced her by khul' without mentioning compensation, it has aspects. First, he is silent about it: Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in his copy that each is free of the other's claim, and Imam Khuwahar Zadeh mentioned that this is one of two narrations from Abu Hanifa, and it is the correct one. And if there is no dower on the husband, she must return what he gave her of dower because the property is mentioned customarily by mentioning khul'. In another narration from Abu Hanifa, which is the statement of the two companions, that neither is free from the other. End quote. And similarly mentioned in al-Bazzaziyyah. And the apparent meaning of their wording first is that if the dower was received, he has no recourse against her. Their wording second implies recourse. Qadi Khan explicitly stated in his Fatawa in this case that she returns what... clear, as he said in al-Kafi: When a woman divorces herself by khul' from her husband, the khul' is one bain divorce unless the husband intends three, then it is three. If he intends two, it is one bain divorce. Likewise, every divorce for compensation is bain. If the husband says, 'I did not intend divorce by khul'' while he has taken compensation, he is not believed in court. And mubara'ah is like khul' in all that. His statement: (Qadi Khan explicitly stated) that is where he said: A man said to his wife, 'I have divorced you by khul'' and she accepted, it occurs...

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal effects of khul' and mubara'ah (mutual release). The author explains that both forms of separation extinguish all claims related to marriage, including the dower (mahr) whether paid or not, and before or after consummation. The key point is that these contracts imply a complete discharge from both sides. A notable intra-Hanafi dispute arises when khul' is performed without specifying any consideration: according to one narration from Abu Hanifa (preferred by Sarakhsi), both are free from claims; but if no dower was paid, the wife must return the dower she received because customarily khul' implies some compensation. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that neither is free from claims. The passage also clarifies that khul' results in a bain (irrevocable) divorce, and the husband's intention regarding the number of divorces is considered; if he says he did not intend divorce, he is not believed if he took compensation. Mubara'ah is treated like khul' in all rulings. The text ends with a quotation from Qadi Khan confirming that khul' is effective.

Key Terms
المبارأة (al-mubāra'ah): A form of separation where both parties mutually agree to release each other from marital rights, similar to khul' but without compensation necessarily.
الطلاق البائن (al-ṭalāq al-bā'in): An irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
Khul' and mubara'ah are valid forms of separation that extinguish all marital claims; when no compensation is mentioned, the preferred view is that both are free and the wife returns any received dower.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Khul' and Mubara'ah Cancel All Mutual Claims
Ruling and proof regarding the effect of khul' and mubara'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal effect of khul' and mubara'ah on mutual claims, apply it to dower cases, and explain the rationale and the intention requirement.

Core Idea
Khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all marriage-related claims, including mahr, because true separation requires complete release.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: when a couple terminates their marriage through khul' or mubara'ah, all mutual financial claims—especially the dower—are automatically cancelled. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the logical basis and also addresses a subtle issue: whether an intention of divorce is required when using these terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with khul' and mubara'ah as modes of divorce. The ruling is that these two acts cancel every right each spouse has over the other arising from the marriage, including the dower (mahr).
The ruling covers both received and unpaid mahr, before and after consummation.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary provides the proof: khul' implies separation (fasl), and separation cannot be complete if any claim remains. This is a rational (istihsani) inference, as no explicit textual proof is cited.
The dalil is based on the linguistic meaning of khul' (to strip, remove) and the purpose of the transaction.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The reasoning is that khul' linguistically denotes parting and cutting off. For the separation to be full, no residual rights or claims should exist. Thus, the very essence of khul' demands extinguishment of all mutual claims.
This is a clear example of istihsan based on the underlying rationale (ma'na).
4
Note the ikhtilaf on intention
The passage highlights a disagreement among Hanafi scholars: is intention of divorce a condition for khul' and mubara'ah? The mashayikh dispensed with intention in khul' due to its widespread usage, but for mubara'ah and other kinayat, intention remains required if the term is not commonly used for divorce.
This distinction affects practical fatwa: in standard khul', no explicit intention is needed; in ambiguous phrases, it is required.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that khul' and mubara'ah cancel all claims, and intention of divorce is not required in khul' because of custom. For mubara'ah, if it is equally common, intention is waived; otherwise it is required.
This is the ruling endorsed by the later Hanafi authorities (mashayikh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلع والمبارأة كل حق لكل واحدة على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح حتى لو خالعها أو بارأها بمال معلوم كان للزوج ما سمت له ولم يبق لأحدهما قبل صاحبه دعوى في المهر مقبوضاً كان أو غير مقبوض قبل الدخول بها أو بعده وإن خلع صغيرة بما لها لم يجز عليها ولو بألف على أنه ضامن طلقت والألف عليه.
قوله : (ويسقط الخلع والمبارأة كل حق لكل واحد على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح حتى لو خالعها أو باراها بمال معلوم كان للزوج ما سمت له ولم يبق لإحدهما قبل صاحبه دعوى في المهر مقبوضاً كان أو غير مقبوض قبل الدخول بها أو بعده لأن الخلع كالبراءة يقتضي البراءة من الجانبين لأنه ينبئ عن الخلع وهو الفصل ولا يتحقق ذلك إلا إذا لم يبق لكل واحد منهما قبل صاحبه حق وإلا تحققت المنازعة بعده والمبارأة بالهمزة وتركها خطأ أن يقول وهي هذه الزوج برئت من نكاحك بكذا ؛ كذا في شرح الوقاية ولا يخفى وقوع الطلاق البائن في الصورة وقد صورها في فتح القدير بأن يقول بارأتك على ألف وتقبل ولم يذكر وقوع الطلاق به، وقد صرح بوقوع الطلاق بهذا اللفظ في الخلاصة والبزازية لكن قال فيها نية الطلاق في الخلع والمبارأة شرط الصحة إلا أن المشايخ لم يشترطوه في الخلع لغلبة الاستعمال، ولأن الغالب كون الخلع بعد مذاكرة الطلاق فلو كانت المبارأة أيضاً كذلك لا حاجة إلى النية وإن من الكنايات وإن لم يكن كذلك فبقيت مشروطه في المبارأة وسائر الكنايات على الأصل كان
Khul' and mubara'ah cancel every right that each one has over the other from what pertains to marriage. So if a man makes khul' with his wife or mubara'ah with her for a known property, the husband gets what she named, and neither of them has any claim against the other regarding the dower, whether it was received or not, before consummation or after. And if he makes khul' with a minor girl with her property, it is not valid against her. And if he says 'upon one thousand on condition that I am a guarantor', she is divorced and the one thousand is due from him.
He said: (Khul' and mubara'ah cancel every right that each one has over the other from what pertains to marriage, so that if he makes khul' with her or mubara'ah with her for a known property, the husband gets what she named, and neither of them has any claim against the other regarding the dower, whether it was received or not, before consummation or after) because khul' is like a release, it necessitates release from both sides, because it indicates khul', which is separation, and that is not achieved unless there remains no right for each of them against the other; otherwise conflict would occur afterward. Mubara'ah is with a hamzah, and omitting it is an error. He says: 'She, this wife, is released from your marriage for such and such'; as in Sharh al-Wiqayah. And it is not hidden that a ba'in divorce occurs in this case. He depicted it in Fath al-Qadir as saying: 'I make mubara'ah with you for one thousand' and she accepts, and he did not mention the occurrence of divorce by it. And the occurrence of divorce by this wording has been explicitly stated in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya, but it said therein: 'Intention of divorce in khul' and mubara'ah is a condition of validity.' However, the mashayikh did not require it in khul' due to the preponderance of usage, and because usually khul' occurs after discussing divorce. If mubara'ah is also like that, then there is no need for intention, and it is among the kinayat. If it is not like that, then it remains conditional in mubara'ah and the rest of the kinayat according to the original principle.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents the foundational ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The matn states that khul' and mubara'ah extinguish all mutual claims arising from the marriage contract, including the dower, regardless of whether it was received, not received, before consummation, or after. The sharh explains the rationale: khul' is essentially a release (bara'ah), and true separation requires that no claims remain. The commentary then discusses the wording of mubara'ah, noting the correct pronunciation. It clarifies that uttering the word 'bara'tu' in the context of khul' results in a ba'in divorce, even if the word 'talaq' is not mentioned. However, it mentions that in khul' and mubara'ah, intention (niyyah) of divorce is generally required for validity in allusive words, but the mashayikh dispensed with it in khul' because it is so commonly used for divorce. For mubara'ah, if it is also commonly used, intention is not required; otherwise, it is.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): A divorce initiated by the wife in consideration of compensation paid to the husband, resulting in a ba'in divorce.
المبارأة (al-mubara'ah): A mutual release from marriage, where both parties give up claims, often used synonymously with khul'.
المهر (al-mahr): The dower given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Both parties are released from any claims regarding the mahr, whether received or not.
D) The mahr remains due but can be claimed after the 'iddah.

Key Takeaway
Khul' and mubara'ah automatically extinguish all mutual marriage claims, and intention of divorce is presumed in khul' due to prevalent usage.
