Rulings When No Compensation is Specified in Khul'
Detailing the three narrations from Abu Hanifa on the effect of khul' without specified compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three narrations from Abu Hanifa on the effect of khul' without specified compensation and identify the preferred view with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
When khul' is made without specifying compensation, the preferred Hanafi view is that all claims between spouses are completely extinguished.

In a khul' (divorce initiated by the wife with compensation), the parties may sometimes omit specifying any compensation. This scenario leads to a significant internal Hanafi dispute: what happens to the mahr and other claims? Abu Hanifa has three different narrations, and his two disciples also hold a distinct position. This lesson unpacks the three narrations and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage discusses khul' where no compensation (mahr or other property) is named. Understand the four-fold classification: whether compensation is explicitly mentioned or not, and whether the mahr was received or not, and whether consummation occurred.
2
List the three narrations from Abu Hanifa
Narration 1: both parties are completely released from all claims (preferred). Narration 2: only the mahr is waived, not other debts. Narration 3: both mahr and other debts are waived.
3
Consider the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)
According to them, the parties are not released from each other unless a specific compensation is mentioned. This is in contrast to Abu Hanifa's first narration.
4
Identify the dalil (proof) for the preferred view
The preferred view relies on custom ('urf): mentioning khul' implies by custom that the mahr is considered part of the compensation, and the mention of khul' itself is taken as an agreement to waive all marital claims.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under the preferred view, the wife keeps any mahr she received and the husband is freed from any unpaid mahr. Under other views, the wife may have to return part or all of the mahr, or the husband may still have claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشمل أول كلامه ستة عشر وجهاً لأنه لا يخلو إما أن لا يسميا شيئاً أو سميا المهر أو اهـ. بعضه أو مالاً آخر، وكل وجه على وجهين إما أن يكون المهر مقبوضاً أو لا، وكل على وجهين إما أن يكون قبل الدخول أو بعده، فإن لم يسميا شيئاً برىء كل منهما كما صححه في الخلاصة والبزازية وعبارة الخلاصة : لو خالعها ولم يذكر العوض عليها فهو على وجوه : الأول أن يسكت عنه : ذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في نسخته أنه يبرأ كل واحد منهما عن دعوى صاحبه وذكر الإمام خواهر زاده أن هذا إحدى الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة، وهو الصحيح وإن لم يكن على الزوج مهر فعليها رد ما ساق إليها من المهر لأن المال مذكور عرفاً بذكر الخلع، وفي رواية عن أبي حنيفة وهو قولهما أنه لا يبرأ أحدهما عن صاحبه ا هـ . وهكذا ذكر في البزازية وظاهر عبارتهما أولاً أن المهر إذا كان مقبوضاً فلا رجوع له عليها، كلامهما ثانياً الرجوع. وقد صرح قاضيخان في فتاويه في هذه الصورة بأنها ترد ما وصريح حيث قال في الكافي : وإذا اختلعت المرأة من زوجها فالخلع تطليقة بائنة إلا أن ينوي الزوج ثلاثاً فتكون ثلاثاً، وإن نوى ثنتين كانت واحدة بائنة، وكذلك كل طلاق بجعل فهو بائن، فإن قال الزوج لم أعن بالخلع طلاقاً وقد أخذ عليه جعلاً لم يصدق في الحكم والمبارأة بمنزلة الخلع في جميع ذلك .
قوله : (وقد صرح قاضيخان الخ) وذلك حيث قال : رجل قال لزوجته خالعتك فقبلت يقع ساق إليها من المهر فحينئذ لم يبرأ كل منهما عن صاحبه، وقد ظهر لي أن محل البراءة لكل منهما ما إذا خالعها بعد ما دفع لها معجل المهر وقد بقي مؤجله فإنه يبرأ عن مؤجله وتبرأ عن معجله، ولذا قال في المحيط : وهو الصحيح أنه يسقط من المهر ما قبضت المرأة فهو لها وما كان باقياً في ذمة الزوج يسقط ا هـ. وفي البزازية : قال لها خلعتك فقالت قبلت لا هي هي . هـ . الطلاق ويبرأ الزوج عن المهر الذي لها عليه فإن لم يكن لها عليه مهر كان عليها رد ما ساق إليها من الصداق؛ كذا ذكر الحاكم الشهيد في الاقرار من المختصر والشيخ الإمام المعروف بخواهر زاده، وبه أخذ الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل. وهذا يؤيد ما ذكرنا عن أبي يوسف أن الخلع لا يكون إلا بعوض ! وفي كلامه إشارة إلى الخلاف في المسألة وفيها ثلاث روايات: إحداها لا يبرأ عن المهر فتأخذه إن لم يكن مقبوضاً . قال في البدائع : وهذا ظاهر جواب ظاهر الرواية الثانية يبرأ كل منهما عن المهر لا غير فلا يطالب به أحدهما الآخر وهو الصحيح على قول أبي حنيفة قبل الدخول أو بعده، مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض. الثالثة براءة كل منهما عن المهر وعن دين آخر، كذا في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان لابن الشحنة ؛ كذا في الشرنبلالية. وقال الزيلعي فإن لم يسميا شيئاً برىء كل واحد منهما عن حق الآخر مما لزمه بالنكاح في الصحيح، سواء كان قبل الدخول أو بعده، وكان المهر مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض حتى لا يجب عليها رد ما قبضت لو كان قبل الدخول. وروي عنه أنه لا يبرأ عنه وروي عنه أنه يبرأ عن دين آخر أيضاً ا وقوله لو كان قبل الدخول أي وبعده بالأولى لأن الطلاق قبل الدخول موجب لرد نصف المهر فإذا لم يلزمها رد شيء منه هنا ففيما بعد الدخول بالأولى. وقال في فتح القدير : والثالثة يبرأ كل منهما عن المهر لا غير فلا يطالب به أحدهما الآخر وهو الصحيح على قول أبي حنيفة، سواء كان قبل الدخول أو بعده، مقبوضاً كان أو لا، حتى لا ترجع عليه بشيء إن لم يكن ،مقبوضاً، ولا يرجع الزوج عليها إن كان مقبوضاً كله والخلع قبل الدخول. وهذا لأن المال مذكور عرفاً بالخلع فحيث لم يصرح به لزم ما هو من حقوق النكاح بقرينة أن المراد الانخلاع منه ا هـ . وفي غرر الأذكار شرح درر البحار إن لم يسميا شيئاً برئ كل منهما من الآخر قبضت المهر أم لا دخل بها أم لا اهـ. وفي متن المختار والمبارأة كالخلع يسقطان كل حق بكل واحد من الزوجين على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح حتى لو كان قبل الدخول وقد قبضت المهر لا يرجع عليها بشيء، ولو لم تقبض شيئاً لا ترجع عليه بشيء، ولو خلعها على مال آخر لزمها وسقط الصداق. ثم قال في شرحه الاختيار : ولو اختلعا ولم يذكرا المهر ولا بدلاً آخر فالصحيح أنه يسقط ما بقي من المهر وما قبضته فهو لها .اهـ. وفي متن الملتقى والمبارأة كالخلع يسقط كل منهما كل حق لكل واحد من الزوجين على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح فلا تطالب بمهر ولا نفقة ماضية مفروضة، ولا يطالب هو بنفقة عجلها ولم تمض مدتها ولا بمهر سلمه وخلع قبل الدخول ا أقول : وبه علم أن المذكور في الفتاوى رواية رابعة، والصحيح ما نقلناه عن هذه الشروح والمتون من براءة كل منهما مطلقاً بلا رجوع لأحد على الآخر بشيء من المهر خلافاً لما استظهره المؤلف والله تعالى أعلم
And his first statement includes sixteen aspects because it is either that they do not name anything, or they name the dower, or part of it, or other property. Each aspect has two subdivisions: either the dower was received or not, and each has two: either before consummation or after. If they do not name anything, both are released, as corrected in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya. The expression of al-Khulasa: If he makes khul' with her and does not mention compensation, it has aspects: first, to remain silent about it: Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi in his copy said that each of them is released from the claim of the other, and Imam Khwaharzadeh said that this is one of two narrations from Abu Hanifa, and it is the correct one. And if the husband owes no dower, then she must return what he gave her as dower because wealth is mentioned customarily by mentioning khul'. And in another narration from Abu Hanifa, which is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not release one from the other. ... He said: (And Qadikhan explicitly stated, etc.) That is where he said: A man said to his wife 'I divorce you by khul'' and she accepted, the divorce occurs, and the husband is released from the dower that she has against him. If she has no dower against him, then she must return what he gave her as dower; thus mentioned by al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Iqrar from al-Mukhtasar and the Imam known as Khwaharzadeh, and Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl adopted it. This supports what we mentioned from Abu Yusuf that khul' is only with compensation! And in his speech there is an indication of the disagreement in the issue, and it has three narrations: one: he is not released from the dower, so she takes it if it was not received. He said in al-Bada'i': This is the apparent answer of the apparent narration the second: each of them is released from the dower only, so neither claims it from the other, and this is the correct view according to Abu Hanifa, before consummation or after, received or not received. The third: release of each from the dower and from another debt. ... And al-Zayla'i said: If they do not name anything, each one is released from the right of the other due to marriage in the correct view, whether before consummation or after, and the dower was received or not, so that she is not required to return what she received if it was before consummation. ... And in the text of al-Mukhtar: And mubara'ah is like khul', both cancel every right that each of the spouses has over the other from what pertains to marriage, so that if it was before consummation and she had received the dower, he does not claim anything from her, and if she did not receive anything, she does not claim anything from him. ... Then he said in its commentary al-Ikhtiyar: And if they make khul' and do not mention the dower nor any other substitute, the correct view is that what remains of the dower is canceled and what she received is hers. ... And in the text of al-Multaqa: And mubara'ah is like khul', both cancel every right that each of the spouses has over the other from what pertains to marriage, so she is not demanded for dower nor past prescribed maintenance, and he is not demanded for maintenance he advanced whose period has not passed, nor for dower he handed over, and khul' before consummation. I say: And by this it is known that what is mentioned in the fatawa is a fourth narration, and the correct view is what we have transmitted from these commentaries and texts of the release of each absolutely without recourse of one against the other for anything of the dower, contrary to what the author inferred, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a khul' or mubara'ah agreement does not specify any compensation (such as the dower or other property). The text first categorizes sixteen possible cases based on whether compensation is named (nothing, dower, part of it, other property), whether the dower was received, and whether consummation occurred. The central dispute is about what happens when no compensation is mentioned. There are three main narrations from Abu Hanifa: (1) Both parties are completely freed from all claims related to marriage (this is the preferred view, as supported by al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and many later scholars). (2) They are only freed from the dower, not from other debts. (3) They are freed from the dower and also from other debts. The text cites various authorities like QadiKhan, al-Muhit, al-Zayla'i, Fath al-Qadir, and others. The preferred view (sahih) according to the later commentators (e.g., in al-Ikhtiyar, al-Multaqa) is that both parties are absolved of all claims, including any return of dower. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (Ibn Nujaym) comments that this is the correct view, contrary to what the author (of the original work) may have suggested.

Key Terms
البراءة (al-bara'ah): Release or freedom from claims; in this context, the mutual release of rights between spouses.
العرف (al-'urf): Custom; the text uses 'urf to justify that mentioning khul' implies compensation of the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (sahih) within the Hanafi school, what happens to the mahr when a khul' occurs without specifying any compensation?
A) The wife must return the mahr she received.
B) The husband must still pay any unpaid mahr.
C) Both parties are completely absolved of any claims regarding the mahr.
D) The wife must return half the mahr if the khul' was before consummation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the preferred view for khul' without specified compensation is that both spouses are released from all financial claims related to the marriage.

Ruling on Saying 'Khal'atuki' and Its Effect on Divorce and Dower
Ruling on divorce and dower via the phrase 'khal'atuki'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband says 'khal'atuki' and his wife accepts, and explain the effect on the dower (mahr).

Core Idea
The phrase 'khal'atuki' with acceptance effects a divorce and releases or returns the dower.

This lesson focuses on a specific ruling from al-Bazzaziyya regarding the phrase 'khal'atuki' (I divorce you by khul'). The passage clarifies that this clear expression, when accepted by the wife, constitutes a valid divorce and determines the financial consequences regarding the dower. Understanding this helps distinguish khul' initiated by the husband's explicit wording from other forms of dissolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its legal effect
The phrase 'khal'atuki' is a direct (sarih) expression for khul'. Recognize that the passage treats it as effective without need for intention.
This is based on the Hanafi view that certain words are inherently clear in meaning.
2
Determine the ruling on divorce
The passage states 'yqa' al-talaq' (the divorce occurs). Note that it results in a ba'in divorce, not a revocable one.
Khul' always results in a ba'in divorce in the Hanafi school.
3
Determine the ruling on the dower
The husband is released from any unpaid dower. If no dower was owed (i.e., the wife already received it), she must return what she received from him.
This mirrors the financial aspect of khul' where the wife compensates the husband for the release.
4
Note the authorities cited
The ruling is supported by al-Hakim al-Shahid, Khwaharzadeh, and Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, indicating it is a relied-upon position among later Hanafi scholars.
These are considered authoritative in the fatawa mutakhkhirin category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي البزازية قال لها خلعتك فقالت قبلت لا هي هي . هـ . الطلاق ويبرأ الزوج عن المهر الذي لها عليه فإن لم يكن لها عليه مهر كان عليها رد ما ساق إليها من الصداق؛ كذا ذكر الحاكم الشهيد في الاقرار من المختصر والشيخ الإمام المعروف بخواهر زاده، وبه أخذ الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل.
He said: (And in al-Bazzaziyya: He said to her 'I divorce you by khul'', and she said 'I accept'...) Unexpected text 'لا هي هي'. End. The divorce occurs, and the husband is released from the dower that she has against him. If she has no dower against him, then she must return what he gave her as dower; thus mentioned by al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Iqrar from al-Mukhtasar and the Imam known as Khwaharzadeh, and Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl adopted it.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage cites a ruling from al-Bazzaziyya regarding a husband saying 'khal'atuki' (I divorce you by khul') and the wife accepting. The ruling is that a divorce (talaq) occurs and the husband is released from any unpaid dower (mahr). If there was no dower owed, the wife must return the dower she received. This is supported by the authorities mentioned. The passage reinforces the principle that khul' with the word 'khal'atuki' effects a divorce and extinguishes or returns the dower depending on the circumstances.

Key Terms
خالعتك (khal'atuki): A phrase meaning 'I divorce you by khul'', which is a direct expression for initiating khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Bazzaziyya, if a husband says 'khal'atuki' to his wife and she accepts, what is the ruling?
A) It is not valid unless he explicitly says 'talaq'.
B) It is considered a valid divorce (talaq) and the husband is released from any unpaid dower.
C) It is considered a khul' but no divorce occurs.
D) It is valid only if he intended divorce.

Key Takeaway
When a husband says 'khal'atuki' and wife accepts, a ba'in divorce occurs and the dower is released or must be returned.

Khul' Without Specified Compensation: The Three Narrations and Their Tarjih
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of khul' without specified compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi narrations on khul' without specified compensation, identify the mufta bihi position, and apply its ruling to a given scenario.

Core Idea
In khul' without specified compensation, the mufta bihi is mutual release from the mahr only — not from other debts.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the financial consequences of khul' (wife-initiated divorce) when no specific compensation is mentioned. The author identifies three narrations (riwayat) attributed to Abu Hanifa, each with a different scope of release. Understanding which narration is relied upon (mufta bihi) is crucial for issuing correct fatwas in marriage dissolution cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three narrations
From the passage, extract the three positions: (1) no release from mahr, (2) release from mahr only, (3) release from mahr and other debts. Note the key phrases: 'لا يبرأ', 'يبرأ عن المهر لا غير', 'يبرأ عن المهر وعن دين آخر'.
The first narration is the apparent answer from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author and multiple commentators (al-Zayla'i, Fath al-Qadir, al-Multaqa) affirm the second narration as the correct view (as-salih, al-mukhtar). This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The second narration is attributed to Abu Hanifa himself in the soundest transmission.
3
Understand the scope of release
Under the mufta bihi, 'yabra' kullu minhuma 'an al-mahr la ghayr' means each spouse is released from any claim related to the mahr. The wife keeps what she received; the husband is freed from any unpaid balance. No other debts (e.g., past maintenance) are waived.
The reasoning: mahr is conventionally understood as the consideration in khul', so only it drops when unspecified.
4
Apply to before/after consummation and receipt
The ruling applies whether khul' occurs before or after consummation, and whether the mahr was received or not. The passage emphasizes 'sawa' kana qabla al-dukhul aw ba'dahu, maqbudan aw ghayra maqbud'.
This differs from regular talaq before consummation where half the mahr is returned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في البدائع : وهذا ظاهر جواب ظاهر الرواية الثانية يبرأ كل منهما عن المهر لا غير فلا يطالب به أحدهما الآخر وهو الصحيح على قول أبي حنيفة قبل الدخول أو بعده، مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض. الثالثة براءة كل منهما عن المهر وعن دين آخر، كذا في شرح منظومة ابن وهبان لابن الشحنة ; كذا في الشرنبلالية. وقال الزيلعي فإن لم يسميا شيئاً برىء كل واحد منهما عن حق الآخر مما لزمه بالنكاح في الصحيح، سواء كان قبل الدخول أو بعده، وكان المهر مقبوضاً أو غير مقبوض حتى لا يجب عليها رد ما قبضت لو كان قبل الدخول. وروي عنه أنه لا يبرأ عنه وروي عنه أنه يبرأ عن دين آخر أيضاً وقوله لو كان قبل الدخول أي وبعده بالأولى لأن الطلاق قبل الدخول موجب لرد نصف المهر فإذا لم يلزمها رد شيء منه هنا ففيما بعد الدخول بالأولى. وقال في فتح القدير : والثالثة يبرأ كل منهما عن المهر لا غير فلا يطالب به أحدهما الآخر وهو الصحيح على قول أبي حنيفة، سواء كان قبل الدخول أو بعده، مقبوضاً كان أو لا، حتى لا ترجع عليه بشيء إن لم يكن مقبوضاً، ولا يرجع الزوج عليها إن كان مقبوضاً كله والخلع قبل الدخول. وهذا لأن المال مذكور عرفاً بالخلع فحيث لم يصرح به لزم ما هو من حقوق النكاح بقرينة أن المراد الانخلاع منه ا هـ . وفي غرر الأذكار شرح درر البحار إن لم يسميا شيئاً برئ كل منهما من الآخر قبضت المهر أم لا دخل بها أم لا اهـ. وفي متن المختار والمبارأة كالخلع يسقطان كل حق بكل واحد من الزوجين على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح حتى لو كان قبل الدخول وقد قبضت المهر لا يرجع عليها بشيء، ولو لم تقبض شيئاً لا ترجع عليه بشيء، ولو خلعها على مال آخر لزمها وسقط الصداق. ثم قال في شرحه الاختيار : ولو اختلعا ولم يذكرا المهر ولا بدلاً آخر فالصحيح أنه يسقط ما بقي من المهر وما قبضته فهو لها .اهـ. وفي متن الملتقى والمبارأة كالخلع يسقط كل منهما كل حق لكل واحد من الزوجين على الآخر مما يتعلق بالنكاح فلا تطالب بمهر ولا نفقة ماضية مفروضة، ولا يطالب هو بنفقة عجلها ولم تمض مدتها ولا بمهر سلمه وخلع قبل الدخول ا أقول : وبه علم أن المذكور في الفتاوى رواية رابعة، والصحيح ما نقلناه عن هذه الشروح والمتون من براءة كل منهما مطلقاً بلا رجوع لأحد على الآخر بشيء من المهر خلافاً لما استظهره المؤلف والله تعالى أعلم
He said in al-Bada'i: And this is the apparent answer of the apparent narration: the second: each one is released from the mahr and nothing else, so neither can claim it from the other, and this is the correct view according to Abu Hanifa, whether before or after consummation, whether the mahr was received or not. The third: each is released from the mahr and from any other debt. Likewise in Sharh Manzumah Ibn Wahban by Ibn al-Shihnah, and likewise in al-Sharnablaliyyah. And al-Zayla'i said: If they did not specify anything, each one is released from the right of the other regarding what was incumbent due to the marriage in the correct view, whether before or after consummation, whether the mahr was received or not, so she is not obliged to return what she received if it was before consummation. And it is narrated from him that he is not released from it, and it is narrated from him that he is released from another debt as well. And his statement 'if it was before consummation' means and after consummation even more so, because divorce before consummation necessitates the return of half the mahr, so if she is not obliged to return anything here, then after consummation it is even more so. And he said in Fath al-Qadir: And the third: each is released from the mahr and nothing else, so neither can claim it from the other, and this is the correct view according to Abu Hanifa, whether before or after consummation, whether received or not, so she does not claim anything from him if it was not received, and the husband does not claim from her if it was all received and the khul' was before consummation. And this is because wealth is conventionally mentioned in khul', so when it was not explicit, what is due from the rights of marriage applies, by the indication that the intention is to dissolve from him. And in Ghurar al-Adhkar Sharh Durar al-Bihar: If they did not specify anything, each is released from the other, whether she received the mahr or not, whether he consummated or not. And in the text of al-Mukhtar: And mubara'ah is like khul', both drop every right that each spouse has over the other related to marriage, so if it was before consummation and she received the mahr, he does not claim anything from her, and if she did not receive anything, she does not claim anything from him. And if he made khul' with her for some other wealth, it is binding on her and the dower is dropped. Then he said in its commentary al-Ikhtiyar: And if they mutually divorced without mentioning the mahr or any other substitute, the correct view is that what remains of the mahr is dropped and what she received is for her. And in the text of al-Multaqa: And mubara'ah is like khul', both drop every right that each spouse has over the other related to marriage, so she does not claim mahr or past maintenance that was obligatory, and he does not claim maintenance that he advanced and its term has not passed, nor mahr he delivered and khul' before consummation. I say: And by this it is known that what is mentioned in the fatawa is a fourth narration, and the correct view is what we have transmitted from these commentaries and texts: absolute release of each, without either claiming anything of the mahr from the other, contrary to what the author deemed apparent. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, discussing the effect of khul' (divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation) when no specific compensation is mentioned. The author presents three narrations (riwayat) within the Hanafi school. The first narration (from Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that neither party is released from the mahr – the wife can still claim it if unpaid. The second, which is the soundest (as-salih) according to Abu Hanifa, holds that each is released from the mahr only (not from any other debts). The third holds that they are released from both the mahr and other debts. Al-Zayla'i and others affirm the second narration as the correct view, emphasizing that this applies whether before or after consummation, and whether the mahr was received or not. The text then quotes various sources (Fath al-Qadir, Ghurar al-Adhkar, al-Mukhtar, al-Multaqa) to support the second narration, concluding that the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is mutual release without any claim regarding the mahr. The author notes that some later fatawa mention a fourth narration, but the correct view remains the second.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife with compensation paid to the husband.
مهر (mahr): The dower given by husband to wife, which can be prompt (mu'ajjal) or deferred (mu'ajjal).
براءة (bara'ah): Release from a financial obligation; here, release from any claim to the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the soundest Hanafi position (mufta bihi), when a husband and wife perform khul' without specifying any compensation, what happens to the mahr?
A) The wife must return any mahr she received, and the husband must still pay any unpaid mahr.
B) Each spouse is released from any claim regarding the mahr: the wife keeps what she received, and the husband owes nothing if unpaid.
C) The husband must pay half the mahr if divorced before consummation, and the wife must return half if she received it.
D) The wife is released from the mahr but not from other debts; the husband can still claim other debts.

Key Takeaway
In khul' without specified compensation, the mufta bihi is the second narration: each spouse is released from claims to the mahr, but not from other debts.

The Core Difference Between 'Khala'tuka' and 'Khala'tuka' in Khul'
Explaining the legal difference between two wordings used for khul'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the unilateral form 'khala'tuka' and the mutual form 'khala'tuka' in khul', and state the legal consequences of each regarding the need for acceptance and release from financial obligations.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'khala'tuka' is unilateral without acceptance or release; 'khala'tuka' is mutual with acceptance and release.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explicitly contrasts two wordings for khul'. This lesson unpacks that comparison, clarifying the roles of acceptance and intention, and the financial consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two wordings
Find the two forms: 'khala'tuka' (without mufa'ala) and 'khala'tuka' (with mufa'ala). Note their literal meaning: the first is from 'khal' (to remove), the second is the mutual form.
The first is a simple past verb; the second is the form of mutual action.
2
First difference: Need for acceptance
According to the passage, 'khala'tuka' does not require the wife's acceptance; if the husband intends divorce, it takes effect as a bain divorce. By contrast, 'khala'tuka' requires her explicit acceptance (qabool).
The husband's intention is decisive for the unilateral form.
3
Second difference: Release from financial rights
'Khala'tuka' does not release the husband from the mahr (if unpaid) or other financial rights. 'Khala'tuka' results in full release (bara'a) from mahr and other obligations.
This is a major practical consequence: one form requires payment, the other does not.
4
Summary of the two differences
First: acceptance needed? No vs yes. Second: financial release? No vs yes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وفي البزازية قال لها خلعتك الخ) قال في النهر : ينبغي أنه لو قال لها برئت من نكاحك يقع . ويسقط شيء من المهر ويقع الطلاق البائن بقوله إذا نوى ولا دخل لقبولها حتى إذا نوى الزوج الطلاق ولم تقبل المرأة يقع البائن، وإن قال لم أرد الطلاق لا يقع ويصدق قضاء وديانة بخلاف قوله خالعتك فقالت قبلت يقع الطلاق والبراءة ا.هـ. وحاصله أن الفرق بين «خالعتك» من وجهين: الأول أن خلعتك لا يتوقف على القبول بخلاف «خالعتك». الثاني لا يبرأ في الأول ويبرأ في الثاني فلذا قال في الكتاب: حتى لو خالعها بصيغة المفاعلة. الثاني أن يصرح بنفي العوض فيه كما لو قال لها اخلعي نفسك مني بغير شيء ففعلت وقبل الزوج صح بغير شيء لأنه صريح في عدم المال ووقوع البائن؛ كذا في البزازية. يعني فلا يبرأ كل منهما عن حق صاحبه كما لا يخفى الثالث أن يقع ببدل على الزوج . قال في البزازية قال الإمام في الأسرار: يجوز الخلع ولا يجوز بدل المال. وقال بعضهم: يجوز والمختار الجواز وطريقه أن يحمل على الاستثناء من المهر لأن الخلع يوجب براءته من المهر فكأنه قال إلا قدراً من المهر فإنه لا يسقط عني فإن لم يكن عليه مهر يجعل كان ذلك القدر استثنى عن نفقة العدة، فإن زاد على نفقة العدة يجعل كأنه زاد على مهرها ذلك القدر قبل الخلع ثم خالع تصحيحاً للخلع بقدر الإمكان ا هـ. وبه علم حكم ما إذا خالعها واشترطت عليه أن يدفع لها بعض المهر فإنه صحيح. الرابع أن يقع بشرط أن يكون المهر لولدها أو لأجنبي . قال في البزازية : خالعها على أن يجعل صداقها لولدها أو لأجنبي جاز والمهر للزوج لا لغيره ا هـ . وإن سميا المهر فإن كان مقبوضاً رجع بجميعه وإلا سقط عنه كله مطلقاً في الأحوال كلها. وفي البزازية : خلع زوجته على أن ترد عليه جميع ما قبضت منه وكانت وهبته أو باعته من إنسان ولم ترد ذلك عليه رجع عليها بقيمة ذلك إن عروضاً وبالمثل في المكيلات والموزونات كأنه استحق بدل الخلع فيرجع بالقيمة ا هـ. وفيها : خالعها بغير خسران يلحق الزوج إذا أبرأته عن مهرها يقع الطلاق وإلا لا لأن ارتفاع الخسران يكون بسلامة المهر له اهـ. وإن سميا بعض المهر كالعشر مثلاً فإن كان مقبوضاً . بالمسمى فقط رجع
His words: (And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He said to her 'Khala'tuka' etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It should be that if he said to her 'I am free from your marriage', it occurs. And something of the mahr is dropped and irrevocable divorce (bain) occurs by his words if he intended, and there is no role for her acceptance. So if the husband intended divorce and the woman did not accept, the bain occurs. And if he said 'I did not intend divorce', it does not occur and he is believed judicially and religiously, contrary to his saying 'Khala'tuka' and she said 'I accept', then divorce and release occur. The summary is that the difference between 'Khala'tuka' has two aspects: first, 'Khala'tuka' does not depend on acceptance unlike 'Khala'tuka'. Second, there is no release in the first, and release in the second. Hence he said in the book: even if he made khul' with her using the mutual form (mufa'ala). Second: that he explicitly negates compensation in it, as if he said to her 'Divorce yourself from me for nothing', and she did so and the husband accepted, it is valid without compensation because it is explicit in the absence of wealth, and occurrence of bain. Like this in al-Bazzaziyyah. Meaning, neither is released from the right of the other, as is not hidden. Third: that it occurs with a substitute upon the husband. He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: al-Imam said in al-Asrar: khul' is permissible but the substitute of wealth is not permissible. And some said: it is permissible, and the chosen is permissibility, and its method is to interpret it as an exception from the mahr, because khul' necessitates his release from the mahr, so it is as if he said except an amount of the mahr that is not dropped from me. If there is no mahr upon him, that amount is considered as excepted from the 'iddah maintenance. If it exceeds the 'iddah maintenance, it is considered as if that amount was added to her mahr before the khul', then he made khul' to validate the khul' as much as possible. And by this the ruling is known for when he makes khul' with her and she stipulates that he pay her part of the mahr: it is valid. Fourth: that it occurs with the condition that the mahr be for her child or a stranger. He said in al-Bazzaziyyah: He made khul' with her on condition that he make her dower for her child or a stranger – it is valid, and the mahr is for the husband, not for others. And if they specified the mahr, if it was received, he takes it all back; otherwise it is dropped from him entirely in all situations. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: He made khul' with his wife on condition that she return to him all that she received from him, and she had gifted it or sold it to someone and did not return it to him – he can claim from her its value if it was goods, and the like in measurable and weighable items, as if she owed the substitute of khul', so he claims the value. And in it: He made khul' with her 'without loss to the husband' – if she released him from her mahr, the divorce occurs, otherwise not, because the absence of loss is by the mahr being safe for him. And if they specified part of the mahr, like a tenth for example, if it was received, he only gets back the specified amount.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the legal differences between two wordings for khul': 'khala'tuka' (I have divorced you in khul') and 'khala'tuka' (the mutual form, I have made khul' with you). The author explains that 'khala'tuka' is a unilateral declaration that does not require the wife's acceptance; if the husband intends divorce, it takes effect as an irrevocable divorce (bain), and he is believed if he denies intent. In contrast, 'khala'tuka' (with mufa'ala) requires the wife's acceptance (qabool) and results in both divorce and release from financial obligations (like the mahr). The passage then discusses various scenarios: (1) when compensation is explicitly negated, the khul' is valid without any money changing hands; (2) when a specific substitute is placed on the husband (e.g., he agrees to pay something), it can be valid if interpreted as an exception from the mahr or from 'iddah maintenance, a technique to uphold the transaction; (3) when the mahr is assigned to a third party, it is valid but the mahr remains with the husband; (4) when the mahr is specified, the husband recovers it if already given, otherwise it is dropped. The overall principle is that the wording and conditions dictate the legal outcome.

Key Terms
خلعتك (khala'tuka): First person singular verb meaning 'I have divorced you in khul'' (unilateral form, without mufa'ala).
خالعتك (khala'tuka): First person singular verb (mutual form, with mufa'ala) meaning 'I have made khul' with you'.
بائن (bā'in): Irrevocable divorce, after which the husband cannot take back his wife except by a new marriage.
بدل (badal): Compensation paid by the wife to the husband in khul'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says 'Khala'tuka' intending divorce, and the wife does not accept. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The divorce does not occur.
B) A bain divorce occurs, and the husband must pay the mahr.
C) A bain divorce occurs, and the mahr is dropped.
D) A revocable divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi khul', wording matters: 'khala'tuka' is unilateral without release; 'khala'tuka' is bilateral with release.

Variations in Khul' Rulings: No Compensation, Substitute on Husband, and Conditions
Explaining the legal differences in wording between 'khala'tuka' and 'khala'tuka' regarding acceptance and release from mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on khul' when compensation is explicitly negated, when a substitute is placed on the husband, and when the mahr is conditioned for a third party.

Core Idea
Khul' with explicit negation of compensation is valid; a substitute on the husband can be validated by interpreting it as an exception from mahr or 'iddah maintenance.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues beyond the core difference to address several practical scenarios. This lesson focuses on the variations: when the husband says 'divorce yourself for nothing', when he agrees to pay a substitute, and when the mahr is assigned to someone else.

Guided Path
1
Scenario 1: Explicit negation of compensation
If the husband says 'Divorce yourself from me for nothing' and the wife does so and he accepts, the khul' is valid without any money changing hands. Both parties remain entitled to their rights (e.g., mahr is not dropped).
This is sahih even without a badal.
2
Scenario 2: Substitute on the husband
When the husband agrees to pay something (e.g., part of the mahr), the substitute is permissible. The preferred view interprets it as an exception from the mahr or from 'iddah maintenance to validate the transaction.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the chosen view is permissibility.
3
Scenario 3: Condition that mahr be for child or stranger
If the khul' is conditioned on the mahr going to the wife's child or a stranger, the khul' is valid, but the mahr remains with the husband (it is not transferred).
The condition is ignored regarding ownership.
4
Scenario 4: Specified mahr and recovery
If they specify a mahr, the husband recovers it if already given; otherwise it is dropped. If the wife cannot return the exact item, she must pay its value or equivalent.
This governs the financial settlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Distinction between خلعتك and خالعتك in Khul'
Explaining the difference in wording and its legal effect in khul'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the legal effects of the phrases 'khala'tuki' and 'khalaktuki' in Hanafi khul', state which requires the wife's acceptance, and identify the financial consequences of each.

Core Idea
'خلعتك' effects divorce without her acceptance; 'خالعتك' requires her acceptance and discharges all financial claims.

In Hanafi fiqh, the wording used by the husband in a khul' transaction can dramatically change the outcome. The difference between saying 'I divorced you (khala'tuki)' and 'I made khul' with you (khalaktuki)' is not merely grammatical—it determines whether the wife's acceptance is needed and whether the husband is discharged from financial obligations. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq highlights this critical distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases
First, locate the two key phrases in the passage: 'خلعتك' (khala'tuki) and 'خالعتك' (khalaktuki). Note that the former is a unilateral form (I divorced you) and the latter is a mutual form (I made khul' with you).
2
Determine the legal effect of 'خلعتك'
According to the passage, when the husband says 'khala'tuki' with the intention of divorce, an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) occurs immediately. The wife's acceptance is irrelevant—the divorce takes effect even if she does not accept. However, the husband is not discharged from financial claims (some mahr is dropped, but full discharge does not occur).
If the husband later denies intent, he is believed both judicially and religiously.
3
Determine the legal effect of 'خالعتك'
If the husband says 'khalaktuki' and the wife responds with 'I accept,' then divorce and full discharge (from all financial claims) occur. Acceptance is required; without it, the khul' is not effective.
This is a bilateral contract (mu'afala).
4
Compare the two aspects
The passage summarizes two differences: (1) 'khala'tuki' does not depend on acceptance, while 'khalaktuki' does; (2) in 'khala'tuki' there is no discharge from financial claims, whereas in 'khalaktuki' there is full discharge.
These differences flow directly from the wording—unilateral vs mutual.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Consider a husband who says either phrase. If he says 'khala'tuki' intending divorce, the divorce is effective regardless of the wife's wishes. If he says 'khalaktuki' without her acceptance, nothing happens. This shows the practical importance of precise wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
«خلعتك» ويسقط شيء من المهر ويقع الطلاق البائن بقوله إذا نوى ولا دخل لقبولها حتى إذا نوى الزوج الطلاق ولم تقبل المرأة يقع البائن، وإن قال لم أرد الطلاق لا يقع ويصدق قضاء وديانة بخلاف قوله خالعتك فقالت قبلت يقع الطلاق والبراءة ا.هـ. وحاصله أن الفرق بين «خالعتك» من وجهين: الأول أن خلعتك لا يتوقف على القبول بخلاف «خالعتك». الثاني لا يبرأ في الأول ويبرأ في الثاني فلذا قال في الكتاب: حتى لو خالعها بصيغة المفاعلة.
‘I divorced you (khala'tuki)’ — and some of the mahr is dropped, and an irrevocable divorce occurs by his statement if he intends it, and there is no role for her acceptance. So if the husband intends divorce and the woman does not accept, the irrevocable divorce occurs. And if he says, ‘I did not intend divorce,’ it does not occur, and he is believed judicially and religiously. Contrary to when he says, ‘I made khul' with you (khalaktuki),’ and she says, ‘I accept,’ then divorce and discharge occur. End. The summary is that the difference between ‘khala'tuki’ and ‘khalaktuki’ is in two aspects: First, ‘khala'tuki’ does not depend on acceptance, unlike ‘khalaktuki’. Second, in the former there is no discharge, and in the latter there is discharge. Hence the author said: So if he makes khul' with her using the mutual form (mu'afala).
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage clarifies a key distinction in the wording of khul'. When the husband says 'khala'tuki' (I have freed you / divorced you) without mentioning a financial consideration, this is treated as a direct pronouncement of irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) that takes effect immediately upon his utterance if he had the intention of divorce. Importantly, the wife's acceptance is irrelevant; the divorce occurs even if she does not agree. If the husband later claims he did not intend divorce, he is believed both in court and religiously, because the wording is ambiguous. In contrast, if he uses the mutual form 'khalaktuki' (I have made khul' with you) and she responds with acceptance, the divorce and discharge (from financial obligations) occur together. This distinction hinges on the fact that 'khala'tuki' is a unilateral divorce, while 'khalaktuki' is a bilateral contract requiring offer and acceptance.

Key Terms
خلعتك (khala'tuki): A unilateral pronouncement of divorce by the husband implying khul' without specifying compensation; its effect is irrevocable divorce with no need for acceptance.
خالعتك (khalaktuki): The mutual form of khul' (bare'at) that requires offer and acceptance; it results in divorce and discharge from financial claims.
البائن (al-ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that does not allow remarriage without a new contract and husband's consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a husband says 'khala'tuki' (خلعتك) with the intention of divorce, but the wife does not accept?
A) The divorce does not occur because acceptance is required.
B) An irrevocable divorce occurs despite her non-acceptance.
C) The husband is believed if he later says he did not intend divorce.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi khul', the unilateral 'خلعتك' effects divorce without the wife's consent, while the mutual 'خالعتك' requires her acceptance and also discharges financial claims.

Validity of Khul' with Husband Paying Compensation
Explaining the third scenario of khul' and its validity via istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that khul' is valid when the husband pays compensation, and explain the interpretive method (haml) that validates it.

Core Idea
Khul' with husband paying compensation is valid — the payment is treated as an exception from mahr or iddah maintenance.

The typical khul' involves the wife paying compensation to the husband. But what if the husband pays the wife? This lesson resolves an apparent contradiction within the Hanafi school and explains the mechanism (haml) that makes such a khul' valid, using istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
Note that some early Hanafis disallowed khul' with the husband paying compensation, while others allowed it. The chosen view (mukhtar) is permissibility.
The dispute is intra-madhhab, not inter-madhhab.
2
Understand the interpretive method
The compensation is interpreted as an exception (istithna) from the mahr or iddah maintenance, so the husband is not actually paying extra — he is simply retaining part of what he would otherwise owe.
This is based on istihsan, not qiyas.
3
Apply the method to cases
If no mahr exists, the compensation is treated as an exception from the iddah maintenance. If it exceeds the iddah maintenance, it is considered as if the husband increased the mahr before the khul'.
This ensures the khul' is valid 'as much as possible.'
4
Confirm the ruling
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that such khul' is valid (sahih). For example, if the wife stipulates that the husband pay her part of the mahr, it is valid.
The compensation becomes an obligation on the husband, not a gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث أن يقع ببدل على الزوج . قال في البزازية قال الإمام في الأسرار: يجوز الخلع ولا يجوز بدل المال. وقال بعضهم: يجوز والمختار الجواز وطريقه أن يحمل على الاستثناء من المهر لأن الخلع يوجب براءته من المهر فكأنه قال إلا قدراً من المهر فإنه لا يسقط عني فإن لم يكن عليه مهر يجعل كان ذلك القدر استثنى عن نفقة العدة، فإن زاد على نفقة العدة يجعل كأنه زاد على مهرها ذلك القدر قبل الخلع ثم خالع تصحيحاً للخلع بقدر الإمكان ا هـ. وبه علم حكم ما إذا خالعها واشترطت عليه أن يدفع لها بعض المهر فإنه صحيح. الرابع أن يقع بشرط أن يكون المهر لولدها أو لأجنبي . قال في البزازية : خالعها على أن يجعل صداقها لولدها أو لأجنبي جاز والمهر للزوج لا لغيره ا هـ . وإن سميا المهر فإن كان مقبوضاً رجع بجميعه وإلا سقط عنه كله مطلقاً في الأحوال كلها. وفي البزازية : خلع زوجته على أن ترد عليه جميع ما قبضت منه وكانت وهبته أو باعته من إنسان ولم ترد ذلك عليه رجع عليها بقيمة ذلك إن عروضاً وبالمثل في المكيلات والموزونات كأنه استحق بدل الخلع فيرجع بالقيمة ا هـ. وفيها : خالعها بغير خسران يلحق الزوج إذا أبرأته عن مهرها يقع الطلاق وإلا لا لأن ارتفاع الخسران يكون بسلامة المهر له اهـ. وإن سميا بعض المهر كالعشر مثلاً فإن كان مقبوضاً . بالمسمى فقط رجع الطلاق ولا يسقط به شيء ا هـ . وما اعترضه بعضهم من مخالفته لما مر عن شرح الوقاية فهو ساقط لأن عبارة الوقاية مصرحة بالعوض حيث قال بكذا بخلاف عبارة النهر قوله : (يقع الطلاق والبراءة ا هـ) قال في الشرنبلالية وباقي عبارة البزازية أن عليه مهر وإن لم يكن عليه مهر يجب رد ما ساق إليها من المهر لأن المال مذكور عرفاً قوله : (الأول) إن خلعتك لا يتوقف على القبول) أي إذا لم يكن بمقابلة مال وإلا توقف كما قدمه عند قوله والواقع به وبالطلاق على مال طلاق بائن». قوله : ( يجعل كأن ذلك القدر استثنى من نفقة العدة أي إذا كان خالعها على نفقة العدة يجعل ما شرطه على نفسه لها استثناء من النفقة فتسقط النفقة عنه إلا هذا القدر منها، أما إذا لم ينص في إن كان بعد الدخول وسلم لها الباقي وبنصفه فقط إن كان قبله وإن لم يكن مقبوضاً سقط الكل مطلقاً المسمى بحكم الشرط والباقي بحكم لفظ الخلع . وإن سميا مالاً آخر غير المهر فله المسمى وبرى كل منهما مطلقاً في الأحوال كلها.
Third: That it occurs with compensation on the husband. Al-Bazzaziyya says: Al-Imam said in al-Asrar: Khul' is permissible but giving financial compensation (to the wife) is not permissible. And some said it is permissible, and the chosen view is permissibility, and its method is that it is interpreted as an exception from the mahr because khul' causes his exoneration from the mahr, so it is as if he said: except an amount of the mahr that is not dropped from me. If he has no mahr upon him, that amount is considered as an exception from the iddah maintenance. If it exceeds the iddah maintenance, it is considered as if he increased her mahr by that amount before the khul' then made khul', to validate the khul' as much as possible. And by this the ruling is known for when he makes khul' with her and she stipulates that he pay her part of the mahr: it is valid. Fourth: That it occurs with the condition that the mahr be for her child or a stranger. Al-Bazzaziyya says: If he makes khul' with her on condition that her dower be for her child or a foreigner, it is valid and the mahr is for the husband, not for anyone else. And if they specify the mahr, then if it was received (by the wife), he gets all of it back; otherwise it is dropped from him entirely in all circumstances. And in al-Bazzaziyya: If he makes khul' with his wife on condition that she return to him all that she received from him, but she had gifted or sold it to someone and did not return it, he can claim its value (if it is goods) or the like (if weighed or measured) from her, as if she became liable for the khul' compensation. And in it: If he makes khul' with her 'without loss to the husband' such that she absolves him of her mahr, the divorce occurs, otherwise not, because the removal of loss is by the safety of the mahr for him. And if they specify part of the mahr, like a tenth, if it was received, he only gets the specified amount back; divorce occurs and nothing else is dropped. And what some objected to regarding contradiction with what passed from Sharh al-Wiqaya is baseless because the wording of al-Wiqaya explicitly mentions consideration. The words: (Divorce and discharge occur). Al-Sharnabaliyya said: The rest of al-Bazzaziyya's words indicate that he owes the mahr, and if he has no mahr, he must return what he gave her because money is conventionally mentioned. His words: (First: 'khala'tuki' does not depend on acceptance) i.e., when it is not in exchange for money; otherwise it depends, as stated earlier at his words: 'And what occurs with it and with divorce on money is a ba'in divorce.' His words: (It is considered as if that amount is excepted from the iddah maintenance) i.e., if he made khul' with her on the iddah maintenance, what he stipulated on himself for her is treated as an exception from the maintenance, so the maintenance falls except that amount. If he did not stipulate it, then if after consummation, he gives her the rest; if before, only half; if not received, everything falls—the specified part due to the condition, the rest due to the wording of khul'. And if they specify a property other than the mahr, he gets what was specified and both are absolutely discharged in all cases.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth scenarios of khul'. The third is when the husband is obligated to pay something to the wife (badal 'ala al-zawj). The author resolves an apparent contradiction: some early scholars said khul' with compensation on the husband is invalid because the husband should receive, not give. But the adopted view (mukhtar) is that it is valid, by interpreting the payment as an exception from the mahr or iddah maintenance. For example, if he makes khul' and agrees to pay her part of the mahr, it is valid. The fourth scenario is making khul' conditionally that the mahr goes to the wife's child or a third party; the ruling is that it is valid but the mahr remains the husband's liability (he must pay it to the wife, not to the third party). Then the text details rules for when the specified compensation is part or all of the mahr, distinguishing between before and after consummation. If the mahr is already received by the wife, she must return it; otherwise it is dropped. If they specify another property, each is discharged. Also, from al-Bazzaziyya, if the wife fails to return property she sold, she must pay its value or the like. And the condition 'without loss to the husband' means if she absolves him of the mahr, khul' is valid; otherwise not, because the absence of loss requires the mahr to be safe for him.

Key Terms
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The compensation paid in exchange for khul', which may be from the wife to the husband or vice versa.
الخسران (al-khusran): Loss; in context, khul' 'without loss' means the husband does not suffer financially, i.e., the wife absolves him of the mahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a husband makes khul' with his wife and agrees to pay her part of the mahr, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The khul' is invalid because the husband should not pay.
B) The khul' is valid, and the payment is treated as an exception from the mahr.
C) The khul' is valid only if the payment exceeds the mahr.
D) The khul' is invalid unless the wife returns her mahr.

Key Takeaway
Khul' with the husband paying compensation is valid by interpreting the payment as an exception from the mahr or iddah maintenance.

Conditions and Effects of Compensation in Khul'
Explaining the fourth scenario of khul' and detailed rules on compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules regarding compensation in khul' when it is conditioned for a third party, or when it involves the mahr or other property.

Core Idea
In khul', compensation conditions regarding third parties are invalid, but the khul' itself remains valid.

The compensation in khul' can be specified in various ways: conditioned for a third party, part of the mahr, or other property. This lesson clarifies the rulings in each case, emphasizing that the fundamental validity of khul' is preserved by adjusting the compensation terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The fourth scenario: khul' conditioned on the mahr going to the wife's child or a stranger. Determine whether the condition affects the validity of the khul'.
This is a conditional khul' regarding the recipient of the compensation.
2
Rule on the condition
The condition regarding the recipient is invalid; the mahr remains the husband's obligation to the wife, not to the third party.
The khul' is valid, but the condition is void.
3
Distinguish based on compensation type
If the compensation is part or all of the mahr, apply rules based on whether the mahr was received. If the compensation is other property, each party is discharged of the specified amount.
Important: Whether the mahr was actually paid (qabd) affects the outcome.
4
Apply the 'no loss' condition
If the khul' is conditioned on 'no loss' (la khusran), it is interpreted as the wife absolving the husband of the mahr. If she does, khul' occurs; otherwise not.
The absence of loss means the mahr is safe for the husband.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If a husband makes khul' with his wife on condition that the mahr be paid to her child, what is the ruling regarding the mahr?

Key Takeaway

24 Khul' Scenarios and Effect of Gross Ignorance
Enumeration of khul' scenarios and ruling on gross ignorance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the 24 khul' scenarios and state the ruling when the compensation specification is invalid due to gross ignorance.

Core Idea
When khul' compensation is grossly uncertain, the specification is void but the khul' remains valid.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq systematically lists the possible khul' arrangements and clarifies when compensation terms are invalid due to ignorance. Understanding these permutations helps the jurist judge khul' contracts correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the variables in khul' compensation
The text lists six categories of compensation: 1) silence about compensation, 2) negating compensation, 3) stipulating on husband, 4) stipulating on wife, 5) her mahr, 6) part of her mahr. Each category has two possibilities: compensation received or not, and each of those has two: before or after consummation. That yields 6 x 2 x 2 = 24 cases.
The multiplication is 6 categories × 2 (received vs not) × 2 (before/after) = 24.
2
Distinguish valid specification from gross ignorance
The specification is valid if the thing is known, existing, valuable, or has a remediable defect (e.g., 'a Herawi cloth'). It is invalid if the ignorance is gross (e.g., 'a cloth' without specification) or the compensation depends on a risky future yield (e.g., this year's produce) or is nonexistent.
Gross ignorance (فحشت الجهالة) makes the term void; remediable ignorance (جهالة مستدركة) is acceptable.
3
State the ruling when specification is invalid
If the specification is void, the khul' itself remains valid, but the wife must return the mahr she had received, as if no specific compensation was agreed.
The khul' is not invalidated; only the compensation term is void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبما قررناه ظهر أن الوجوه أربعة وعشرون لأنه إما أن يسكتا عن البدل أو ينفي أو يشترط على الزوج أو عليها أو مهرها أو بعضه وكل على وجهين إما أن يكون مقبوضاً أو لا، وكل على وجهين إما أن يكون قبل الدخول أو بعده. هذا إن كان المسمى معلوماً موجوداً متقوماً أو محمولاً جهالة مستدركة كثوب هروي أو مروي. وإن فحشت الجهالة كمطلق ثوب أو تمكن الخطر بأن خلعها على ما يثمر نخلها العام أو على ما في البيت وليس فيه شيء بطلت التسمية وردت ما قبضت من المهر؛ كذا في البزازية.
And by what we have established, it becomes apparent that the cases are twenty-four: because either they are silent about the compensation, or they negate it, or they stipulate it on the husband, or on her, or her mahr, or part of it. And each is of two types: either it is received or not, and each is of two types: either before consummation or after. This is if the specified thing is known, existing, valuable, or bears an ignorable defect that can be remedied, like a Herawi or Marawi cloth. But if the ignorance is gross, like an unspecified cloth, or the danger is possible, like if he makes khul' for what her palm tree will produce this year, or for what is in the house but there is nothing in it, then the specification becomes void and she returns what she received of the mahr; similarly in al-Bazzaziyya.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive categorization of khul' scenarios. The author identifies 24 distinct cases by combining the following factors: the nature of the compensation (none, negated, stipulated on husband, on wife, the mahr itself, or part of the mahr), whether the compensation was actually received by the wife, and whether the khul' occurs before or after consummation. This careful enumeration shows the thoroughness of Hanafi fiqh. However, these cases assume the specified compensation is valid: known, existing, and legally valuable. If the compensation is grossly uncertain (e.g., 'a cloth' without specification) or depends on a risky future yield (like produce of a palm tree in the current year), or if it is nonexistent (like 'what is in the house' when empty), the specification is void. In such cases, the khul' is still valid but the wife must return the mahr she had received, as if no specific compensation was agreed upon.

Key Terms
الوجوه (al-wujuh): The possible legal scenarios or cases.
الجهالة المستدركة (al-jahalah al-mustadrakah): Ignorance that can be remedied or compensated; a known defect that can be priced.
فحشت الجهالة (fahushat al-jahalah): Gross ignorance or uncertainty in the specification that renders the transaction void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband makes khul' with his wife for 'what is in this box' but the box is empty, what is the ruling?
A) The khul' is invalid because the compensation is unknown.
B) The khul' is valid and she gets nothing.
C) The khul' is valid but the compensation term is void; she must return the mahr she had received.
D) The khul' is valid and she keeps her mahr.

Key Takeaway
Khul' remains valid even if the compensation specification is void due to gross ignorance; the wife must return the mahr she had received.

The Effect of Khul' on Mahr: When Does the Wife Return the Mahr?
Ruling on effect of khul' on mahr with exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the return of mahr in khul' and distinguish when the wife is absolved from the mahr debt.

Core Idea
In khul', if the consideration is the mahr itself and it was received, the wife must return it and is not absolved.

Khul' is a form of divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for a payment. A common misconception is that khul' automatically cancels all marital financial rights. In this lesson, we examine the rule regarding the mahr (dower) and how its treatment depends on whether the consideration is the mahr itself or other property, and whether the wife has already taken possession of it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Type of Consideration
Determine whether the consideration specified in the khul' is the mahr (or part of it) or some other property.
The passage distinguishes between mahr and other property as the consideration.
2
Check Receipt (Qabd)
Verify if the wife has already taken possession (qabd) of the consideration. If the consideration is the mahr and it was received, the ruling changes.
Qabd is a key factor in liability.
3
Apply the Ruling on Mahr
If the consideration is the mahr and it was received, the wife must return it and is not absolved from the mahr debt. If the consideration is other property, she keeps the mahr and is absolved of it.
The text: 'إذا خالعها على مهرها أو بعضه وكان مقبوضاً فإنها ترده ولا تبرأ'
4
Understand the Exception to 'Khul' Drops All Rights'
The common statement that khul' drops all rights is not absolute; it must be excepted when the consideration is the mahr and received. In that case, the mahr is not dropped.
The author clarifies that the exception applies only to the mahr when it serves as consideration.
5
Consider Consummation
If the khul' is after consummation and the consideration is the mahr and not received, the entire mahr drops? Actually the text says: 'إذا كان بعد الدخول وسلم لها الباقي' (if after consummation, he gives her the remainder). This refers to the part of mahr not taken as consideration. The details of before/after consummation are more systematically covered in the 24 aspects.
For this lesson, focus on the core rule of return when consideration is mahr and received.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إن كان بعد الدخول وسلم لها الباقي وبنصفه فقط إن كان قبله وإن لم يكن مقبوضاً سقط الكل مطلقاً المسمى بحكم الشرط والباقي بحكم لفظ الخلع . وإن سميا مالاً آخر غير المهر فله المسمى وبرى كل منهما مطلقاً في الأحوال كلها. وبما قررناه ظهر أن قولهم «الخلع يسقط كل الحقوق» ليس في جميع الصور ويستثنى منه ما إذا خالعها على مهرها أو بعضه وكان مقبوضاً فإنها ترده ولا تبرأ ومقتضى إطلاقهم البراءة إلا أن يقال إن مرادهم البراءة عن سائر الحقوق ما عدا بدل الخلع والمهر بدل الخلع فلا تبرأ عنه كما لو كان مالاً آخر. وبما قررناه ظهر أن الوجوه أربعة وعشرون لأنه إما أن يسكتا عن البدل أو ينفي أو يشترط على الزوج أو عليها أو مهرها أو بعضه وكل على وجهين إما أن يكون مقبوضاً أو لا، وكل على وجهين إما أن يكون قبل الدخول أو بعده. هذا إن كان المسمى معلوماً موجوداً متقوماً أو محمولاً جهالة مستدركة كثوب هروي أو مروي. وإن فحشت الجهالة كمطلق ثوب أو تمكن الخطر بأن خلعها على ما يثمر نخلها العام أو على ما في البيت وليس فيه شيء بطلت التسمية وردت ما قبضت من المهر؛ كذا في البزازية. وقدمناه.
If it was after consummation and he gives her the remainder, and only half if it was before, and if it was not received, the whole drops absolutely: what was named by virtue of the condition, and the remainder by virtue of the word khul'. If they name some property other than the mahr, he gets what was named, and each is absolved absolutely in all circumstances. By what we have established, it becomes clear that their statement 'khul' drops all rights' is not in all cases; an exception is when he made khul' with her on her mahr or part of it and it was received, for then she returns it and is not absolved. The apparent meaning of their absolute statement is absolution, unless it is said that they mean absolution from all other rights except the consideration of khul', and the mahr is the consideration of khul', so she is not absolved from it, just as if it were other property. By what we have established, it becomes clear that the aspects are twenty-four: either they are silent about the consideration, or negate it, or stipulate it on the husband, or on her, or her mahr, or part of it; each can be in two ways: either received or not; each in two ways: either before consummation or after. This is if what is named is known, existing, valuable, or carried with a remediable ignorance, like a Herati or Marwazi cloth. If the ignorance is excessive, like an absolute cloth, or there is risk, as when he makes khul' with her on what her palm trees produce that year, or on what is in the house and there is nothing in it, then the naming is invalid and she returns what she received of the mahr; thus in al-Bazzaziyya. We have already presented it.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effects of khul' (divorce by redemption) regarding the mahr and other consideration. The author explains that if the khul' consideration is the mahr or part of it and it was received (qabd), the wife must return it and she is not absolved from the mahr. If the consideration is something other than the mahr, then the husband gets that property and both are absolved entirely. The author then clarifies that the common saying 'khul' drops all rights' is not absolute; it applies only when the consideration is not the mahr. He then enumerates 24 possible scenarios based on three binary variables: type of consideration (six options), whether received or not, and before or after consummation. Finally, he discusses cases of excessive ignorance (jahalah fahishah) or risk (khatar) in the consideration, which invalidate the naming and require the wife to return any mahr she received.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for property or other consideration.
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The property or consideration given by the wife in exchange for the divorce.
المسمى (al-musamma): The named consideration in the khul' contract.
قبض (qabd): Physical receipt or taking possession of the consideration.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance or uncertainty about the consideration; if excessive, invalidates the naming.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In khul', if the consideration is the mahr itself and it has been received (qabd) by the wife, what is the ruling?
A) She keeps the mahr and is absolved of all claims.
B) She must return the mahr and is not absolved of the mahr debt.
C) She returns the mahr but is absolved of all other claims.
D) The khul' is invalid because the mahr cannot be consideration.

Key Takeaway
When the mahr serves as the consideration in khul' and the wife has received it, she must return it and remains liable for the mahr debt.

The 24 Permutations of Khul' and Invalidity Due to Excessive Ignorance
Enumeration of 24 aspects and condition of valid naming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the 24 aspects of khul' and identify when excessive ignorance (jahalah fahishah) invalidates the naming.

Core Idea
Khul' permutations: six consideration options × (received or not) × (before or after consummation) = 24; excessive ignorance nullifies the naming.

The Hanafi jurists have systematically enumerated all possible scenarios of khul' based on three binary variables: the type of consideration, whether it was received, and whether the divorce occurred before or after consummation. This lesson breaks down the 24 aspects and explains the crucial condition that the consideration must be known and free from excessive ignorance or risk.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Six Consideration Options
The passage lists six possibilities: they are silent about the consideration, or negate it, or stipulate it on the husband, or on the wife, or on her mahr, or on part of the mahr.
These are the 'first dimension' of permutations.
2
Add the Receipt Dimension
For each of the six options, the consideration may be either received (qabd) or not received. This doubles the count to 12.
Qabd affects liability as seen in Lesson 1.
3
Add the Consummation Dimension
For each of the 12, the divorce may be before or after consummation (dukhul). This doubles again to 24.
Consummation affects the default mahr rules but not the validity of consideration directly.
4
Note Condition for Valid Naming
The enumeration assumes the consideration is validly named. For the naming to be valid, the consideration must be known (ma'loom), existing (mawjood), valuable (mutaqawwim), or if a cloth, specified to a degree that remedies ignorance (e.g., 'Herati' or 'Marwazi' cloth).
If the ignorance is excessive (jahalah fahishah), the naming invalidates.
5
Identify Excessive Ignorance and Risk
Excessive ignorance includes describing the consideration merely as 'a cloth' (muthlaq thawb), or a risky item like 'what my palm trees will produce this year' (if uncertain) or 'what is in the house' if the house is empty. In such cases, the naming is invalid (batalat al-tasmiyah), and the wife must return any mahr she received.
The contract of khul' itself may remain valid, but the consideration reverts to the mahr default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does Talaq on Property Drop the Mahr?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq on property and mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on whether talaq on property drops the mahr and identify the fatwa position.

Core Idea
In talaq on property, the Sahibayn drop only the named amount; Imam has two narrations — the fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

Khul' and talaq on property are both forms of divorce involving payment, but they differ in who initiates. The key legal question is whether talaq on property, like khul', drops all marital rights (including the mahr) or only the amount paid. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi disagreement on this issue, examining the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and the later fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish khul' and talaq on property
Identify who initiates each: khul' is initiated by the wife, talaq on property by the husband. This initial difference leads to different rulings in the Hanafi school.
The source text explicitly restricts the discussion to khul' and mubara'ah, excluding talaq on property from the same ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
Imam Abu Hanifa has two narrations: (1) talaq on property drops all rights like khul', (2) it drops only the named amount. The Sahibayn consistently hold that it drops only the named amount.
The Sahibayn position is the same for both khul' and talaq on property: only the consideration is dropped.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the view that it drops all rights is followed, the wife is absolved from the mahr; if only the named amount is dropped, the mahr remains due.
This difference affects real settlements: a wife may lose her mahr if the wrong view is applied.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text states that the fatwa is upon the view of al-Balkhi's opponents, meaning the view that explicit talaq for an amount does not cause absolution from the mahr. This is the Sahibayn's position and the correct narration from Imam.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه بقي هنا صورة وهي ما في البزازية : اختلفت مع زوجها على مهرها ونفقة عدتها على أن الزوج يرد عليها عشرين درهماً . صح ولزم الزوج عشرون دليله ما ذكر في الأصل خالعت على دار على أن الزوج يرد عليها ألفاً لا شفعة فيه، وفيه دليل على أن إيجاب بدل الخلع عليه يصح. وفي صلح القدوري : ادعت عليه نكاحاً وصالحها على مال بذله لها لم يجز، وفي بعض النسخ جاز والرواية الأولى تخالف المتقدم والتوفيق أنها إذا خالعت على بدل يجوز إيجاب البدل على الزوج أيضاً ويكون مقابلاً ببدل الخلع، وكذا إذا لم يذكر نفقة العدة في الخلع ويكون تقديراً لنفقة العدة، أما إذا خالعت على نفقة العدة ولم تذكر عوضاً آخر ينبغي أن لا يجب بدل الخلع على الزوج وقد ذكرنا ما فيه من الوجه ا هـ . قيد بالخلع والمبارأة لأن الطلاق على مال لا يسقط شيئاً مما يتعلق بالنكاح في ظاهر الرواية وصححه الشارحون وقاضيخان وفي البزازية والولوالجية وعليه الفتوى بعد أن حكي الخلع على نفقة العدة فإنها لا تسقط عنه لكن يجعل ذلك القدر تقديراً لنفقة العدة كما سيأتي عن البزازية أيضاً في آخر الصفحة الثانية قوله : (وصححه الشارحون وقاضيخان) ذكر في النهر عن قاضيخان خلاف هذا فإنه قال : وذكر القاضي أنه عندهما كالخلع والصحيح من الروايتين عند الإمام كقولهما اهـ. :قلت الذي في قاضيخان موافق لما في البحر فإنه قال : فإن طلقها بمال أو بمهرها فعندهما الجواب فيه كالجواب في الخلع عندهما وعن أبي حنيفة فيه روايتان في رواية الجواب فيه ما ذكرنا في الخلع عنده . وفي رواية الجواب فيه ما قلنا لأبي يوسف ومحمد وهو الصحيح ومعناه أن الخلع عند الإمام مسقط لكل حق، وعندهما مسقط لما سمى فقط كما صرح به في الملتقى وغيره. وحينئذ فالطلاق بمال حكمه عندهما حكم الخلع عندهما أي أنه لا يسقط إلا المسمى دون المهر، وعنده يوجب أن فيه روايتين عن الإمام وأن عندهما هو كالخلع. وفي موضع منها: طلقها على ألف قبل الدخول ولها عليه ثلاثة آلاف تسقط ألف وخمسمائة بالطلاق قبل الدخول وبقي عليه ألف وخمسمائة وتقاصا بألف ولا ترجع عليه بخمسمائة عند البلخي وترجع عند غيره، وعليه الفتوى بناء على أن صريح الطلاق بقدر من المال هل يوجب البراءة من المهر عند الإمام أم لا، فالبلخي يوجبه وغيره لا ا هـ .
Then know that here remains a case, namely that in al-Bazzaziyya: She disputed with her husband over her mahr and the nafaqah of her iddah on condition that the husband returns to her twenty dirhams. It is valid and the twenty dirhams are obligatory on the husband. Its proof is what was mentioned in al-Asl: she made khul' on a house on condition that the husband returns to her a thousand, with no pre-emption right in it. This contains evidence that imposing the consideration of khul' on the husband is valid. In Sulh al-Quduri: She claimed marriage from him and he settled with her for property he gave her; it is not permissible. In some copies, it is allowed, and the first narration contradicts what preceded. The reconciliation is that when she makes khul' for consideration, it is permissible to impose the consideration on the husband also, and it is in exchange for the consideration of khul', and similarly if she does not mention nafaqah of iddah in the khul', then it becomes an estimate for nafaqah of iddah. But if she makes khul' for nafaqah of iddah and does not mention another consideration, it would seem that the consideration of khul' is not obligatory on the husband, and we have mentioned the face of it. End. It is restricted to khul' and mubara'ah because talaq for property does not drop anything related to the marriage in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), and the commentators and Qadikhan corrected it, and in al-Bazzaziyya and al-Walwalijiyya, and upon it is the fatwa after relating the khul' for nafaqah of iddah, for it does not drop from him, but that amount is made an estimate for nafaqah of iddah, as will come from al-Bazzaziyya also at the end of the second page. His saying: (And the commentators and Qadikhan corrected it) – in al-Nahr there is something from Qadikhan contrary to this, for he said: Al-Qadi mentioned that according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is like khul', and the correct of the two narrations from Imam is like their saying. I say: What is in Qadikhan agrees with what is in al-Bahr, for he said: If he divorced her for property or her mahr, then according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) the answer in it is like the answer in khul' according to them, and from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations. In one narration, the answer in it is what we mentioned in khul' according to him. In another narration, the answer in it is what we said for Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and that is the correct one. Its meaning is that khul' according to Imam drops every right, but according to them it drops only what was specified, as is clarified in al-Multaqa and others. In that case, talaq for property, according to them, has the same ruling as khul' according to them, i.e., it drops only the named amount, not the mahr. And according to him (Imam), there are two narrations, and according to them it is like khul'. And in one place: He divorced her for a thousand before consummation, and she has three thousand against him; one thousand five hundred is dropped by the divorce before consummation, and one thousand five hundred remains on him. They set off one thousand, and she does not have recourse against him for five hundred according to al-Balkhi, but she has recourse according to others. The fatwa is upon this, based on whether explicit talaq for an amount of money causes absolution from the mahr according to Imam or not. Al-Balkhi holds that it does, while others do not. End.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of talaq on payment (طلاق على مال) on the mahr. The author presents various views. According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, talaq on property does not drop any marital rights, unlike khul'. However, the commentators and Qadikhan correct this view, and the fatwa is based on a different understanding. The key point is that khul' according to Imam Abu Hanifa drops all rights, while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) it drops only the named consideration. For talaq on payment, there are two narrations from Abu Hanifa: one that it drops all rights like khul', and another that it drops only the named amount. The Sahibayn always rule that it drops only what is named. The author also discusses a specific case of khul' on nafaqah of iddah and the application of set-off (muqasah).

Key Terms
طلاق على مال (talaq 'ala mal): Divorce pronounced by the husband in exchange for property paid by the wife or forgo of a right.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known narrations transmitted by Imam Muhammad from Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in the six books.
براءة (bara'ah): Absolution or discharge from a debt or right.
تقاص (taqas): Set-off: mutual cancellation of debts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon position (fatwa) regarding whether talaq on property drops the mahr?
A) It drops the mahr absolutely.
B) It does not drop the mahr; only the named consideration is dropped.
C) It drops the mahr only if the wife initiates.
D) It drops the mahr only if the husband says 'khul''.

Key Takeaway
The fatwa in the Hanafi school is that talaq on property does not drop the mahr, only the named consideration, protecting the wife's right.
