Khul' with Sale Language and Its Effect on Mahr and Other Rights
Legal discussion on khul' with sale language and related rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether khul' with sale language drops the mahr, and distinguish the rulings for nafaqah of iddah, suknah, and child maintenance.

Core Idea
Khul' with sale language does not automatically drop the mahr; each right has its own rule.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides detailed rulings on the effects of khul' when expressed using sale language (lafz al-bay'). It clarifies that the mahr is not dropped unless explicitly mentioned, and then addresses several related rights: nafaqah of iddah, suknah (housing), and child maintenance. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying the Hanafi school's position on khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling on khul' with sale language
The passage states that according to Qadikhan, khul' with sale language does not drop the mahr unless it is explicitly mentioned. Another view allows dropping, but Qadikhan's is correct.
This sets the baseline for the entire discussion.
2
Examine the treatment of nafaqah of iddah
Nafaqah of iddah is a right that only becomes obligatory after divorce, so it cannot be dropped by general khul' wording. It must be explicitly stipulated to be waived. However, if included as part of a package (e.g., mahr + nafaqah), it is valid even if unknown at the time.
This is because nafaqah of iddah is not yet due at the moment of khul'.
3
Understand the ruling on suknah
Suknah (the right to reside in the marital home during iddah) cannot be dropped under any circumstances, because it involves a religious obligation. However, the wife can absolve the husband from the expense of suknah if she lives elsewhere.
The physical right to housing is non-waivable; only the financial burden can be shifted.
4
Study the rules for child maintenance and nursing
If the parties agree to waive maintenance and nursing expenses for the child, such a stipulation is valid only if a specific time period is mentioned (e.g., one year). For a suckling infant, it is valid even without a time limit, as the natural period is two years.
This protects the child's welfare while allowing flexibility for the parents.
5
Synthesize the differences between the two narrations
The passage ends with a note that in one narration khul' drops all rights, while in another it drops only the consideration explicitly named. This shows the need for caution in applying general rules.
The preferred view is that only the named consideration is dropped.

Then know that the better expression is to say that talaq on property does not drop the mahr, for it is explicitly stated in Sharh al-Wiqayah, al-Khulasa, al-Bazzaziyya, and al-Jawhara that the nafaqah that is obligatory is dropped by divorce, and they made it absolute, so it includes talaq with property and otherwise, and we will discuss it, God willing, in the Book of Nafaqat. As for khul' using the words of sale and purchase, Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: There is no absolution from the mahr except by mentioning it, unanimously, and that is correct. In al-Fatawa al-Sughra, it is corrected that there is absolution like khul', and al-Imadi chose it in al-Fusul, and he made it absolute regarding the right, so it includes the mahr, obligatory and past nafaqah, and clothing as well. As for the mut'ah, al-Bazzaziyya said: If he made khul' with her before consummation and he had not named a mahr, the mut'ah drops without mention. End. As for nafaqah of iddah, it does not enter under the general because it was not obligatory before the khul' to be dropped by it; rather, it is dropped only by explicit stipulation. End. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. Commentary
This passage addresses several specific issues related to khul' and talaq on property. First, it clarifies that the better view is that talaq on property does not drop the mahr. Second, it discusses khul' using the words of sale (bida'a) and purchase: according to Qadikhan, there is no absolution from the mahr unless it is explicitly mentioned; but there is another view that it does drop the mahr like regular khul'. Third, it covers nafaqah of iddah: it must be explicitly mentioned in the khul' to be dropped; it does not fall under general wording because it was not obligatory at the time of khul'. However, if the wife makes khul' on her mahr and nafaqah of iddah together, it is valid even though the nafaqah is unknown, because it enters as a follow-up. Settlement regarding nafaqah of iddah is valid only if the duration is known (like months). Fourth, suknah (housing) cannot be dropped at all, but the wife can absolve the husband from its expense. Fifth, regarding the child's maintenance and nursing, if a time is specified, it is valid; for a suckling infant, it is valid even without specification. Finally, the author notes that there is a narration that khul' drops all rights, and another that it drops only the named consideration.

Key Terms
لفظ البيع والشراء (lafz al-bay' wa al-shira'): Using the words of sale and purchase (e.g., 'I sold you my divorce') instead of the word 'khul''.
نفقة العدة (nafaqah al-'iddah): Maintenance during the waiting period after divorce.
سكنى (suknah): The right of the divorced wife to reside in the husband's house during iddah.
رضاع (rada'): Nursing of the child; its maintenance can be included in khul' if specified.

Key Takeaway
Khul' with sale language does not automatically drop the mahr; explicit mention is required, and suknah can never be dropped.

Khul' of a Minor: Talaq Valid, Compensation Not Binding
Commentary explaining the effect of khul' of a minor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khul‘ of a minor girl and explain why the talaq occurs while the financial compensation is not obligatory.

Core Idea
In khul' of a minor, the divorce takes effect, but the property is never owed.

This passage clarifies a common misunderstanding: when a minor is divorced by khul‘ with her own property, the divorce is valid, but she is not liable for the compensation. The commentator distinguishes between the dissolution of marriage (which occurs) and the financial obligation (which does not bind the minor). Understanding this distinction is key to many Hanafi rules on capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
The matn states that khul‘ of a minor with her property is 'not valid over her'. The commentator clarifies that this means the compensation (badal) is not binding, not that the divorce itself fails.
This distinction is crucial: talaq occurs, but no financial obligation.
2
Locate the reasoning (talil)
The text explains that the compensation is not binding because the minor has no valid financial consideration at the time of exit. The vulva (bud‘) is not appraised at this moment.
The minor lacks capacity to incur a debt for khul‘.
3
Analyze the analogy to conditional divorce
The khul‘ is treated as a suspension on the condition of acceptance, analogous to other conditional divorces (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced'). In such cases, the talaq occurs upon fulfillment of the condition, regardless of the financial aspect.
This is a qiyas (analogical reasoning) used to uphold the validity of the talaq.
4
Examine the minor's own acceptance
If the minor is rational (ʿāqila) and understands that marriage brings benefits and khul‘ removes them, her own acceptance causes the talaq to occur by consensus, but still no compensation is owed.
This exception shows that her rationality does not make her liable for payment.
5
Determine the practical effect
The husband is divorced (talaq falls) but receives no property. The marriage ends irrevocably (bā'in if wording 'khul‘', raj‘ī if wording 'talaq').
The distinction between bā'in and raj‘ī affects the possibility of remarriage without a new contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو خلع صغيرة بمالها لم يجز عليها أي لا يلزمها المال لأنه لا نظر لها فيه لعدم تقوم البضع حالة الخروج، وإنما فسرنا عدم الجواز في كلامه بعدم لزوم المال لأن الصحيح وقوع الطلاق كما في الهداية لأنه تعليق بشرط قبوله فيعتبر بالتعليق بسائر الشروط . هذا إذا قبل الأب، فإن قبلت وهي عاقلة تعقل أن النكاح جالب والخلع سالب وقع الطلاق بالاتفاق ولا يلزمها المال. وذكر صاحب المنظومة أن خلع الصغيرة بمال مع الزوج إن كان بلفظ الخلع يقع البائن، وإن كان بلفظ الطلاق يقع الرجعي. وفي جامع الفصولين : لو طلق الصبية بمال يقع رجعياً وفي الأمة بائناً إذا الطلاق بمال يصح في الأمة لكنه مؤجل يصير وفي الصبية يقع بلا مال ا هـ . . وفي جوامع الفقه : طلقها بمهرها وهي صغيرة عاقلة فقبلت وقعت طلقة ولا يبرأ وإن قبل أبوها أو أجنبي روى هشام عن محمد أنه يقع، وروى الهندواني عن محمد أنه لا يقع فلو بلغت وأجازت جاز؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وذكر الشارح ولو شرط الزوج البدل عليها توقف على قبولها إن كانت أهلاً، فإن قبلت وقع اتفاقاً ولا يلزم المال، وإن قبل الأب عنها صح في رواية لأنه نفع محض لأنها تتخلص بلا مال، ولا يصح في أخرى لأن قبولها بمعنى شرط اليمين وهو لا يحتمل النيابة وهذا هو الأصح ا هـ.
His saying: 'And if he divorces a minor girl by khul' with her property, it is not valid over her' i.e., the compensation is not obligatory upon her because she has no consideration for it due to the lack of valuation of the vulva at the time of exit. And we have interpreted 'lack of validity' in his statement as non-obligation of the compensation because the correct view is that the talaq occurs, as in al-Hidayah, because it is a suspension upon the condition of acceptance, so it is analogized to suspension upon other conditions. This is if the father accepts. If she accepts while she is rational, understanding that marriage brings and khul' removes, the talaq occurs by agreement and the compensation is not obligatory upon her. The author of al-Manẓūma stated that khul' of a minor with property from the husband: if it is in the wording of khul', it falls as bā'in, and if in the wording of talaq, it falls as raj'ī. And in Jāmi' al-Fuṣūlayn: if he divorces a minor girl with [a condition of] property, it falls as raj'ī; in the case of a slave-girl, as bā'in because talaq with property is valid in the slave-girl but it is deferred; in the minor girl it falls without property. In Jawāmi' al-Fiqh: he divorced her with her mahr while she was a minor but rational, and she accepted, one talaq falls and he is not discharged. If her father or an outsider accepted, Hishām narrated from Muḥammad that it falls, and al-Hindwānī narrated from Muḥammad that it does not fall. Then if she comes of age and ratifies, it is valid. Al-Shāriḥ said: If the husband stipulated the compensation upon her, it depends on her acceptance if she is competent. If she accepted, it occurs by agreement and the compensation is not obligatory. If the father accepted on her behalf, it is valid in one narration because it is a pure benefit as she is released without compensation, and not valid in another because her acceptance is like a condition of an oath which does not accept deputyship, and this is the most correct.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding khul' of a minor girl. The matn stated that if a husband divorces his minor wife by khul' using her own property, it is not valid over her. The commentator explains that 'not valid' here means the compensation (the property) is not obligatory on her, because at the time of khul' the marital right (buda') is not considered to have market value (since she is leaving the marriage involuntarily? The reasoning: the vulva is not appraised at the time of exit). Crucially, the talaq itself does occur, according to the correct position in al-Hidayah. This is because the khul' is a suspension on the condition of acceptance, analogous to other conditional divorces. If her father accepts the compensation, the talaq falls. If she herself accepts and she is rational enough to understand that marriage benefits and khul' removes, the talaq falls by consensus, but she is still not liable for the compensation. The author of al-Manẓuma adds nuance: if the wording is 'khul'' it is bā'in; if 'talaq' it is raj'ī. Then there is a dispute among narrations from Imam Muhammad: according to Hisham, if the father or an outsider accepts, the talaq falls; according to al-Hindwani, it does not fall unless she later ratifies upon majority. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) then states the relied-upon position: if one stipulates the compensation on her, it depends on her acceptance if she is competent; if she accepts, the talaq occurs but no compensation. If the father accepts on her behalf, one narration says it is valid (because it is a pure benefit), another says not (because acceptance involves an oath-like condition that cannot be delegated). The correct view is that the father's acceptance does not make it valid—this is the mufta bihi. The passage covers intra-Hanafi differences and the underlying principle that a minor cannot be liable for compensation in khul' because she lacks capacity to assume financial obligations at the time the marriage is dissolved.

Key Terms
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband, resulting in a bā'in divorce.
صغيرة (ṣaghīra): A minor female who has not reached puberty, lacking full legal capacity for financial transactions.
بدل (badal): The compensation paid by the wife in khul‘, usually the mahr or an agreed sum.
بائن (bā'in): An irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately without a right to take back the wife without a new marriage contract.
رجعي (raj‘ī): A revocable divorce that allows the husband to take back his wife during the waiting period (ʿidda).
تعليق (ta‘līq): Suspension of a divorce upon the occurrence of a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a minor girl is divorced by khul‘ with her property and she herself accepts (being rational), what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The talaq does not occur because the minor cannot initiate divorce.
B) The talaq occurs but the compensation is binding.
C) The talaq occurs and the compensation is not binding.
D) The talaq does not occur because the property is not valid.

Key Takeaway
In khul' of a minor, the divorce takes effect, but the minor is never liable for the compensation, even if she is rational and accepts.

The Guardian's Acceptance: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding guardian's acceptance in khul' of a minor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two narrations within the Hanafi school regarding the father's acceptance of khul‘ on behalf of a minor daughter and evaluate which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The father's acceptance of khul‘ does not bind the minor; the divorce is suspended until she ratifies.

This passage deepens the analysis by exploring a disagreement within the Hanafi school. When the father (or an outsider) accepts the compensation on behalf of a minor girl, does the talaq fall immediately? Two narrations from Imam Muhammad give different answers. The commentator weighs the proofs and concludes that the correct view is that it does not fall without the girl's later ratification. This lesson clarifies the reasoning behind each narration.

Guided Path
1
State the two narrations
Hishām narrated from Imam Muhammad that the talaq falls immediately upon the father's acceptance. Al-Hindwānī narrated that it does not fall until the minor ratifies upon reaching puberty.
Both narrations are from the same Imam Muhammad, showing a genuine ikhtilaf within the school.
2
Identify the proof for each
Hishām's narration relies on the concept of 'pure benefit' (naf‘ maḥḍ): the father can accept because it frees the daughter without any financial burden. Al-Hindwānī argues that the acceptance is akin to a condition of an oath (shart al-yamīn), which cannot be delegated.
The difference hinges on the nature of the acceptance: is it a financial act or an oath-like personal commitment?
3
Analyse the reasoning
The 'pure benefit' view emphasizes the guardian's power to contract for the child's advantage. The 'oath condition' view sees the minor's acceptance as a personal act akin to taking an oath, which requires her own consent.
The commentator notes that the condition of oath is metaphorical (majāzī), not literal, weakening the second view's basis.
4
Determine the tarjih
Ibn Nujaym states that the narration that the father's acceptance is invalid (i.e., talaq does not fall) is 'the most correct' (al-aṣaḥḥ). Thus, the mufta bihi is that the talaq is suspended pending the minor's ratification.
This tarjih is based on the principle that a conditional acceptance involving a personal element cannot be deputized.
5
Apply the ruling
If a father accepts khul‘ for his minor daughter today, the marriage remains intact until she reaches puberty and explicitly ratifies the divorce. If she does not ratify, no talaq occurs.
This protects the minor's right to decide her marital status when she attains capacity.

قوله : (ولو خلع صغيرة بمالها لم يجز عليها أي لا يلزمها المال لأنه لا نظر لها فيه لعدم تقوم البضع حالة الخروج، وإنما فسرنا عدم الجواز في كلامه بعدم لزوم المال لأن الصحيح وقوع الطلاق كما في الهداية لأنه تعليق بشرط قبوله فيعتبر بالتعليق بسائر الشروط . هذا إذا قبل الأب، فإن قبلت وهي عاقلة تعقل أن النكاح جالب والخلع سالب وقع الطلاق بالاتفاق ولا يلزمها المال. وذكر صاحب المنظومة أن خلع الصغيرة بمال مع الزوج إن كان بلفظ الخلع يقع البائن، وإن كان بلفظ الطلاق يقع الرجعي. وفي جامع الفصولين : لو طلق الصبية بمال يقع رجعياً وفي الأمة بائناً إذا الطلاق بمال يصح في الأمة لكنه مؤجل يصير وفي الصبية يقع بلا مال ا هـ . . وفي جوامع الفقه : طلقها بمهرها وهي صغيرة عاقلة فقبلت وقعت طلقة ولا يبرأ وإن قبل أبوها أو أجنبي روى هشام عن محمد أنه يقع، وروى الهندواني عن محمد أنه لا يقع فلو بلغت وأجازت جاز؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وذكر الشارح ولو شرط الزوج البدل عليها توقف على قبولها إن كانت أهلاً، فإن قبلت وقع اتفاقاً ولا يلزم المال، وإن قبل الأب عنها صح في رواية لأنه نفع محض لأنها تتخلص بلا مال، ولا يصح في أخرى لأن قبولها بمعنى شرط اليمين وهو لا يحتمل النيابة وهذا هو الأصح ا هـ.
His saying: 'And if he divorces a minor girl by khul' with her property, it is not valid over her' i.e., the compensation is not obligatory upon her because she has no consideration for it due to the lack of valuation of the vulva at the time of exit. And we have interpreted 'lack of validity' in his statement as non-obligation of the compensation because the correct view is that the talaq occurs, as in al-Hidayah, because it is a suspension upon the condition of acceptance, so it is analogized to suspension upon other conditions. This is if the father accepts. If she accepts while she is rational, understanding that marriage brings and khul' removes, the talaq occurs by agreement and the compensation is not obligatory upon her. The author of al-Manẓūma stated that khul' of a minor with property from the husband: if it is in the wording of khul', it falls as bā'in, and if in the wording of talaq, it falls as raj'ī. And in Jāmi' al-Fuṣūlayn: if he divorces a minor girl with [a condition of] property, it falls as raj'ī; in the case of a slave-girl, as bā'in because talaq with property is valid in the slave-girl but it is deferred; in the minor girl it falls without property. In Jawāmi' al-Fiqh: he divorced her with her mahr while she was a minor but rational, and she accepted, one talaq falls and he is not discharged. If her father or an outsider accepted, Hishām narrated from Muḥammad that it falls, and al-Hindwānī narrated from Muḥammad that it does not fall. Then if she comes of age and ratifies, it is valid. Al-Shāriḥ said: If the husband stipulated the compensation upon her, it depends on her acceptance if she is competent. If she accepted, it occurs by agreement and the compensation is not obligatory. If the father accepted on her behalf, it is valid in one narration because it is a pure benefit as she is released without compensation, and not valid in another because her acceptance is like a condition of an oath which does not accept deputyship, and this is the most correct.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding khul' of a minor girl. The matn stated that if a husband divorces his minor wife by khul' using her own property, it is not valid over her. The commentator explains that 'not valid' here means the compensation (the property) is not obligatory on her, because at the time of khul' the marital right (buda') is not considered to have market value (since she is leaving the marriage involuntarily? The reasoning: the vulva is not appraised at the time of exit). Crucially, the talaq itself does occur, according to the correct position in al-Hidayah. This is because the khul' is a suspension on the condition of acceptance, analogous to other conditional divorces. If her father accepts the compensation, the talaq falls. If she herself accepts and she is rational enough to understand that marriage benefits and khul' removes, the talaq falls by consensus, but she is still not liable for the compensation. The author of al-Manẓuma adds nuance: if the wording is 'khul'' it is bā'in; if 'talaq' it is raj'ī. Then there is a dispute among narrations from Imam Muhammad: according to Hisham, if the father or an outsider accepts, the talaq falls; according to al-Hindwani, it does not fall unless she later ratifies upon majority. The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) then states the relied-upon position: if one stipulates the compensation on her, it depends on her acceptance if she is competent; if she accepts, the talaq occurs but no compensation. If the father accepts on her behalf, one narration says it is valid (because it is a pure benefit), another says not (because acceptance involves an oath-like condition that cannot be delegated). The correct view is that the father's acceptance does not make it valid—this is the mufta bihi. The passage covers intra-Hanafi differences and the underlying principle that a minor cannot be liable for compensation in khul' because she lacks capacity to assume financial obligations at the time the marriage is dissolved.

Key Terms
خلع (khul‘): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband, resulting in a bā'in divorce.
صغيرة (ṣaghīra): A minor female who has not reached puberty, lacking full legal capacity for financial transactions.
بدل (badal): The compensation paid by the wife in khul‘, usually the mahr or an agreed sum.
هشام (Hishām): Hishām ibn ‘Abdallāh al-Rāzī, a narrator from Imam Muhammad, known for transmitting the narration that the father's acceptance causes immediate talaq.
الهندواني (al-Hindwānī): A narrator from Imam Muhammad, known for transmitting the narration that the talaq does not fall until the minor ratifies.
نفع محض (naf‘ maḥḍ): Pure benefit; an advantage without any financial cost or liability.
شرط اليمين (shart al-yamīn): Condition of an oath; a personal undertaking that cannot be performed by a proxy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view in the Hanafi school, what is the effect of the father accepting khul‘ on behalf of his minor daughter?
A) The talaq falls immediately and the father must pay the compensation.
B) The talaq does not fall; it depends on the minor's ratification upon majority.
C) The talaq falls but the minor is liable for the compensation.
D) The talaq does not fall because the father cannot act as guardian in khul‘.

Key Takeaway
The father's acceptance of khul‘ does not bind the minor; the divorce is pending until she ratifies upon reaching majority.
